§ 52.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CONSUMER or CUSTOMER. Any individual, partnership, association, firm, public
or private corporation or governmental agency receiving water service. In the
case of property occupied by a tenant, the property owner is and shall be
considered the ultimate CUSTOMER and responsible for payment of service.
   CURB BOX. A cast iron or plastic tube like device to provide easy access to
curb valves which are located underground.
   CURB VALVE. A valve installed in the water service line and accessible for
operation from the surface of the ground for routinely interrupting flow
through the service line.
   CUSTOMER SERVICE PIPE. The portion of the service pipe from the distribution
main to the structure or premises supplied, installed at the cost and expense
of the customer.
   DISTRIBUTION MAIN. Water pipe owned, operated or maintained by the Water
Department which is used for the purpose of distribution of water and from
which service connections with customers are taken.
   EXTENSION. The act or process of extending, adding to or enlarging the city
water supply system to provide water service to a customer or a group of
prospective customers.
   METER. The instrument, including all auxiliary devices and equipment, owned
and used by the city to measure the amount of water delivered to a customer.
   POINT OF DELIVERY. The point at which the city water supply system connects
physically to the customers’ facilities, which point is located at the
corporation stop which is normally attached to the public water main located in
the public right-of-way that abuts the property to be served.
   PRIVATE FIRE SERVICE CONNECTION. One which is attached to fixtures from
which water is taken only for extinguishment of fire.
   WATER DEPARTMENT. Those who own, operate or control any plant or equipment,
any part of a plant or equipment or any water right within the state for the
projection, delivery or furnishing for or to other persons, firms, associations
or corporations, private or municipal, of water for business, manufacturing or
household use within the limits of the city.
   WATER SERVICE LINE. All service pipe, curb stop, curb box, meter box or
vault, backflow prevention device, pressure reducing valve, inside piping,
appliances and other apparatus on the customer’s side of the point of delivery,
except the Water Department’s water meter and any other equipment owned by the
city.
   WATER SUPPLY SYSTEM. Any devices, facilities, structures, equipment, land or
works controlled by the city for the purpose of the processing, treatment,
transmission, storage, distribution, pumping and measurement of water supplied
to customers.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-1) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.02 SERVICE CONNECTIONS.
   (A)   Costs.
      (1)   Tapping. Where an application for water service has been granted by
the Water Department, the Water Department shall tap the main up through a two-
inch service line tap.
      (2)   Service pipes. All expense of laying and maintaining the service
pipes from the mains to the consumer’s premises shall be borne by the customer.
The Water Department will specify the kind, quality and the location of all
materials used in the service line. The service pipe shall be laid below the
final street grade and on the consumer’s premises at a depth of six and one-
half feet to prevent freezing. If shallower at the water main, insulation shall
be used to protect the service pipe from freezing until the standard depth is
obtained.
   (B)   Service pipe materials. Water services three-fourths inch through two
inches shall be of Type K soft copper, or polyethylene ASTM D2737 CTS SDR 9 200
psi NSF certified or better and of copper tube size from the corporation stop
(connection to the main) to the curb stop at the property line. The
polyethylene pipe shall be of continuous construction in rolls of the
manufacturer’s standard length. Pipe ends shall be cut square and joined using
brass or reinforced insert compression type fittings recommended by the
manufacturer. The water service line shall be a continuous run of pipe from the
water main to the curb stop, no joints shall be allowed. From the curb stop to
the meter valve, any material acceptable under State Plumbing Codes is
acceptable.
   (C)   Shutoff. Within two feet of the point of service entrance to a
building, and from one to three feet above the floor, an approved valve of good
quality and good hydraulic characteristics must be placed so that the water can
be readily shut off from the building. Fullway gate valves or rotary valves,
which include ball, cone and plug types are recommended. However, better
quality compression stops or globe valves are permissible.
   (D)   Taps in excess of two inches; costs. All expenses associated with
making taps in excess of two inches or for extra capacity or special taps for
fire lines, lawn sprinkling systems and the like, shall be made at the
customer’s sole expense. All other such work, such as, but not limited to, any
trench backfilling and compaction work and any surface restoration work shall
be performed by and at the expense of the person installing the water service
line, fire line or combination thereof in question.
   (E)   Safe trench conditions. The person installing a water service line,
fire line or combination thereof, shall be responsible for providing safe
trench conditions for the employees of the city when making a tap to the public
water main. Failure to provide safe trench conditions shall be cause for
immediate refusal by the Water Department to perform any such tapping work.
   (F)   Water from other sources. No person shall make or maintain a
connection with any pipes or private services connected with the city water
supply system so as to obtain water from any source other than the water supply
of the city.
   (G)   Inspection. The customer’s service pipe and all connections and
fixtures attached thereto shall be subject to the inspection of the utility
before the water will be turned on, and all premises receiving a supply of
water and all services pipes, meter and fixtures, including any and all
fixtures within said premises, shall at all reasonable hours be subject to
inspection by any duly authorized employees of the utility. No inspections or
taps will be made after regular working hours, on Saturday, Sunday or city
holidays. Persons requesting an inspection and/or tap to the public water main
shall be ready to have the inspection and/or tap at the time designated by such
persons.
   (H)   Curb box. The curb box shall be set at a location approved by the
utility and shall be accessible at all times.
   (I)   Service pipes passing through or across other premises. Service pipes
supplying premises shall not pass through or across any premises or property
other than that to be supplied, nor across any portion of the property that
could practicably be sold separately from the immediate premises supplied, and
no water pipes or plumbing in any premises shall be extended therefrom to
adjacent or other premises. At no time will it be allowed to extend a water
service which is intended to supply water to a property facing one avenue or
street to another property facing another avenue or street if said water
service has to cross a public right-of-way, such as an avenue, street or alley.
   (J)   Attachment of fixtures. No fixture shall be attached to, or any branch
made in, the service pipe between the meter and the distribution system.
   (K)   Separate service lines. Service pipes shall be so arranged that each
separate building and/or house shall be supplied by a separate service line
from the city main. A valve or curb stop (with box) shall be installed in each
service line so that the supply may be controlled from the street side of the
property line. This curb valve and box must be kept in repair by the owner of
the premises and easily accessible to city utility crews.
   (L)   Ownership; maintenance. Water service lines, fire lines or
combinations thereof, are owned by the owner of the property served. Said
owners shall keep their water service lines, fire lines or combinations thereof
in good repair and condition at all times and in addition to other penalties if
not repaired within ten days after receipt of notice by the Water Department to
do so, water service to the property involved may be discontinued. Except as
otherwise provided herein, all costs and expenses incidental to the
installation of water service lines, fire lines or combinations thereof, or
making connections of same with the public water mains, or making repairs,
alterations or extensions to such facilities, shall be borne by the owners of
said facilities. Water service lines, fire lines or combinations thereof, are
nontransferable and shall run with the property originally served by said
facilities.
   (M)   Permissions required. No plumber or other person shall make
connections with any water main, pipe or other fixture connecting therewith,
connect pipes when they have been disconnected, or turn water on or off on any
premises without permission of the Water Department.
   (N)   Permits issued only to licensed plumbers. Permits for the installation
and repair of service pipes shall be issued to regular licensed plumbers only.
Such work shall conform with the rules and specifications of the Water
Department and other ordinances of the city. All water plumbing work shall be
under the supervision and subject to inspection of the Water Department. The
words “service pipe” as used in this section shall embrace that potion of the
water supply pipe laying between the main and the outlet side of the meter.
   (O)   Curb valves or stops. Curb valves or stops shall be provided with a
stop to enable the operator to tell whether the stop is full open or closed.
The top of the valve may be threaded to attach to the curb box.
   (P)   Single service.
      (1)   Multiple users. Where water is now supplied through one service to
several houses, families or persons such as a trailer court, the Water
Department may decline to furnish water until separate services are provided,
or may continue to furnish water under the conditions that one person shall pay
for all on the same service, and assume full responsibility for the maintenance
and repair of the entire service line.
      (2)   Metering point. Certain multiple building complexes such as trailer
courts, apartment complexes and the like, under one ownership may be metered at
one metering point at the option of the Water Department.
   (Q)   Trenches. All trenches shall be dug at right angles to the main
whenever possible. The trenches shall be of sufficient depth to furnish six and
one-half feet of cover for the pipe. All excavation, backfilling and compaction
shall comply with §§
151.080 through
151.094 for trench backfill and street restoration.
   (R)   Inspections; tests.
      (1)   Excavation permit required. A permit for excavation shall be
obtained from the Public Works Department before any excavation is made in a
dedicated right-of-way.
      (2)   Inspection and approval required. The Public Works Department shall
inspect and approve all water service work for water service pipes two inches
and smaller.
      (3)   Materials and installation. All materials and installation shall
conform to all applicable codes and statutes.
      (4)   Pressure tests. Before any trench is filled, or pipes covered, all
pressure tests shall be conducted satisfactorily.
      (5)   Pressure, leakage and bacteriological tests. For fire lines and
domestic lines larger than two inches in diameter, pressure, leakage and
bacteriological tests shall be conducted in accordance with the Montana Public
Works Standard Specifications, current edition, before acceptance.
      (6)   Inspections.
         (a)   Water service or fire line work. The Director of Public Works,
or authorized representative, shall inspect and approve all water service or
fire line work for lines larger than two inches in diameter from the water main
to the building entrance valve.
         (b)   Piping beyond entrance valve. The Fire Chief or other authorized
representative shall inspect and approve all piping beyond the entrance valve.
         (c)   Replacement pavement, landscaping. The Director of Public Works
or authorized representative shall inspect and approve all replacement of
pavement, right-of-way landscaping, concrete curb box, curb and gutter and
sidewalk removed for the construction or maintenance of water service or fire
lines.
      (7)   Reexcavation. Any trench backfilled before any inspection is
conducted will necessitate the reexcavation of the trench.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-2) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001; Ord. 01-2012, passed 3-
20-2012; Ord. 01-2014, passed 4-1-2014) Penalty, see §
10.99
Cross-reference:
   Trench backfill and street restoration, see §§
151.080 through
151.094
§ 52.03 RATE SCHEDULE.
   (A)   Water and sewer rates and service charge. Every customer shall pay
water and sewer rates and other water service charges according to the schedule
established by resolution of the City Council, as provided in M.C.A. Title 69,
Chapter 7, part 1; provided, that said resolution shall not have an effective
date until ten days after the date of adoption.
   (B)   Hydrant charge. A hydrant charge shall be assessed yearly against all
taxable property in the city according to a schedule set down by the City
Council, in writing, as provided in M.C.A. Title 69, Chapter 7, part 1.
   (C)   Rate schedule. The City Water Department may adopt either a flat rate
schedule, meter rate schedule, or both, according to such schedule being
established by the City Council, as provided in M.C.A. Title 69, Chapter 7,
part 1.
   (D)   Free water. The Water Department shall not supply free water to any
customer.
   (E)   Connection/disconnection fee. Should the owner of a premises request
to temporarily discontinue the use of the water, or should the premises become
vacant, the city, after receiving a signed request, will shut off the water at
the curb box, if operational. The City Water Department shall charge a fee for
such connection/disconnection of water meters according to a schedule
established by the City Council in accordance with M.C.A. Title 69, Chapter 7,
part 1.
   (F)   Reestablishment fee. The City Water Department shall charge a
reestablishment fee, according to a schedule established by resolution of the
City Council, in accordance with M.C.A. Title 69, Chapter 7, part 1, for
turning off/on the curb stop if the disconnection is caused by the delinquent
payment of water rate fees by the customer or because of damage to the water
meter, or connections thereto, because of the customer’s failure to maintain
water service lines and fire lines, as set forth in §
52.02(L), or to provide appropriate precautions to prevent the freezing of
water meters.
   (G)   Water and sewer connection fees. The City Council shall adopt water
and sewer connection fee schedules by resolution as deemed necessary. Fee
schedules shall be available to the public at the City Hall.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-3) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001; Ord. 01-2012, passed 3-
20-2012)
§ 52.04 FLAT RATES; FURNISHING WATER WITHOUT PERMISSION.
   (A)   Flat rate. Flat rates will cover the use of water for domestic use
where impractical to meter.
   (B)   Furnishing water without permission. If a customer furnishes other
people with water without permission from the Water Department or uses water
for purposes other than those the consumer is paying for, it is a violation of
the consumer’s contract with the utility.
   (C)   Notice of violation; discontinuance of service. Ten days after the
consumer in violation has received written notice from the Water Department,
the Water Department may have the water shut off and service discontinued.
   (D)   Service reestablished. When the unauthorized service has been paid
for, together with payment of the reconnecting charge, service will be
reestablished.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-4) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 52.05 METERS.
   (A)   Owned, maintained and operated by city. The Water Department shall
provide meters and shall continue to own, maintain and operate equipment
necessary for the regulation and measurement of water. Where additional meters
are requested by the customer and are furnished by the Water Department for the
convenience of the customer, a charge for such meters shall be made.
   (B)   Replacement. The Water Department may replace any meter at such time
as it may see fit and shall be the judge of the size of any meter installed.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-5) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.06 SECONDARY METERS.
   (A)   The Water Department will not make collections for any secondary
meters, and all water charges for any single building must be paid by one
consumer when water is supplied by meter measurement through one service.
   (B)   In no case will the Water Department furnish water from one meter to
two or more houses, whether the same are owned by one person or not.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-6) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.07 TEMPORARY METERS FOR CONSTRUCTION SITES.
   Water for construction purposes will be furnished through temporary meters
and paid for at the regular meter rates. In addition to the cost of the water,
the customer will be required to pay the actual cost of setting and removing
the temporary meter. In case it is not possible or practical to set a temporary
meter, the cost will be determined by applying the regular meter rates to a
quantity of water estimated by the city.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-7) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.08 LOCATION AND INSTALLATION OF METERS.
   (A)   Removal and replacement of obstruction. The removal and replacement of
any obstruction which interferes with the installation of the water meter is
the responsibility of the property owner.
   (B)   Insufficient space. When insufficient space is available in existing
water piping to accept a proper meter installation, the cost of plumbing
modifications or special meter setting equipment shall be charged to the
property owner.
   (C)   New construction. For new construction, the permittee shall fully
install the meter and appurtenances. The meter shall be furnished by the city.
   (D)   Leaking or defective water shutoff valve. A leaking or otherwise
defective water shutoff valve must be replaced in order to facilitate meter
installation. The property owner must replace this valve with all costs and
installation to be charged to the property owner. Curb box locations and
shutoff services to accommodate valve replacement will be provided by the city
at no charge during normal working hours.
   (E)   Installation. Every displacement meter, compound meter and turbo meter
shall be installed level in a horizontal plane with register or registers
facing upward.
   (F)   Valve on inlet side of meter. Every meter setting shall include an
approved valve at the inlet side of the meter thereby enabling service or
replacement of the meter. It is recommended that a valve be placed on the
outlet side of the meter to prevent back flooding during meter replacement.
   (G)   Meter box or meter vault. When required by the Water Department, an
easily accessible outside meter box or meter vault shall be installed by and at
the customer’s expense on each service line serving each separate building. The
location of the meter box or vault shall be designated by the Water Department.
All meter boxes or meter vaults shall be constructed in accordance with plans
and specifications approved by the Water Department and Public Works Director.
Pursuant to conditions of this chapter, customers must keep their meter boxes
or meter vaults in good repair and condition at all times.
   (H)   Frost protection. In all cases where meters are installed, the
customer shall furnish proper protection from frost or other damage. Cost of
parts replaced on meters damaged due to customer neglect or misuse shall be
borne by the customer.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-8) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.09 ACCESS TO PROPERTY.
   (A)   Location of meter. The meter must be located where it is easily
accessible for reading purposes and repair.
   (B)   Remote receptacle.
      (1)   When required. Where a meter is located inside a home or building
where access is not readily available, the Water Department may install a
remote receptacle on the exterior of a home or building accessible for meter
reading.
      (2)   Location. The location of the remote receptacle shall be determined
by the Water Department for convenience of reading. Receptacles shall not be
placed behind any shrub or vegetation and the city may relocate if fences or
structure changes block direct access to the receptacle.
      (3)   Height. The remote receptacle height shall be determined by the
Water Department, but in no case shall it be less than 30 inches above ground
level.
   (C)   Department access. The Water Department with proper credentials and
identification shall at all reasonable times have access to meters and other
property owned by it on the customer’s premises, for purpose of maintenance,
operation, inspection, sampling and testing. Where reasonable notice by the
Water Department has been given, neglect or refusal on the part of customers to
provide reasonable access to their premises for the above purposes shall be
deemed to be sufficient cause for discontinuance of service on the part of the
Water Department.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-9) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.10 INTERFERENCE WITH METER.
   (A)   Meter seal broken; damage to working parts. Water consumers are not
permitted to interfere in any way with the meter and appurtenances thereto
after it is set in place. In case the meter seal is broken or the working parts
of the meter have been tampered with or the meter damaged, the city may render
a bill for the current month, based on an average of the previous quarter or
the same quarter of the previous year, if available, whichever the city
determines more accurately reflects water usage for the inaccurate period,
together with the full cost of such damage as has been done to the meter, and
may refuse to furnish water until account is paid in full.
   (B)   Liability to utility. A person who bypasses or tampers, either for his
or her own benefit or the benefit of another, with any metering device is
liable to the utility as provided in M.C.A. §§ 69-4-1101 through 69-4-1104.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-10) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.11 SERVICE INTERRUPTIONS.
   (A)   Reasonable effort to avoid. The Water Department shall make reasonable
effort to avoid interruptions of service and, when interruptions occur, shall
reestablish service with reasonable diligence.
   (B)   Liability. The Water Department shall not be liable to the customer or
others for failure or interruption of water service due to acts of God,
governmental regulations, court or commissioner orders, acts of a public enemy,
strikes or labor difficulties, accidents, weather conditions, acts of third
parties, droughts or, without limitation by the foregoing, any other cause
beyond the reasonable control of the Water Department.
   (C)   Notice of interruption. Wherever possible, the Water Department shall
give individual notice of service interruption; however, general advice by
newspaper in the affected area or radio or television announcement shall meet
the notice requirement.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-11) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.12 APPLICATION FOR WATER SERVICE.
   (A)   Written application. All customers desiring water service must make
written application at the office of the Water Department on printed forms
provided therefor, setting forth in said application all purposes for which
water will be used upon their premises. In cases where the customer is not the
owner of the premises, the customer is primarily liable for payment for his or
her water service and the property owner is ultimately liable for such payment.
   (B)   Signature of property owner required. All applications for the
introduction of water service to any premises must be signed by the property
owner.
   (C)   Change of contracting customer. Any change in the identity of the
contracting customer at a premises will require a new application for water
service.
   (D)   Deposit required. All customers applying for water service who are
tenants shall pay a deposit upon application as set forth by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-12) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.13 CONSUMER INFORMATION.
   (A)   Provided by Department. The Water Department shall, upon request give
its customers such information and assistance as is reasonable, in order that
customers may secure safe and efficient service.
   (B)   Explanation of rates. The Water Department shall explain to the
customer at the beginning of service, or whenever the customer shall request,
the Water Department rates applicable to the type of service furnished. The
Water Department shall also supply the customer, upon request, a copy of the
Water Department rate or rates applicable to the type of service to be
furnished.
   (C)   Records maintained for inspection. The Water Department shall maintain
in its office for inspection by the public, the following:
      (1)   A copy of the rates, rules and regulations of the Water Department
and forms of applications; and
      (2)   A copy of these rules and regulations.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-13) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.14 BILLING INFORMATION.
   (A)   Meter readings. Bills shall show the readings of the meter at the
beginning and end of the period for which the bill is rendered, the date of the
meter readings, the number of cubic feet or gallons of water supplied and the
authorized rate or approved flat rate.
   (B)   Opening and closing bills. Opening and closing bills, monthly or
quarterly, for water service rendering for periods of five days or more or five
days less than the normal billing period will be computed in accordance with
the rate applicable to that service, by the amount of water blocks.
   (C)   Reading of meters.
      (1)   The Water Department shall normally read meters for all urban
customers at monthly or bimonthly intervals. The day of the month for reading
any meter as determined by the Water Department shall as closely as practicable
be the same for each reading.
      (2)   The Water Department, at its option, and subject to the approval of
the City Council, may read the meters at less frequent intervals if in the
opinion of the Water Department such procedure contributes to certain operating
economics, but in no instance shall a meter be read less than once in six
months.
   (D)   Readings by customer. In months when meters are not read, the Water
Department may provide the customer with a postcard and request the customer to
read the meter and return the card to the Water Department. If such postcard is
not received by the utility in time for billing, the Water Department may
estimate meter readings and render a bill accordingly.
   (E)   Delinquency. Each bill shall be delinquent on the thirtieth of each
month and service shall be discontinued by the tenth of the following month.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-14) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.15 ADJUSTMENT OF BILLS.
   In case of a dispute as to the accuracy of a meter, the consumer, upon
depositing the estimated cost of making a test, may demand that the meter be
removed and tested as to accuracy, in his or her presence.
   (A)   Meter working correctly. In case the meter is found to be registering
correctly or in favor of the consumer, the cost of such testing and replacing
of the meter shall be borne by the consumer.
   (B)   Incorrect reading. In case the meter is found to be recording
incorrectly and against the consumer, the amount deposited by the consumer will
be refunded and a reasonable adjustment made for overcharges during a period of
not exceeding 60 days previous to the demand of the consumer for such test.
   (C)   Meter stopped. In case a meter is found stopped for any reason, so
that it is not correctly recording the consumption of water, the Water
Department may average the amount due for the current month, using the past two
months as a basis for such average.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-15) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.16 COMPLAINTS.
   (A)   Investigation of complaints. The Water Department shall make a full
and prompt investigation of all complaints made to it by its customers. In the
event that the complaint is not adjusted, the Water Department will notify the
customer that he or she has the privilege of appeal to the consumer service
representative of the Public Service Commission.
   (B)   Billing disputes. In the event of a dispute between the customer and
the utility respecting any bill, the Water Department shall make forthwith such
investigation as shall be required by the particular case and report the result
thereof to the customer. In the event that the complaint is not adjusted, the
Water Department shall notify the customer that he or she has the privilege of
appeal to the consumer service representative of the Public Service Commission.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-16) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.17 DISCONTINUANCE OF SERVICE.
   (A)   Customer discontinuance.
      (1)   Notice required. Every customer who is about to vacate any premises
supplied with service by the Water Department, or who for any reason wishes to
have service discontinued, shall give at least 24 hours’ notice thereof to the
Water Department, specifying the date on which it is desired that service be
discontinued. Until the Water Department shall have such notice, the customer
shall be held responsible for all service rendered.
      (2)   Temporary discontinuance. Should the consumer desire to discontinue
the use of water temporarily, the Water Department, when notified to do so in
writing, will shut off the water at the curb. No deduction in bill will be made
for the time any service pipes may be frozen.
   (B)   Utility discontinuance.
      (1)   Notice of discontinuance.
         (a)   Attempt for compliance. The Water Department shall not
discontinue service to any customer for violation of rules and regulations for
nonpayment of bills without first having tried diligently to induce the
customer to comply with its rules and regulations, or to pay his or her bills.
A record of such effort shall be maintained.
         (b)   Notice. Service shall be discontinued after seven days’ written
notice has been given to the customer by the utility that bills are delinquent
or that violation of rules must cease; provided, however, that where fraudulent
use of water is detected, or where the Water Department’s regulating or
measuring equipment has been tampered with, or where a dangerous condition is
found to exist on the customer’s premises, the water may be shut off without
notice in advance.
      (2)   Charge for reconnection.
         (a)   Turned off due to violation. Whenever the supply of water is
turned off for the violation of rules and regulations, nonpayment of bills or
fraudulent use of water, the Water Department may make a charge as set forth in
its regulations for reestablishing service.
         (b)   Turned off for nonpayment. After service has been turned off
because of nonpayment, service shall not be turned on again until all back
water bills have been paid or an agreeable pay arrangement has been made,
together with a turn on charge as set forth in its regulations.
         (c)   Discontinued at request of customer. If service is discontinued
at the request of the customer, the Water Department may refuse service to such
customer, at the same premises, unless it shall first receive payment as set
forth in its regulations for the reconnecting charge.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-17) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.18 REFUSAL TO SERVE APPLICANT.
   (A)   Compliance with rules and regulations. The Water Department may
decline to serve an applicant until he or she has complied with the rules and
regulations governing water service.
   (B)   Installation of piping equipment. The Water Department may refuse to
serve an applicant if, in its judgment, the applicant’s installation of piping
equipment is regarded as hazardous, illegal or of such character that
satisfactory service cannot be given.
   (C)   Duty to inform. In the event that the utility shall refuse to serve an
applicant under the provisions of this rule, the utility must inform the
applicant that the request may be submitted to the commission for decision.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-18) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.19 SPRINKLING REGULATIONS.
   (A)   Power to regulate use; publication of notice. In the interest of
preventing waste and promoting conservation of water during periods of high
usage and water shortage, the Water Department may specify the hours and days
during which sprinkling will be permitted and will publish notice thereof in
newspapers at the start of the sprinkling restriction period.
   (B)   Waste.
      (1)   Power to determine. The Water Department may make a reasonable
determination based upon existing facts whether a customer is using water in a
wasteful manner.
      (2)   Notice to customer. When the Water Department discovers any
customer failing to observe the hours and days for sprinkling service or
wasting water, it shall deliver to such customer a copy of the notice of hours
and days of sprinkling and shall advise the customer of the conservation fee
which is to be charged if water is wasted or the specified sprinkling hours or
days are not observed by the customer. If the customer is not at home at the
time the Water Department discovers the customer’s waste of water or failure to
observe the specified sprinkling times, then the Water Department shall leave a
notice of the violation at the customer’s door and it shall be deemed the
customer has been adequately notified.
      (3)   Conservation fee. If this customer is found to be wasting water or
failing to observe specified sprinkling times at a subsequent time during the
sprinkling restriction, the Water Department may charge and bill the customer a
“conservation fee” equal to the current average cost which would be incurred
had the Water Department actually disconnected and connected the customer’s
water service.
      (4)   Discontinuance of service. If the customer does not pay the charge
(s) within seven days’ written notice, the Water Department may discontinue
service until paid.
      (5)   Extraordinary expense. Extraordinary expense incurred by the Water
Department to discontinue service and subsequent reconnecting shall be paid by
the customer.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-19) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.20 PREVENTION OF FREEZING.
   If there is a general danger of freezing of the Water Department mains or of
customer’s service lines, the Water Department may inform its customers that
the water may be run to prevent freezing at no additional cost. The water then
will be billed only for the amount based on average use rather than actual
amounts determined by meter readings until the danger of freezing has passed.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-20) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.21 HYDRANTS.
   (A)   All fire hydrants not installed on private lines or systems shall be
the property of the Water Department. Those hydrants installed in newly
developed areas shall be the type specified by the Water Department.
   (B)   All hydrants owned by the Water Department shall be properly
maintained, and said cost of maintenance and operation shall be charged to the
city tax rolls where the distribution of costs will be based upon the taxable
value of the property.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-21) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.22 PRIVATE FIRE PROTECTION SERVICE.
   (A)   Special application. Service connections for water taken for the
extinguishment of fires shall be made only under the terms of and conditions
contained in the “Special Application” for such service, a copy of which is on
file in the Water Department.
   (B)   Advance approval required. The customer must agree to obtain in
advance the approval of the Water Department for any change, alteration or
addition in the fixtures, openings and uses specified in the applications.
   (C)   Connection. The Water Department shall determine the location of any
connections made to its distribution mains for private fire protection service.
Size of service shall be made by a qualified sprinkler design company. At the
cost and expense of the customer, the connection to the distribution system
shall be made by a plumber licensed to practice in the state.
   (D)   Materials. Fire lines and domestic lines over two inches in diameter
shall be C900 Class 200 PVC or ductile iron. When C900 Class 200 pipe is used,
it can run to a point ten feet outside the building foundation. From that
point, the material used shall be of ductile iron the remainder of the way into
the building up to the water meter or fire system apparatus.
   (E)   Extent of rights. The extent of the rights of the private fire
protection service customer is to receive, but only at times of fire on his or
her premises, such supply of water as shall then be available. The Water
Department shall not be considered in any manner an insurer of property or
persons, or to have undertaken to extinguish fire or to protect any persons or
property against loss or all claims for damages on account of any injury to
property or persons by reason of fire, water, failure to supply water or
pressure, or for any other cause whatsoever.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-22) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.23 EXTENSION OF MAINS.
   (A)   Service outside corporate limits. The Water Department shall not
furnish water to consumers outside the corporate limits of the city. Upon
annexation of any tract to the city, the developer or developers shall provide
the Water Department with complete plans and specifications and an engineering
report accepted by the State Department of Environmental Quality.
   (B)   New system or major alteration or extension.
      (1)   Review and approval of Department of Health and Environmental
Services. Before any construction of a new system or major alteration or
extension of any existing public water system, an engineering report along with
necessary plans and specifications for the public water system shall be
submitted to the Department of Environmental Quality for review and approval.
The acceptance of plans will be completed before construction commences.
      (2)   Costs. Cost of the design, engineering study and all material for
the extension shall be borne by the area receiving service or the developer
thereof.
      (3)   Acceptance of system; maintenance. Upon acceptance of the new
system, or extension of existing mains by the Water Department, maintenance of
the main line will be provided by the Water Department and will become part of
the overall water system.
      (4)   Reservation of right. The Water Department shall reserve the right
to specify the necessary size of main for any and all extensions and new
systems.
   (C)   Specifications. All water main line and appurtenances design, service
line design, fire line design and combinations thereof, along with the
installation of all water main line, service line, fire line and combinations
thereof shall meet all specifications as set forth in the most current edition
of Montana Public Works Standard Specifications.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-23) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.24 GUARANTEE.
   (A)   Required. Persons who contract to make connections to public water
mains, or to install water service lines, fire lines or combinations thereof,
or to make repairs, alterations or extensions to such facilities, shall
guarantee all materials and equipment furnished and work performed for a period
of one year from the date of completion of said work.
   (B)   Defects.
      (1)   Necessary corrections. Said persons warrant guarantee for a period
of one year from the date of completion of the work that said completed work is
free from all defects due to faulty materials or workmanship, and such persons
shall promptly make such corrections as may be necessary by reason of such
defects, including the repairs of any damage to the public water main resulting
from such defects.
      (2)   Notice of defects. The city shall give notice of observed defects
with reasonable promptness.
      (3)   Failure to correct defects. In the event the persons performing
such work should fail to make such repairs, adjustments or the work that may be
made necessary by such defects, the city may make arrangements for the
performance of such work by others and charge such persons the cost thereby
incurred.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-24) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.25 DAMAGE TO UTILITY FACILITIES.
   (A)   The person installing water service lines, fire lines or combinations
thereof, shall cause to be immediately repaired at his or her expense, any
damage to the public mains occasioned by his or her operations.
   (B)   No person(s) shall maliciously, willfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or
equipment which is a part of the utility facilities of the Water Department.
Any person(s) violating this provision shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
   (C)   It is an offense punishable pursuant to the general penalty provided
in §
10.99 for any person to do the following:
      (1)   To open, close, turn or interfere with, or attach to, or connect to
a fire hydrant, stop valve or main line valve belonging to the Water Department
without proper permission; and
      (2)   To throw any deleterious matter into the river within 3,000 feet of
the inlet pipes to the water treatment plant pumping works.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-25) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 52.26 UNDERGROUND UTILITY INFORMATION.
   The state statutes set forth certain procedures for obtaining information
concerning underground utilities prior to making or beginning any excavation in
any public street, alley, right-of-way dedicated to public use or utility
easement. The statutes also set forth penalties for failure to comply with the
provisions enumerated therein. Persons making excavations within the city
limits must comply with the provisions of said state statutes when making
connections to public water mains, or installing water service lines, fire
lines or combinations thereof, or making repairs, alterations or extensions to
such facilities.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-26) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.27 ABANDONED WATER SERVICE LINES.
   Property owners desiring to abandon water service lines, fire lines or
combinations thereof, or who are removing structures from property, shall cause
such water service lines, fire lines or combinations thereof, to be
disconnected at their expense at the point of delivery or connection with the
public water main if the material used in such line is not of acceptable
material. If the service line is copper from the curb stop to the city water
main, it shall be physically disconnected from the building side of the
controlling curb stop. The curb box shall be reset over curb stops for live
water services remaining. The corporation cock, tapping valve or service valve
at the public water main shall be sealed by the Water Department when same is
exposed and the person disconnecting the water service line, fire lines or
combinations thereof, has disconnected same. Old water service lines, fire
lines or combinations thereof, may be used in connection with new buildings
only when they are found on examination and/or test by the Water Department to
meet the requirements of these and all other applicable rules and regulations.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-27) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 52.28 WATER SERVICE LINE STUBOUTS.
   Pursuant to and in accordance with the provisions of M.C.A. § 7-12-4133, as
amended, connections from the public water main to the property line of the
adjacent property shall be made prior to the permanent improvement of the
streets whereon they are located. The making of such connections on streets
already improved, or on unimproved streets, shall be in accordance with all
applicable provisions of these rules and regulations. In case the owners of the
property on such streets fail to make such connections prior to the
commencement of such street improvements, the city may cause such connections
to be made and shall assess against the property in front of which said
connections are made the entire cost and expense thereof. All assessments
levied under the provisions of this section shall be enforced and collected in
the same manner as other special assessments provided for in M.C.A. Title 7,
Chapter 6, part 44, and amendments thereof.
(Prior Code, § 10-3-28) (Ord. 03-2001, passed 3-20-2001)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 53.001 PURPOSE AND POLICY.
   (A)   This chapter sets forth uniform requirements for industrial users
(“IUs”) of the publicly owned treatment works (“POTW”) for the city related to
pretreatment. It is intended to enable the POTW to comply with its national
pollutant discharge elimination system (“NPDES”) permit from the State
Department of Environmental Quality as well as all applicable state and federal
laws, including the Clean Water Act (33 U.S.C. §§ 1251 et seq.) and the general
pretreatment regulations (40 C.F.R. part 403). The objectives of this chapter
are:
      (1)   To prevent the introduction of pollutants into the POTW that will
interfere with its operation;
      (2)   To prevent the introduction of pollutants into the POTW that will
pass through the POTW, inadequately treated, into receiving waters or otherwise
be incompatible with the POTW;
      (3)   To protect both POTW personnel, who may be affected by wastewater
and sludge in the course of their employment, and the general public;
      (4)   To promote and protect the reuse and recycling of wastewater and
sludge from the POTW; and
      (5)   To enable the POTW to comply with its NPDES permit conditions,
sludge use and disposal requirements, and any other federal or state laws to
which the POTW is subject.
   (B)   This chapter shall apply to all IUs of the POTW.
(Prior Code, § 10-2A-1-1) (Ord. 01-2016, passed 7-5-2016)
§ 53.002 ADMINISTRATION.
   Except as otherwise provided herein, the POTW shall administer, implement
and enforce the provisions of this chapter. Any powers granted to or duties
imposed upon the POTW may be delegated to a duly authorized municipality
employee.
(Prior Code, § 10-2A-1-2) (Ord. 01-2016, passed 7-5-2016)
