GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.01 “NUISANCE” DEFINED.
   (A)   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      NUISANCE. Anything which is injurious to health, or is a life safety
issue or hazard, or is an obstruction to the free use of another’s property, so
as to interfere with the comfortable enjoyment of life or property of another;
or including, but not limited to, placement and/or maintenance of any motor
vehicle, motorcycle, trailer, camp trailer or mobile home on any property in
the city in violation of any zoning regulation or other city ordinance; or any
residential structure (including all appurtenant structures) to remain vacant
for more than one year where its condition constitutes a hazard or where the
property is maintained so as to obstruct the free passage or use, in the
customary manner, of any navigable lake, or river, bay, stream, canal or basin,
or any public park, square, street or highway.
   (B)   This declaration of nuisance by the City Council is made pursuant to
M.C.A. § 7-5-4104.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-1) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011; Ord. 01-2025, passed 1-
7-2025)
§ 90.02 SUMMARY ABATEMENT; LIEN PROCEDURE.
   The City Council declares that it is in the public interest to establish a
summary abatement procedure utilizing a lien process to abate any nuisance, as
defined in §
90.01. The expense of abatement of nuisances shall be a lien against the
property on which it is maintained and a personal obligation shall exist as
against the property owner.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-2) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011)
§ 90.03 LIEN PROCEDURES FOR ABATEMENT OF NUISANCE.
   (A)   The City Zoning Coordinator or other city personnel specifically
designated by the City Council shall examine or cause to be examined whether
any property or thing has been maintained so as to constitute a nuisance, as
defined in §
90.01. With owner’s consent, city personnel may enter upon private premises at
any reasonable time to perform an inspection or if such consent cannot be
obtained, resort to other legal process inclusive of a search warrant.
   (B)   If city personnel find that a nuisance does exist, they shall obtain a
preliminary title report on the real property where the nuisance exists, which
shall identify all owners of record, lessees of record, holders of mortgages,
deed of trust or other liens and encumbrances of record. They shall serve upon
each such person by personal service or by certified mail, postage prepaid,
return receipt requested, a written notice stating the nature of the nuisance
and requiring the owner to commence either the required repairs, demolition,
removal or other appropriate action within ten days and to complete such work
within 30 days from the date of notice. Such notice shall contain the office,
address, phone number of city personnel empowered to review the subject matter
and the days and hours the same may be contacted. The notice shall be sent to
each such person at his or her address as it appears on the last equalized
assessment roll of the county as known to city personnel. If no address of any
such person so appears, then a copy of the notice shall be mailed and addressed
to such person at the address of the real property where the nuisance is found
to exist.
      (1)   The service by certified mail shall be effective on the date of
mailing. City personnel shall cause at least one copy of the notice to be
posted conspicuously on the building, structure or on the real property or
thing alleged to be a nuisance.
      (2)   Proof of service notices shall be certified to at the time of
service by written declaration executed by the person effecting service,
declaring the time, date and manner in which service was made. The declaration,
together with any receipt care, returned acknowledgment or receipt by certified
mail, shall be affixed with a copy of the notice and order by city personnel.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-3) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011)
§ 90.04 NOTICE OF HEARING BEFORE CITY COUNCIL.
   If the property owner does not comply with the notice prescribed by §
90.03 by commencing the required work within the time allowed, or makes such
other arrangements as may be satisfactory, city personnel shall thereupon send
a notice, by certified mail, postage prepaid, return receipt requested, to the
owner, mortgage holder, deed of trust holder or holder of any other lien,
encumbrance, estate or legal interest of record as disclosed by the preliminary
title report obtained pursuant to §
90.03. The cost of said title report shall be charged to the owner.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-4) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011)
§ 90.05 HEARING BY CITY COUNCIL; FINDING OF NUISANCE.
   (A)   At the time fixed on the notice, the City Council shall proceed to
hear the testimony of the city personnel and the testimony of any other
interested party who may be present and desire to testify respecting the
condition of the property or thing, the estimated cost of repair, demolition,
removal or other appropriate action.
   (B)   Upon the conclusion of the hearing, the City Council will by
resolution, declare its findings and in the event it so concludes, it may
declare the property or thing to be a nuisance and direct the owner to obtain
the proper permits and physically commence abatement of the nuisance within ten
days, and to complete said abatement within 30 days by having the property
repaired, demolished, removed or other appropriate act necessary to cure the
nuisance.
   (C)   Such resolution shall further notify the owner of the property that if
the nuisance is not abated, the property will be the subject of repair,
demolition, removal or other appropriate act, as the case may be, by the city,
and the expenses thereof shall remain a lien on the property.
   (D)   The city personnel shall send copies of the resolution to the person
owning the property or thing, as such person’s name and address appears on the
last equalized assessment roll or as known to the city personnel, and to each
lessee, mortgage holder, deed of trust holder or other holder of any other
lien, encumbrance, estate or legal interest of record as shown on the
preliminary title report obtained pursuant to this chapter, at the last known
address of each such person.
   (E)   The City Clerk shall file a certified copy of any resolution declaring
real property a nuisance with the County Clerk and Recorder.
   (F)   The City Council will consider any extension of time limits set by
resolution, if the owner posts a cash deposit, in an amount fixed by the City
Council, within three days from the date of the grant of extension request.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-5) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011)
§ 90.06 ABATEMENT.
   (A)   In the event the owner does not commence the abatement of the nuisance
located on the real property within ten days prescribed, city personnel are
authorized to undertake the appropriate action such as demolition, repair or
removal necessary to cure the nuisance in accordance with the resolution of the
City Council or have the work done pursuant to purchase order or contract.
   (B)   City personnel shall keep an itemized account of all expenses involved
in the repair, demolition, removal or other appropriate act necessary to cure
the nuisance.
   (C)   City personnel shall mail a copy of the statement to the property
owner and to any holder of any interest of record, along with a notice of time
and place when and where the statement shall be submitted to the City Council
for approval and confirmation.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-6) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011)
§ 90.07 HEARING BY CITY COUNCIL; STATEMENT OF EXPENSE.
   (A)   Objections; protests. At the time fixed for the hearing of the
statement of expense, the City Council shall consider the statement together
with any objection or protest which may be raised by any of the property owners
liable to be assessed for the work and any other interested person and the same
shall be confirmed as stated, revised, corrected or modified by the City
Council.
   (B)   Payment of expenses. If said statement is not paid within five days of
the adoption of the resolution, it shall constitute a lien upon the real
property and shall be collected as a special assessment against the real
property.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-7) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011)
§ 90.08 RECORDATION OF CERTIFICATE; WHEN NUISANCE IS ABATED.
   When the City Council has by resolution declared that such property or thing
is being maintained as a nuisance, and such resolution has been recorded and
thereafter such nuisance is abated, city personnel shall prepare and file with
the County Clerk and County Recorder a certificate stating that such nuisance
has been abated and indicating the method of abatement.
(Prior Code, § 4-1-8) (Ord. 01-2011, passed 12-6-2011)
WEEDS
§ 90.20 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   WEED. Any plant which is ordinarily grown without cultivation and is not
grown for the purpose of landscaping or food production, except that lawns
shall be included in the term WEEDS for the purposes of height control as set
out in §
90.22.
(Prior Code, § 4-3-1) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
§ 90.21 UNCONTROLLED PLANT GROWTH; UNCONTROLLED WEEDS.
   It shall be unlawful and it is hereby declared a nuisance for any owner of
real property within the city to maintain, permit or suffer to exist in or upon
any real property within the city, any uncontrolled plant growth of any nature
which obstructs the view of motorists, creates a fire hazard or provides cover
for wild animals or reptiles, or any uncontrolled weed growth.
(Prior Code, § 4-3-2) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 90.22 DUTY OF OWNER.
   It shall be the duty of every owner of real property to cut, destroy or
remove or cause to be cut, destroyed or removed, all weeds in excess of 12
inches in height, growing thereon and upon any one-half of any street or alley
abutting his or her property to a height of four inches or less.
(Prior Code, § 4-3-3) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
§ 90.23 INSPECTION; NOTICE TO OWNER.
   (A)   Inspection. Whenever the Director of Public Works or his or her agents
have reason to believe that uncontrolled plant growth is present upon property
within the city in violation of this subchapter, he or she shall forthwith
inspect the premises.
   (B)   Notice. If such growth is found, the Director of Public Works shall
cause written notice to be served upon the owner of the property on which such
growth exists, directing the owner to comply with the provisions of this
subchapter by removing said conditions within seven days after service of
notice. Such notice shall advise the owner of what steps are required to come
into compliance with the provisions of this subchapter. The owner shall be
determined from the last completed assessment roll of the County Assessor.
(Prior Code, § 4-3-4) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
§ 90.24 PUBLICATION OF PUBLIC NOTICE.
   The City Administrative Clerk shall give notice to destroy weeds within the
city limits by publishing notice to the public at least once each week for two
consecutive weeks. Such notice shall advise the public as follows.
   (A)   Responsibility to destroy, remove or cut. All owners of real property
or agents having control thereof are responsible for destroying, removing or
cutting all weeds not later than 14 days from the date of the last publication
and to keep such property free of weeds through the end of the year.
   (B)   Failure to comply. Failure to remove weeds may cause the city to
remove the weeds and charge the cost thereof against the real property together
with an administrative cost and penalty for each time the city provides the
removal.
   (C)   Removal by city. If the owner or agent of the property continues to
neglect to maintain the prohibited areas free from weeds, the city may, at its
sole discretion, exterminate, remove or cut the weeds again as needed without
additional notice of any kind. Charges, including penalty, will be assessed for
each time the city removes the weeds.
(Prior Code, § 4-3-5) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 90.25 SERVICE OF NOTICE.
   Except for the notice to destroy weeds, which shall be deemed to be
completed to all property owners upon the second publication thereof, any
notice required to be given shall be sufficient if served personally or mailed
regular mail to the last known address or the last address shown on the tax
rolls of the county. Notice shall be deemed given when deposited in a United
States postal service receptacle.
(Prior Code, § 4-3-6) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
§ 90.26 FORCED COMPLIANCE; ASSESSMENT.
   (A)   Failure of owner to comply. The owner must take appropriate steps to
bring such property into compliance with the provisions of this subchapter
pursuant to the notice within seven days after service of such notice.
   (B)   Removal by city. If the notice shall not be obeyed within the time
specified, the Director of Public Works shall cause such work to be done and
make report thereof to the Clerk with an itemized account of the expenses
incurred in bringing such property into compliance and a description of the
land involved and shall include such necessary costs.
   (C)   Statement of costs; lien. The Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall promptly
send a statement of such account requesting payment to the owner of the
property. If such statement is not paid prior to the time that the city tax
assessments are submitted to the County Treasurer’s office, the Administrative
Clerk shall place such account as a special assessment on the property and such
special assessment shall be levied and collected in the same manner as other
special assessments by the city.
(Prior Code, § 4-3-7) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
CHAPTER 91: NOISE CONTROL
Section
   
91.01   Policy
   
91.02   Definitions
   
91.03   Noise prohibited
   
91.04   Maximum permissible levels
   
91.05   Measurement of noise
   
91.06   Action to abate
   
91.07   Permit for relief
 
   
91.99   Penalty
§ 91.01 POLICY.
   It is hereby declared to be the public policy of the city to regulate the
ambient noise levels in the city so as to preserve, protect and promote the
public health, safety and welfare and the peace and quiet of the inhabitants of
the city. It is the public policy of the city that every person is entitled to
live in an environment where ambient noise levels are not detrimental of life,
health and enjoyment of his or her property and community. It is hereby
declared that the making, creation and maintenance of excessive and unnecessary
noise within the city affect and are a menace to public health, comfort,
convenience, safety, welfare and prosperity of the people of the city. For the
purpose of controlling and reducing such noise, the city shall hereby set
necessary noise standards.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-1)
§ 91.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   dB(A). Sound levels in decibels measured on the A scale of a standard sound
level meter having characteristics defined by the American National Standards
Institute in their application standard.
   DECIBEL. A unit used to express the magnitude of the change in sound
intensity or some pressure level. The difference in decibels between a measured
sound pressure level and a reference sound pressure level is 20 times the
logarithm of their ration (i.e., SPL (dB) = 20 log Pa/Po, e.g., an increase of
six decibels (dB) represents a doubling of the sound pressure level, and a
decrease of six dB represents a halving of the sound pressure level (SPL)).
   GENERAL BUSINESS DISTRICT. All those areas designated as Business Districts
according to the city zoning laws and including those areas zoned C-1.
   GENERAL BUSINESS DISTRICT and HIGHWAY COMMERCIAL. All those areas designated
as Commercial Districts and Highway Commercial Districts according to the city
zoning laws and including those areas zoned C-2 and C-3.
   HEALTH. An optimal state of physical, mental and emotional well being and
not merely the absence of disease.
   INDUSTRIAL DISTRICTS. All those areas designated as industrial districts
according to the city zoning laws and including those areas zoned M.
   RESIDENTIAL ZONE. All those areas designated as essentially residential
districts according to the city zoning laws and including those areas zoned R-
1, R-2, R-3, R-4 and RP.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-2)
§ 91.03 NOISE PROHIBITED.
   (A)   The making and creating of an excessive or unusually loud noise within
the city as heard without measurement or as measured in the manner prescribed
in §
91.05 is hereby declared to be unlawful except when made under and in
compliance with a permit issued pursuant to §
91.07.
   (B)   No person shall operate any vehicle, machine or device or carry on any
other activity in such a manner as violates this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-3) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.04 MAXIMUM PERMISSIBLE LEVELS.
   (A)   Time periods and zones. Sound levels of noise radiating to a distance
of 25 feet or more from a source within the public right-of-way or from a
private or public property line in excess of the dB(A) levels established for
the time periods and zones listed in this section shall constitute prima facie
evidence such noise is a public nuisance and a violation of this chapter.
 
Zone                    8:00 a.m. to Next 8:00 p.m. 8:00 p.m. to Next 8:00 a.m.
Business District       86 dB(A)                    65 dB(A)
Commercial District and 86 dB(A)                    65 dB(A)
Light Industrial
Industrial District     86 dB(A)                    65 dB(A)
Residential             86 dB(A)                    65 dB(A)
 
   (B)   Allowable increase. In the hours between 8:00 a.m. and the next 8:00
p.m., the noise levels permitted in division (A) above may be increased by ten
dB(A) for a period not to exceed 15 minutes in any one-hour period.
   (C)   Construction projects. Construction projects shall be subject to the
maximum permissible noise levels specified for industrial zones for the period
within which construction is to be completed pursuant to any applicable
construction permit issued by proper authority. If no time limitation is
imposed, then for a reasonable period for completion of project.
   (D)   Speed or endurance events. This chapter is applicable to the use of
property for purposes of conducting speed or endurance events involving motor
or other vehicles, except during the specific period or periods of time within
which such use of the property is authorized by the jurisdictional authorities.
   (E)   Vehicles for off highway use. Except for such vehicles as are designed
exclusively for racing purposes, no person shall sell or offer for sale a new
motor vehicle or any self-propelled vehicle designed for off highway use which
produces a maximum noise exceeding the following noise limits as measured at a
distance of 25 feet from the center of the lane of travel or 25 feet from said
vehicle designed for off highway use, under test procedures established by the
City Council or its designee.
Any cycle, including motor driven cycle, manufactured before July 1,   93 dB(A)
1973
Any cycle, including motor driven cycle, manufactured after July 1,    91 dB(A)
1973
Any motor vehicle with gross vehicle weight rating of 6,000 pounds or  93 dB(A)
more manufactured before July 1, 1973
Any motor vehicle with gross vehicle weight rating of 6,000 pounds or  91 dB(A)
more manufactured after July 1, 1973
Any other motor vehicle manufactured before July 1, 1973               91 dB(A)
Any other motor vehicle manufactured after July 1, 1973                89 dB(A)
Any self-propelled vehicle for off highway use manufactured before     90 dB(A)
July 1, 1973
Any self-propelled vehicle for off highway use manufactured after July 80 dB(A)
1, 1973
 
   (F)   Exceptions. The requirements, prohibitions and terms of this chapter
shall not apply to the following uses:
      (1)   Emergency vehicles. Warning signal devices of any authorized
emergency vehicles acting in time of emergency;
      (2)   Civil defense. Civil defense warning signal devices when sounded
either for testing purposes or in time of actual emergency; and
      (3)   Temporary duration. Activities of a temporary duration permitted by
law and for which a license or permit has been granted by the city, including,
but not limited to, parades and fireworks displays.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-4) (Ord. 04-2006, passed 7-18-2006) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.05 MEASUREMENT OF NOISE.
   For the purpose of determining and classifying any noise as excessive or
unusually loud, as prohibited by this chapter, the following test measurements
and requirements may be applied; but a violation of §
91.03 may occur without the following measurements.
   (A)   A-weighted scale. The noise shall be measured on a sound level meter
meeting current American National Standard Institute standards operated on the
A-weighted scale.
   (B)   Wind velocity. Measurements with sound level meters shall be made when
the wind velocity at the time and place is not more than five mph.
   (C)   Ambient noise level. In all sound level measurements, the ambient
noise shall be at least ten dB(A) below the specific noise source being
measured.
   (D)   Environment. In all sound level measurements, consideration shall be
given to the effect of the ambient noise level created by the encompassing
noise of the environment from all sources at the time of said sound level
measurement.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-5)
§ 91.06 ACTION TO ABATE.
   Whenever there is a reason to believe a nuisance exists as defined in §
91.04, any resident of the city may maintain an action in equity in the
district court to abate and prevent such nuisance and to perpetually enjoin the
person conducting or maintaining the same, and the owner, lessee or agent of
the building or place in or upon which such nuisance exists, from directly or
indirectly maintaining or permitting such nuisance. The court may stay the
effect of any order issued hereunder for such time as is reasonably necessary
for the defendant to come into compliance with the provisions of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-6)
§ 91.07 PERMIT FOR RELIEF.
   (A)   Application. Applications for a permit for relief from the noise level
designated in this chapter, on the basis of undue hardship, may be made to the
City Council or its duly authorized representative.
   (B)   Conditions for issuance; term. Any permit so granted shall contain all
conditions upon which it has been granted and shall specify a reasonable time
that the permit shall be effective.
   (C)   Criteria for approval. The City Council, or its duly authorized
representative, may grant the relief as applied for if it finds:
      (1)   Additional time is necessary for applicant to alter or modify his
or her activity or operation to comply with this chapter;
      (2)   The activity, operation or noise source will be of temporary
duration and cannot be done in a manner complying with §
91.04;
      (3)   No other reasonable alternative is available to applicant; and
      (4)   The City Council may prescribe any conditions or requirements it
deems necessary to minimize adverse effects upon the community or the
surrounding neighborhood.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-7)
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   Any person, partnership, association or corporation violating the provisions
of this chapter shall be fined not less than $50 nor more than $300. Each
offense or violation of this chapter shall be deemed a separate and distinct
offense.
(Prior Code, § 5-6-8) (Ord. 52-85, passed 5-16-1994)

FIRE CODE
§ 92.01 ADOPTION.
   The current edition of the Fire Code and all accompanying appendices,
amendments and modification adopted by the Fire Marshal’s Bureau, State
Department of Justice (or its successor), as set out in the administrative
rules of the state, as amended from time to time by the Department of Justice,
shall be adopted by reference by administrative order of the City Council as
authorized by M.C.A. § 50-61-102(2) except for any exceptions noted in this
chapter or any regulations not applicable to local government jurisdictions.
These codes are applicable to all buildings within the code enforcement area of
the city.
   (A)   The adopted Fire Code shall regulate the fire safety/engineering in
the erection, construction, enlargement, alteration, repair, moving, removal,
demolition, conversion, occupancy, equipment, use, height, area and maintenance
of all buildings and/or structures in the city and its jurisdictional area.
   (B)   One copy of each code shall be on file in the office of the Fire
Chief.
   (C)   Any codes or amendments adopted by the Fire Marshal’s Bureau which
apply to local government jurisdictions, including the adoption of the latest
editions of the model technical codes or applicable administrative rules of the
state, shall become effective in the city upon order of the City Council within
ten days after the date that they are approved by a resolution at a City
Council meeting.
   (D)   City amendments thereto: In order to hear and decide appeals of
orders, decisions or determinations made by the Fire Chief relative to the
application and interpretation of this code, there shall be and is hereby
created a Board of Adjustment. The Board of Adjustment proceedings will be in
accordance with §§
155.295 through
155.308.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-1) (Ord. 02-2004, passed 6-15-2004)
§ 92.02 DUTIES OF FIRE DEPARTMENT.
   The 1997 Uniform Fire Code as adopted and amended herein shall be enforced
by the City Fire Department which is hereby established and be operated under
the supervision of the Chief of the Fire Department.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-2) (Ord. 02-99, passed 2-1-1999)
Cross-reference:
   Fire Department, see §§ 35.30 through 35.37
§ 92.03 DEFINITION.
   Wherever the word JURISDICTION is used in the Uniform Fire Code, it means
the City of Glendive.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-3) (Ord. 02-99, passed 2-1-1999)
§ 92.04 STORAGE OF FLAMMABLE OR COMBUSTIBLE LIQUIDS OUTSIDE OR INSIDE
ABOVEGROUND TANKS.
   (A)   Limits established. The limits referred to in Article 79 of the
Uniform Fire Code in which storage of flammable or combustible liquids in
outside or inside aboveground tanks is allowed are hereby established as
follows:
      (1)   Three hundred feet south of Allard Street from Sargent Avenue to
the centerline of the Burlington Northern Railroad tracks, 300 feet wide north
of Allard Street from the centerline of the Burlington Northern Railroad
mainline tracks to a point east in line with a projected line of the center of
Sargent Avenue;
      (2)   Areas designated as C-3 Highway Commercial as specified in Chapter
155 with minimum setback as specified in tables 7902.2-A through 7902.2-G and
7902.3-A of the Uniform Fire Code; and
      (3)   An area 600 feet north of the north right-of-way line of the Belle
Prairie Frontage Road in the Sunrise Division and east of the east property
line of Arizona Avenue, more particularly described as follows: tracts 10A,
10B, 10C, 10D, 10E, 11A and certificate of survey no. 216 of the amendment of
tracts 2, 8, 9, 10, 11, 1H, 1I, 1J of Sunrise Subdivision as those tracts are
recorded in the Clerk and Recorder’s office in Dawson County, Montana, under
book A131, page 284 and book A133, page 256.
   (B)   Exceptions.
      (1)   This section shall not apply to the storage of flammable or
combustible liquids used for the heating of structures; however, nothing in
this division (B) shall be construed to permit the storage of flammable or
combustible liquids for the purpose of sale except as provided in division (A)
above. The storage tank or reservoir permitted herein must comply fully with
any applicable sections of the Uniform Fire Code, Uniform Building Code,
Uniform Mechanical Code and NFPA and all storage reservoirs or tanks permitted
in this division (B) must be underground and in conformity with the uniform
codes stated above.
      (2)   If natural gas is readily available, bulk storage shall not be
allowed except as allowed in divisions (A)(1) and (A)(2) above.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-4) (Ord. 19-85, passed 8-17-1987)

      (3)   An area 600 feet north of the north right-of-way line of the Belle
Prairie Frontage Road in the Sunrise Division and east of the east property
line of Arizona Avenue, more particularly described as follows: tracts 10A,
10B, 10C, 10D, 10E, 11A and Certificate of Survey No. 216 of the amendment of
tracts 2, 8, 9, 10, 11, 1H, 1I, 1J of Sunrise Subdivision as those tracts are
recorded in the Clerk and Recorder’s Office in Dawson County, Montana, under

      (4)   Tract 1-2 description:

on the right side of the following described centerline, thence N58 39'11"W a
distance of 31.17 feet to the southwest corner of Tract A-2, which is also the
point of ending.
         (c)   Said above described access easement contains 623 square feet or
0.01 acres more or less and is subject to any previous easements, agreements,
conveyances and surveys.
   (B)   Exceptions.
      (1)   This section shall not apply to the storage of liquefied petroleum
gases used for the heating of structures; however, nothing in this division (B)
shall be construed to permit the storage of liquefied petroleum gases for the
purposes of sale except as provided in division (A) above. The storage tank or
reservoir permitted herein must comply fully with any applicable sections of
the Uniform Fire Code, Uniform Building Code, Uniform Mechanical Code and NFPA
58.
      (2)   If natural gas is readily available, bulk storage shall not be
allowed except as allowed in divisions (A)(1) and (A)(2) above.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-5) (Ord. 01-2013, passed 7-2-2013)
§ 92.06 UNDERGROUND STORAGE.
   No underground storage reservoir or tank as permitted herein shall be
installed or set in place or used until permission is first obtained from the
Fire Chief and the City Engineer or his or her representative.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-6)
§ 92.07 NEW MATERIALS, PROCESSES OR OCCUPANCIES.

committee to determine and specify, after giving affected persons an
opportunity to be heard, any new materials, processes or occupancies which
shall require permits in addition to those now enumerated in said code.
   (B)   The Chief of the Fire Department shall post such list in a conspicuous
place in his or her office and distribute copies thereof to interested persons.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-7)
§ 92.08 APPEALS.
   Whenever the Fire Chief disapproves an application or refuses to grant a
permit applied for, or when it is claimed the provisions of the code do not
apply, or the true intent and meaning of the code have been misconstrued or
wrongly interpreted, the applicant may appeal from the decision of the Fire
Chief to the City Council within 30 days from the date of the decision
appealed.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-8) (Ord. 02-99, passed 2-1-1999)
RESTRICTED AREAS AT FIRES

   Whenever a fire incident occurs within the city, the senior fire officer of
the Fire Department may prescribe the boundaries in the vicinity of any fire
incident within which no person except those admitted by order of the senior
fire officer shall be permitted to enter.
(Prior Code, § 7-3-1)

of the senior fire officer at any fire incident.
(Prior Code, § 7-3-2)
§ 92.22 BREAKING THROUGH LIMITS PROHIBITED.

so designated by the Chief of the Fire Department or officer in charge.
(Prior Code, § 7-3-3) Penalty, see §
92.99
FIREWORKS
§ 92.35 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   FIREWORKS. As defined in M.C.A. § 50-37-101.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-1) (Ord. 80-85, passed 5-18-1998)
§ 92.36 STORAGE.
   No person, firm or corporation shall store any fireworks meant for public
sale anywhere within the city limits except as necessary for the performance of
a public exhibition to be held pursuant to a permit issued as hereinafter
provided. Such storage shall be in a safe place, securely locked or guarded so
that no unauthorized person shall have access thereto, and protected from fire
hazards. The Fire Chief shall inspect the storage to determine whether the same
complies with the terms of this section.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-2) (Ord. 80-85, passed 5-18-1998)
§ 92.37 SALE.
   No person, firm or corporation shall sell any fireworks anywhere within the
city limits.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-3) (Ord. 80-85, passed 5-18-1998)
§ 92.38 PUBLIC DISPLAY.
   (A)   Permit required. A permit for a public display of fireworks shall be
issued by the City Fire Chief. No such permit shall be issued if it appears
from the information available to the Fire Chief that there are substantial
dangers to people or property due to the location, the fireworks proposed to be
used and the procedures to be used.
   (B)   Examination for permit. No person shall discharge fireworks at any
public display without a permit therefor issued by the Fire Chief. The City
Fire Chief shall issue the permit if the applicant demonstrates an ability to
provide a safe fireworks program.
   (C)   Indemnification. Any person who applies for such a permit, as a
condition therefor, shall agree to indemnify and hold harmless the city for any
damages caused as a result of such public display.
   (D)   Bond; certificate of insurance. No person, firm or corporation shall
discharge fireworks at any public exhibition held pursuant to a permit issued
as provided herein unless he or she shall have furnished a bond or certificate
of insurance in the amount of $1,000,000 for the payment of all damages which
may be caused either to a person or persons or to property by reason of the
permitted public exhibition and arising from any acts of the person so
obtaining a permit, his or her agents, employees or subcontractors.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-4) (Ord. 80-85, passed 5-18-1998) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.39 DISCHARGE OF FIREWORKS RESTRICTED.
   (A)   Except as permitted in division (B) below, no person shall combust,
detonate or display any kind of fireworks within the city limits.
   (B)   (1)   The City Council, at a time as designated in §
30.20, shall determine by resolution the appropriate permissible times of
detonation, combustion or display of legally authorized fireworks within the
city limits. The resolution must be approved no later than 15 days prior to the
permissible time periods authorized for the use of fireworks.
      (2)   Failure of the Council to pass such a resolution for a specific
year, in an appropriate timely manner, will revert the prior year’s resolution
as current policy for the present year.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-6) (Ord. 03-2009, passed 4-21-2009) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.40 AGE RESTRICTION.
   Anyone 15 years of age and younger shall have adult supervision at all times
when combusting or detonating fireworks.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-7) (Ord. 03-2003, passed 12-16-2003)
§ 92.41 SPECIAL EVENTS.
   Any special celebrations shall be coordinated through the Fire Department
and approved by the City Council prior to the event.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-8) (Ord. 03-2003, passed 12-16-2003)
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of the codes
adopted in §
92.01, or fail to comply therewith, or who shall violate or fail to comply with
any order made thereunder, or who shall build in violation of any detailed
statement of specifications or plans submitted and approved, and from which no
appeal has been taken, or who shall fail to comply with such an order as
affirmed or modified by the City Council or by a court of competent
jurisdiction, within the time fixed herein, shall, severally for each and every
such violation and noncompliance respectively, be guilty of a misdemeanor,
punishable by a fine of not less than $100 nor more than $500 or by
imprisonment for not less than three days nor more than 180 days or by both
such fine and imprisonment. The imposition of one penalty for any violation
shall not excuse the violation or permit it to continue; all of such persons
shall be required to correct or remedy such violations or defects within a
reasonable time; and when not otherwise specified, each ten days that
prohibited conditions are maintained shall constitute a separate offense. The
application of the penalty shall not be held to prevent the enforced removal of
the prohibited conditions.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-1)
   (C)   Any person who violates any provision of the 1997 Uniform Fire Code as
adopted and amended herein or fails to comply therewith, or who violates or
fails to comply with any order made thereunder, or who builds in violation of
any detailed statement of specifications or plans submitted and approved
thereunder, or any certificate or permit issued thereunder, and from which no
appeal has been taken, or who fails to comply with such an order as affirmed or
modified by the City Council or by a court of competent jurisdiction, within
the required time, shall, severally for each and every such violation and
noncompliance, respectively, be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine
of not less than $50 nor more than $500 or by imprisonment for not less than
seven days nor more than 180 days, or by both such fine and imprisonment. The
imposition of one penalty for any violation shall not excuse the violation or
permit it to continue; and all such persons shall be required to correct or
remedy such violations or defects within a reasonable time; and when not
otherwise specified, each ten days that prohibited conditions are maintained
shall constitute a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 7-2-9)
   (D)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §§
92.35 through
92.41 shall be punished in accordance with §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-5)
   (E)   Any person committing such an offense as provided in §
92.39(A) shall be deemed guilty of committing a misdemeanor punishable by a
fine of not less than $25 and not exceeding $500 or imprisoned for a term not
to exceed six months, or both.
(Prior Code, § 7-4-6)
(Ord. 80-85, passed 5-18-1998; Ord. 02-99, passed 2-1-1999; Ord. 02-2004,
passed 6-15-2004; (Ord. 03-2009, passed 4-21-2009)

Works designating the exterior boundaries of all dedicated parks and other park
property in the city.

   No person shall intentionally remove from its place, break, destroy, injure,
mar, cut or interfere with or deface any sign, image, fixture or ornament,
sidewalk, shrubbery, hedge, trees, lawn, grass, flowers, goods, chattels or any
other improvements or property in or about any city park.
(Prior Code, § 8-7-2) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 93.03 SWIMMING POOL; CHILDREN UNDER AGE.

the bathing pool of Lloyd Park, unless such person is accompanied by his or her
parent or legal guardian.

any unleashed dog or animal within the confines of all city parks, except such
parts as are used for public highways and are unimproved for park purposes.
(Prior Code, § 8-7-4)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 94.01 DEFECATION.
   (A)   Removal. An owner or person having custody of any dog or any other
animal shall not permit said dog or other animal to defecate on any school
ground, public street, alley, sidewalk, tree bank, boulevard, park or any other
public ground or any private property within the city other than the premises
of the owner or person having custody of said dog or other animal unless such
defecation is removed immediately.
   (B)   Disposal. No defecation or manure shall be dumped or left on any
street, alley, sidewalk, boulevard, tree bank, park, public grounds nor on any
open area or lot in any portion of the city, and any private property within
the city other than the premises of the owner or person having custody of such
dog or other animal; provided, however, that this provision shall not be
construed to prohibit the use of manure as fertilizer for lawns and gardens in
keeping with ordinary and customary practices in a manner that does not create
a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 5-3-1) (Ord. 75-85, passed 9-15-1997) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.02 RUNNING AT LARGE.
   (A)   Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for the owner or custodian of any
horses, cattle, swine, sheep, goats or other animals to allow any of such
animals to run at large in any of the streets, alleys or public places of the
city.
   (B)   Fowl; rabbits included. No owner or keeper of any chickens, ducks,
geese, turkeys, pigeons, domestic fowl or rabbits shall permit them to run at
large upon any street, alley, avenue, boulevard or public park or to trespass
upon the premises of another person within the city.
(Prior Code, § 5-3A-1) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.03 KEEPING LIVESTOCK.
   (A)   Prohibited. No person owning or having control of any goats, cattle,
horses, swine or sheep shall keep the same within the city, except to bring the
same to market for commercial or exhibition purposes and when brought therein
for that purpose the same shall be kept and cared for by the owner or person in
charge thereof.
   (B)   Exception. This section shall not preclude the stabling of animals at
the fairgrounds, livestock sales arena or a veterinary clinic.
   (C)   Agricultural or residential zoning districts.
      (1)   Permitted. Areas located within certain agricultural or residential
zoning districts as shown in the residential district regulations shall be
permitted to have livestock and/or fowl. However, the standards outlined below
must be satisfied, depending upon the size of the property.
      (2)   Criteria for allowing. The allowance of livestock and/or fowl in
agricultural and agricultural residential districts, situated within the limits
of the city, may be permitted when the regulations established in this division
(C)(2). However, if the number of animals requested exceeds the allowed limit
in below divisions, then the property must conform to the uses allowed by right
or conditional use application, as shown in the zoning regulations of the city.
         (a)   Lots two and a half to five net acres. Lots which are two and
one-half to five net acres in size are allowed to have livestock and/or fowl;
provided, that all of the following regulations are met.
            1.   One livestock and/or fowl unit is allowed per 20,000 square
feet of land devoted exclusively to the raising of the animal(s). Livestock or
fowl that are listed in the livestock and/or fowl unit table(s) below are
allowed types of animals under this division (C)(2)(a).
            2.   Supplemental feeding of the animal(s) is required.
            3.   Any keeping of animal(s) in this section shall be secondary
and accessory to the primary residential use of the property. Commercial
breeding and/or commercial raising of any type of animal or fowl shall be
prohibited, except as allowed by right or through conditional use in the zoning
regulations matrix.
            4.   All accessory structures used for the purpose of housing,
keeping or sheltering livestock or fowl shall be set back a distance of 50 feet
from any property line and 50 feet from any dwelling.
            5.   No accessory building or structure used for the housing of
livestock or fowl shall occupy any portion of a required front yard in any
district, except in the Agricultural Zoning District.
         (b)   Lots five acres to nine and ninety nine hundredths (9.99) acres.
Lots which are five to nine and ninety hundredths (9.99) net acres in size and
zoned agricultural are allowed to have livestock and/or fowl; provided, that
all of the following regulations are met:
            1.   One livestock and/or fowl unit per one acre of land devoted
exclusively to the raising of the animal(s), in which the animal(s) is
supplementally fed and/or is on irrigated pasture land.
            2.   One livestock and/or fowl unit per four acres of land devoted
exclusively to the raising of the animal(s), in which there is no supplemental
feeding and/or the animal is on unirrigated pasture land.
            3.   All accessory structures used for the purpose of housing,
keeping or sheltering livestock or fowl shall be set back a distance of 100
feet from any property line and 50 feet from any dwelling.
            4.   No accessory building or structure used for the housing of
livestock or fowl shall occupy any portion of a required front yard in any
district, except in the Agricultural Zoning District.
         (c)   Lots over nine and ninety nine hundredths (9.99) acres. Lots
which are greater than nine and ninety nine hundredths (9.99) net acres and
zoned agricultural shall be exempt from this section.
   (D)   Livestock and fowl units.
      (1)   Livestock and fowl units, for the purpose of this section, shall be
defined as follows.
Livestock Class Livestock Units
Livestock Class                 Livestock Units
Bull - mature                   1.00
Bull - yearling                 0.50
Calf - weaned or under 6 months 0.50
Colt - weaned                   1.00
Cow - mature                    1.00
Cow with calf                   1.00
Ewe - mature                    0.50
Ewe with lamb                   0.50
Goat - mature                   0.50
Goat with kid                   0.50
Heifer - one year or older      1.00
Horse - mature                  1.50
Horse with colt                 1.50
Kid - weaned or under 6 months  0.50
Lamb - weaned or under 6 months 0.50
Llama                           1.00
Ram - mature                    0.50
Steer - one year or older       1.00
Fowl Class                      Fowl Units
Hens, roosters or ducks         0.25 each
Turkeys or geese                0.50 each
 
      (2)   Livestock and/or fowl units for animals not listed herein shall be
determined if allowable by the Zoning Administrator.
(Prior Code, § 5-3A-2) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.04 CRUELTY TO ANIMALS.
   No person shall wantonly or cruelly injure, abuse or torture any animals
within the city.
(Prior Code, § 5-3A-3) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.05 VICIOUS, FEROCIOUS ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful and a nuisance for any person to keep, feed or harbor
or allow to stay about the premises occupied by him or her within this city,
any vicious, unruly or ferocious animal.
(Prior Code, § 5-3A-4) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
94.99
Cross-reference:
   Vicious dogs, see §
94.33
§ 94.06 FREEING ANIMALS FOR PURPOSE OF IMPOUNDMENT.
   No person shall take or drive any animal out of any enclosure, stable or
other building, or from outside of the city into the city, with the intent that
such animal shall be impounded.
(Prior Code, § 5-3A-5) (Ord. 04-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
94.99
DOGS
§ 94.20 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DOGS. Both male and female dogs, including those neutered or spayed.
   OWNER. Any person owning, having in possession or custody of or harboring or
giving shelter or refuge to any dog.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-1)
§ 94.21 RUNNING AT LARGE.
   (A)   Prohibited. No owner of a dog shall allow such dog to be on any public
street, alley, sidewalk or any public way or public place within the city;
provided, that this shall not prevent the owner from having the dog on the
streets in public places of the city when the dog is controlled either by chain
or leash.
   (B)   Dog shows, exhibitions and training courses. The Mayor may, upon
application of any person, authorize within the city, dog shows, exhibitions
and dog training courses, allowing the dogs participating therein to be
controlled only by competent attendants.
   (C)   Consent required. No owner of a dog shall allow such dog to run upon
any property in the city without the consent of the owner or tenant in
possession of such property.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-2) (Ord. 02-2023, passed 12-5-2023) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.22 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   (A)   Required. In the event any dog, excepting those under the age of five
months, is brought within the city within the license year, the owner or person
having possession or custody of or harboring or giving shelter or refuge to
such dog shall obtain a license for such dog as provided in this subchapter. It
shall be unlawful to have possession or custody of or harbor or give shelter or
refuge to any dog without a valid dog license, excepting those under the age of
five months.
   (B)   Exception. The provisions of this subchapter shall not apply to any
person visiting the city for a period not exceeding 30 days, and owning, having
in possession or custody of or harboring or giving shelter to a dog currently
licensed and bearing a license issued by another licensing authority.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-3) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.23 LICENSE FEES.
   All dog licenses obtained after April 1 of each year shall be double the
amount as set forth by resolution; except that this provision of double license
fee shall not apply to dogs brought into the city after April 1, or those
ineligible for licensing prior to that date.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-4)
§ 94.24 CERTIFICATES REQUIRED.
   (A)   Rabies vaccination. No license shall be issued for any dog until the
Finance Clerk-Treasurer has been furnished with a certificate of a licensed
veterinarian that such dog has been vaccinated against rabies within two years
immediately preceding the application for such license; provided, that such a
license may be issued for a dog under the age of six months with the
requirement that such dog be vaccinated for rabies as soon as such dog reaches
the age of six months.
   (B)   Spayed or neutered. No license shall be issued for a spayed female dog
or a neutered male dog until the Finance Clerk-Treasurer has been furnished
with a certificate from a licensed veterinarian that such dog has been so
altered.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-5) (Ord. 27-85, passed 5-15-1989)
§ 94.25 ISSUANCE OF LICENSE.
   Upon the delivery to the Finance Clerk-Treasurer of a veterinarian’s
certificate, as required in this subchapter, and the payment of the required
license fee, it shall be the duty of the Finance Clerk-Treasurer to issue a
license to the person applying therefor, bearing the number as provided in this
subchapter. The license shall give the date of issue, the date of expiration,
the amount paid, the name and address of the person to whom issued and the name
and sex of the dog.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-6)
§ 94.26 LICENSE TAGS.
   (A)   Metal tag issued. The Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall furnish with each
dog license issued pursuant to this subchapter a metal tag which shall be
stamped with the number corresponding with the number of the license and the
year for which issued.
   (B)   Display required. Such metal tag shall be conspicuously displayed on a
collar, strap or other device placed on such dog.
   (C)   Duplicate tag. If the metal tag is lost, a duplicate tag shall be
obtained by making application to the Finance Clerk-Treasurer who shall issue
such duplicate tag upon payment by the applicant of a fee as provided by
resolution.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-7)
§ 94.27 TERM.
   Dog licenses shall expires at 12:00 a.m. on December 31 of each and every
year, regardless of the date of issuance.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-8)
§ 94.28 TRANSFERABILITY.
   Dog licenses shall be issued in the name of the person having possession or
custody of or harboring or sheltering or giving refuge to the dog and shall be
serially numbered. Such license shall not be transferable or used to the
benefit of any other person than the person to whom issued, except upon
transfer of ownership of the dog for whom the license was purchased.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-9)
§ 94.29 RECORDS.
   The Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall keep a suitable record of the licenses
issued under the provisions of this subchapter and shall record all of the
facts required to be stated in the licenses.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-10)
§ 94.30 POLICE DOGS.
   (A)   Exempt from licensing. Dogs used by the Police Department are exempt
from all and any license fees established with respect to the regulation of
dogs kept within the city prescribed in §
94.22.
   (B)   Cruelty to police dogs. It shall be unlawful for any person at any
time to willingly or maliciously, aggravate, torment, disturb, incite, torture,
beat, kick, strike, mutilate, injure, disable or kill any dog used by the
Police Department of the city in the performance of the functions or duties of
such department, or to interfere with, distract or meddle with any such dog
while the dog is being used by said Police Department or any member thereof in
the performance of any of the functions or duties of said department or of said
officer or member.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-11) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.31 RABIES, DOGS SUSPECTED TO BE RABID.
   (A)   Authority to order impoundment. Any police officers, dogcatcher or the
poundmaster shall have the authority to order the owner of any dog showing
symptoms of rabies, or any dog which has bitten any person so as to cause an
abrasion of the skin, to subject such dog to the pound for a period not to
exceed 15 days.
   (B)   Alternative to impoundment. In lieu of submitting such dog to the
pound, the owner may, at his or her own expense, admit such dog to a licensed
veterinarian for examination.
   (C)   Uninfected animals; impoundment fees. If such dog shall be determined
free of rabies the same shall be returned to the owner upon payment of pound
fees as prescribed in §
94.34 for each day that the dog was impounded as and for boarding of same.
   (D)   Disposal of afflicted animals. Any dog found to be afflicted with
rabies shall be disposed of immediately either by the poundmaster or other
designated person.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-12)
§ 94.32 NUISANCE DOGS.
   (A)   Nuisance declared. It is hereby declared a public nuisance for any dog
to destroy property or other pets, to bite or chase after persons not
trespassing on the property of, or injuring or attempting to injure the person,
family or property of the owner, to chase vehicles in public streets or way; or
by prolonged howling, yelping, barking or by any other means causing annoyance
or disturbance to any person.
   (B)   Citations; complaints. No person shall own, harbor, keep or maintain
any such nuisance animal and it shall be the duty of the police, poundmaster or
other designated person to issue citations or file complaints for all such
violations occurring in their presence. Any person aggrieved by a nuisance
animal may file a complaint in the police court charging the owner with the
violation of this section, where the offense is not committed in the presence
of the police, poundmaster or other designated person.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-13)
§ 94.33 VICIOUS DOGS.
   On proper complaint filed in police court by or on behalf of any person
bitten by any dog within the city, brought against the person who owns, keeps
or harbors such dog at the time of the filing of the complaint, and upon due
proof, in the judgment of the court, that such dog bit such person without
provocation and not in defense of person or property, it shall be within the
discretion of the court that such dog be destroyed, and the poundmaster or
other designated person shall forthwith destroy such dog.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-14) (Ord. 02-2023, passed 12-5-2023)
§ 94.34 IMPOUNDMENT.
   (A)   Licensed dogs.
      (1)   Duty to impound. It shall be the duty of all police officers,
poundmaster and the dogcatcher to seize and impound any properly licensed dog
as defined in §
94.26 found to be running at large in violation of this subchapter.
      (2)   Notice of impoundment. Such dogs shall be retained in the pound.
The owner or an adult member of the owner’s family of every such dog so seized
shall be notified by the Police Department, poundmaster or dogcatcher of such
seizure within 48 hours of such seizure by personal notice or is sent by
registered or certified mail to the owner’s last known address.
      (3)   Redemption. The same may redeem such dog upon payment of pound fees
and all costs incurred, as provided by resolution.
      (4)   Unredeemed animals. At the expiration of 72 hours after impounding
any dog, and after a reasonable and diligent effort has been made to locate the
dog’s owner, the poundmaster is authorized to sell any such dog to any such
person not the owner thereof for the best price obtainable, and the sum
received shall be paid by the poundmaster in the office of the Finance Clerk-
Treasurer; or, if the dog cannot be sold, the dog shall be disposed of in any
humane and lawful manner.
   (B)   Unlicensed dogs.
      (1)   Nuisance declared; duty to impound. All dogs not licensed as
provided in this subchapter are declared to be a public nuisance, whether or
not they are running at large, and it is the duty of all police officers, the
poundmaster or the dogcatcher to take up and impound any dog not so licensed.
      (2)   Detention; attempt to notify owner. Every dog so seized shall be
retained in the pound for a period of 72 hours, during which time a reasonable
and diligent search shall be made by the poundmaster, police or dogcatcher to
locate and notify the owner of such dog.
      (3)   Redemption. At any time during the 72 hour period of detention, the
owner of such dog may redeem the same by procuring the required dog license and
by paying, in addition, a fee as provided by resolution to the Finance Clerk-
Treasurer, poundmaster or dogcatcher, plus the fees for impoundment established
by resolution. Such money shall be paid to the office of the Finance Clerk-
Treasurer by the poundmaster or dogcatcher.
      (4)   Unredeemed animals. At the expiration of the 72 hours after
impounding any dog, and after a reasonable and diligent effort has been made to
locate the dog’s owner, the poundmaster is authorized to sell any such dog to
any such person not the owner thereof for the best price obtainable, and the
sum received shall be paid by the poundmaster in the office of the Finance
Clerk-Treasurer, or the dog shall be disposed of in any humane and lawful
manner.
      (5)   Penalty. Any owner of any unlicensed dog running at large shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished
as provided in §
94.99
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-15) (Ord. 23-85, passed 8-1-1988)
Cross-reference:
   Vicious animals generally, see §
94.05
CATS
§ 94.45 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   (A)   Required. In the event any cat, excepting those under the age of six
months, is brought within the city within the license year, the owner or person
having possession or custody of or harboring or giving shelter or refuge to
such cat shall obtain a license for such cat as provided in this subchapter. It
shall be unlawful to have possession or custody of or harbor or give shelter or
refuge to any cat without a valid cat license excepting those under the age of
six months.
   (B)   Exception. The provisions of this subchapter shall not apply to any
person visiting the city for a period not exceeding 30 days and owning, having
in possession or custody of or harboring or giving shelter to a cat currently
licensed and bearing a license issued by another licensing authority.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-1) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.46 LICENSE FEES.
   The fees for all cat licenses are set forth by resolution. The fees for all
cat licenses obtained after April 1 of each year shall be double the amount as
set forth herein; except that the provision of double license fee shall not
apply to cats brought into the city after April 1 or those ineligible for
licensing prior to that date.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-2) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993)
§ 94.47 CERTIFICATES REQUIRED.
   (A)   Rabies vaccination. All persons residing in the city and owning or
having in their possession any cat shall be required to have said cat
inoculated for rabies, distemper and other dangerous disease, and no license
shall be issued for any cat until the Finance Clerk-Treasurer has been
furnished with a certificate of a licensed veterinarian that such cat has been
inoculated as set forth above within two years immediately proceeding the
application for such license; provided, however, that such a license may be
issued for a cat under the age of six months with the requirement that such cat
be vaccinated as soon as such cat reaches the age of six months.
   (B)   Spayed or neutered. No license shall be issued for a spayed female cat
or a neutered male cat until the Finance Clerk-Treasurer has been furnished
with a certificate from a licensed veterinarian that such cat has been so
altered.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-3) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993)
§ 94.48 ISSUANCE OF LICENSE.
   Upon the delivery to the Finance Clerk-Treasurer of a veterinarian
certificate, as required in this subchapter, and the payment of the required
license fee, it shall be the duty of the Finance Clerk-Treasurer to issue a
license to the person applying therefor, bearing the number as provided in this
subchapter. The license shall give the date of issue, the date of expiration,
the amount paid, the name and address of the person to whom issued and the name
and sex of the cat.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-4) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993)
§ 94.49 LICENSE TAGS.
   (A)   Metal tag issued. The Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall furnish with each
cat license issued pursuant to this subchapter a metal tag which shall be
stamped with the number corresponding with the number of the license and the
year for which issued.
   (B)   Display required. Such metal tag shall be conspicuously displayed on a
collar, strap or other device placed on such cat.
   (C)   Duplicate tag. If the metal tag is lost, a duplicate tag shall be
obtained by making application to the Finance Clerk-Treasurer who shall issue
such duplicate tag upon payment by the applicant of a fee as provided by
resolution.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-5) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993)
§ 94.50 TERM.
   Cat licenses shall expire at 12:00 a.m. on December 31 of each and every
year regardless of the date of issuance.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-6) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993)
§ 94.51 RECORDS.
   The Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall keep a suitable record of the licenses
issued under the provisions of this subchapter and shall record all of the
facts required to be stated in the licenses.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-7) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993)
§ 94.52 TRANSFERABILITY.
   Cat licenses shall be issued in the name of the person having possession or
custody of or harboring or sheltering or giving refuge to the cat and shall be
serially numbered. Such license shall not be transferrable or used to the
benefit of any other person than the person to whom issued except upon transfer
of ownership of the cat for whom the license was purchased.
(Prior Code, § 5-3C-8) (Ord. 43-85, passed 2-1-1993)
§ 94.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of §
94.30 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and punished in accordance with §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-11)
   (C)   Any person violating §
94.32 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and punished in accordance with §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-13)
   (D)   In addition to the dog in §
94.33 being subject to destruction, the dog’s owner(s) shall be deemed guilty
of a misdemeanor and punished with a fine of up to $500.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-14)
   (E)   The owner of any dog running at large shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof shall be punished by a penalty as
provided in division (F) below.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-15)
   (F)   The penalty for violation of §§
94.21 and
94.34 shall be in the following amounts.
      (1)   First violation. For the first violation, the fine shall be $100.
      (2)   Second violation. For the second violation occurring within one
year of the first violation, the penalty shall be $200.
      (3)   Third and subsequent violations. For the third and any additional
violation within one year, the fine shall be $300.
      (4)   Imprisonment. In addition to the fines as herein provided, a
penalty not to exceed 30 days’ imprisonment in the city jail shall be imposed.
(Prior Code, § 5-3B-16)
(Ord. 23-85, passed 8-1-1988; Ord. 03-2015, passed 2-3-2015; Ord. 01-2020,
passed 5-5-2020; Ord. 02-2023, passed 12-5-2023)

CHAPTER 110: AMUSEMENTS
Section
Gaming
   
110.01   Short title

110.99   Penalty
GAMING
§ 110.01 SHORT TITLE.
   This subchapter may be cited as the Glendive Gaming Ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 3-3-1)
§ 110.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AUTHORIZED CARD GAME. Card games known as poker.
   GAMING DEVICE. An apparatus or machine used for the playing of the games
commonly referred to as keno, bingo or poker.
   MINOR. An individual under the age of 18 years.
   PERSON. Every individual, copartnership, corporation, nationally recognized
veterans’ organization or nationally recognized fraternal organization.
   PREMISES. Any building, structure, lot or parcel of real property under the
control of any person.
(Prior Code, § 3-3-2) (Ord. 15-85, passed 5-18-1987)
§ 110.03 CLOSING HOURS.
   (A)   Card game. No authorized card game may legally be played from 2:00
a.m. to 8:00 a.m. on Monday through Friday of each week. Authorized card games
may be played during any hour on Saturdays and Sundays.
   (B)   Gaming device. All gaming devices shall be shut off each day during
the hours from 2:00 a.m. to 8:00 a.m.
(Prior Code, § 3-3-3) (Ord. 15-85, passed 5-18-1987; Ord. 02-2009, passed 3-17-
2009)
§ 110.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to a
penalty as provided in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 3-3-4)
CHAPTER 111: PEDDLERS, ITINERANT MERCHANTS AND SOLICITORS
Section
   
111.01   Definitions
   
111.02   License requirement
   
111.03   Application procedure
   
111.04   Standards for issuance
   
111.05   Revocation procedure
   
111.06   Standards for revocation
   
111.07   Appeal procedure
   
111.08   Exhibition of identification
   
111.09   City policy on soliciting
   
111.10   Notice regulating soliciting
   
111.11   Duty of solicitors to ascertain notice
   
111.12   Prohibited solicitation
 
   
111.99   Penalty
§ 111.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BUSINESS. The business carried on by any person who is an itinerant
merchant, peddler or solicitor as defined in this section.
   GOODS. Merchandise of any description whatsoever, and includes, but is not
restricted to, wares and foodstuffs.
   ITINERANT MERCHANT. Any person, whether as owner, agent or consignee, who
engages in a temporary business of selling goods within the city and who, in
the furtherance of such business, uses any building, structure, vehicle or any
place within the city.
   PEDDLER. Any person, not an itinerant merchant, who:
      (1)   Travels from place to place by any means carrying goods for sale,
or making sales, or making deliveries; or
      (2)   Without traveling from place to place, sells or offers goods for
sale from any public place within the city.
   SOLICITOR. Any person who travels by any means from place to place, taking
or attempting to take orders for sale of goods to be delivered in the future or
for service to be performed in the future. A person who is a SOLICITOR is not a
peddler.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025)
§ 111.02 LICENSE REQUIREMENT.
   (A)   Any person who is an itinerant merchant, peddler or solicitor shall
obtain a license before engaging in such activity in the city.
   (B)   The fee for the license required by this chapter shall be set from
time to time by the City Council.
   (C)   No license issued under this chapter shall be transferable.
   (D)   All licenses issued under this chapter shall expire 90 days after the
date of issuance thereof. (Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025) Penalty see §
111.99 
§ 111.03 APPLICATION PROCEDURE.
   (A)   All applicants for licenses required by this chapter shall file an
application with the City Finance Clerk-Treasurer. This application shall be
signed by the applicant if an individual, or by all partners if a partnership,
or the president if a corporation. The applicant may be requested to provide
information concerning the following items:
      (1)   The name and address of the applicant;
      (2)   (a)   The name of the individual having management authority or
supervision of the applicant’s business during the time that it is proposed to
be carried on in the city;
         (b)   The local address of such individual;
         (c)   The permanent address of such individual; and
         (d)   The capacity in which said individual will act;
      (3)   The name and address of the person, if any, for whose purpose the
business will be carried on, and, if a corporation, the state of incorporation;
      (4)   The time period or periods during which it is proposed to carry on
an applicant’s business;
      (5)   (a)   The nature, character and quality of the goods and serviced
to be offered for sale or delivered;
         (b)   If goods, their invoice value and whether they are to be sold by
sample as well as from stock; and
         (c)   If goods, where and by whom such goods are manufactured or
grown, and where such goods are at the lime of application;
      (6)   The nature of the advertising proposed to be done for the business;
and
      (7)   Whether or not the applicant, or the individual identified in
division (A)(2)(a) above, or the person identified in division (A)(3) above has
been convicted of any crime or misdemeanor and, if so, the nature of each
offense and the penalty assessed for each offense.
   (B)   Applicants for peddler or solicitor licenses may be required to
provide further information concerning the following items, in addition to that
requested under division (A) above:
      (1)   A description of the applicant; and
      (2)   A description of any vehicle proposed to be used in the business,
including its registration number, if any.
   (C)   All applicants for licenses required by this chapter shall attach to
their application, if required by the city, credentials from the person, if any
for which the applicant proposes to do business, authorizing the applicant to
act as such representative.
   (D)   Applicants who propose to handle foodstuffs shall also attach to their
application, in addition to any attachments required under division (C) above,
a statement from a licensed physician, dated not more than ten days prior to
the date of the application, certifying the applicant to be free of contagious
or communicable disease.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025) Penalty, see §
111.99 
§ 111.04 STANDARDS FOR ISSUANCE.
   (A)   Upon receipt of an application, an investigation of the applicant’s
business reputation and moral character shall be made.
   (B)   The application shall be approved unless such investigation discloses
tangible evidence that the conduct of the applicant’s business would pose a
substantial threat to the public health, safety, morals or general welfare. In
particular, tangible evidence that the applicant:
      (1)   Has been convicted of a crime of moral turpitude;
      (2)   Has made willful; misstatements in the application;
      (3)   Has committed prior violations of ordinances pertaining to
itinerant merchants, peddlers, solicitors and the like;
      (4)   Has committed prior fraudulent acts; or
      (5)   Has a record of continual breaches of solicited contracts.
will constitute valid reasons for disapproval of an application.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025)
§ 111.05 REVOCATION PROCEDURE.
   Any license or permit granted under this chapter may be revoked by the City
Finance Clerk-Treasurer after notice and hearing, pursuant to the standards in
§
111.06. Notice of hearing for revocation shall be given in writing, setting
forth specifically the grounds of the complaint and the time and place of the
hearing. Such notice shall be mailed to the licensee at the last known address,
at least ten days prior to the date set for the hearing.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025)
§ 111.06 STANDARDS FOR REVOCATION.
   A license granted under this chapter may be revoked for any of the following
reasons:
   (A)   Any fraud or misrepresentation contained in the license application;
   (B)   Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made in connection
with the business being conducted under the license;
   (C)   Any violation of this chapter;
   (D)   Conviction of the licensee of any felony, or conviction of the
licensee of any misdemeanor involving moral turpitude; or
   (E)   Conducting the business licensed in an unlawful manner or in such a
way as to constitute a menace to the health, safety, morals or general welfare
of the public.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025)
§ 111.07 APPEAL PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Any person aggrieved by a decision under §§
111.04 or
111.06 shall have the right to appeal to the City Council. The appeal shall be
taken by filing with the City Council, within 14 days after notice of the
decision has been mailed to such person’s last known address, a written
statement setting forth the ground for appeal. The City Council shall set the
time and the place for a hearing, and notice of such hearing shall be given to
such person in the same manner as provided in §
111.05.
   (B)   The order of the City Council after the hearing shall be final.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025)
§ 111.08 EXHIBITION OF IDENTIFICATION.
   (A)   Any license issued to an itinerant merchant under this chapter shall
be posted conspicuously in or at the place named therein. In the event more
than one place within the city shall be used to conduct the business licensed,
separate licenses shall be issued for each place.
   (B)   The City Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall issue a license to each peddler
or solicitor licensed under this chapter. The license shall contain the words
“Licensed Peddler” or “Licensed Solicitor,” the expiration date of the license,
and the number of the license. The license shall be kept with the licensee
during such time they are engaged in the business licensed.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025) Penalty, see §
111.99 
§ 111.09 CITY POLICY ON SOLICITING.
   It is hereby declared to be the policy of the city that the occupants of the
residences in the city shall make the determination of whether solicitors shall
be, or shall not be, invited to their respective residences.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025)
§ 111.10 NOTICE REGULATING SOLICITING.
   (A)   Notice of the refusal of invitation to solicitors, to any residence,
shall be given on a weatherproof card, approximately three inches by four
inches in size, exhibited upon or near the main entrance door to the residence,
indicating the determination by the occupant, containing the applicable words,
as follows: “NO SOLICITORS INVITED.”
   (B)   The letters shall be at least one-third-inch in height. For the
purpose of uniformity, the cards shall be provided by the Chief of Police to
persons requesting, at the cost thereof.
   (C)   The card so exhibited shall constitute sufficient notice to any
solicitor of the determination by the occupant of the residence of the
information contained thereon.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025)
§ 111.11 DUTY OF SOLICITORS TO ASCERTAIN NOTICE.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of every solicitor upon going onto any premises
in the city upon which a residence is located to first examine the notice
provided for in §
111.10, if any is attached, and be governed by the statement contained on the
notice. If the notice states: “NO SOLICITORS INVITED” then the solicitor,
whether registered or not, shall immediately and peacefully depart from the
premises.
   (B)   Any solicitor who has gained entrance to any residence, whether
invited or not, shall immediately and peacefully depart from the premises when
requested to do so by the occupant.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025) Penalty, see §
111.99 
§ 111.12 PROHIBITED SOLICITATION.
   It is hereby declared to be unlawful and shall constitute a nuisance for any
person to go upon any premises and ring the doorbell upon or near any door, or
create and sound in any manner calculated to attract the attention of the
occupant of such residence, for the purpose of securing an audience with the
occupant thereof and engage in soliciting in defiance of the notice exhibited
at the residence in accordance with the provisions of § 110.10.
(Ord. 02-2025, passed 2-18-2025) Penalty, see §
111.99 
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall,
upon conviction thereof, be punished as set forth in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 3-4-5)
