112.999   Penalty
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 112.001 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the words LIQUOR, BEER and WINE shall be
defined in accordance with the definitions given in the State Alcoholic
Beverage Code.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-1)
§ 112.002 APPROVAL OF LOCATION REQUIRED.
   (A)   No license shall be issued or transferred to any person for the sale
of liquor, wine or beer unless the location of the place and/or the building in
which the liquor, wine or beer is to be sold at retail is approved by a vote of
two-thirds of the City Council, which vote shall be held at a regular session
of the City Council with all members of the City Council present, and after a
full hearing upon the application. This section applies to both on- and off-
premises licenses.
   (B)   The decision of the City Council shall be conclusive.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-2)
§ 112.003 LIGHTING.
   All places where beer or intoxicating liquors are sold, served or given away
shall maintain, during business hours, lights in such place of business of at
least one-fourth candlepower as determined by standard gauges for measuring
light.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-3)
§ 112.004 ADMISSION AFTER HOURS.
   No person shall be permitted in any place where beer or intoxicating liquors
are sold, served or given away during the hours or times when such places of
business are required under law or ordinance to be closed, except the owner or
employees thereof occupied in the lawful discharge of their duties.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-4) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.005 MINORS.
   (A)   Frequenting liquor establishments.
      (1)   Prohibited. Minors under the age of 18 years shall not frequent,
loiter, go or remain in any premises which derives its principal business from
the sale of alcoholic beverages or which advertises as an establishment whose
principal business is the sale of alcoholic beverages, unless the minor is upon
some lawful errand and sent under the direction, consent and knowledge of the
parent or guardian; where, under this section, a minor’s presence in such an
establishment is permitted, the minor, under no circumstances, shall purchase,
possess or consume any alcoholic beverage.
      (2)   Unlawful to allow. No owner, proprietor or agent or employee of an
owner may allow or permit any such minor to frequent, loiter or remain within
the premises in violation of this section.
      (3)   Exceptions. This section shall not apply to those premises which
serve food or permit recreation or amusement as the principal business and
would serve alcoholic beverages only incidentally. This section shall also not
apply to those premises, otherwise restricted, during hours that said premises
do not sell or make available alcoholic beverages.
   (B)   Sale to minors. No licensee under this chapter or his or her employees
shall sell, deliver or give away or cause or permit to be sold, delivered or
given away any liquor, beer or wine to any person under the age of 21 years.
   (C)   Purchase. No person under the age of 21 years shall purchase any
liquor, beer or wine, and no person shall sell or purchase for a person under
the age of 21 years any liquor, beer or wine.
   (D)   Misrepresentation of age. No person who is prohibited by state law
from purchasing alcoholic beverages shall knowingly misrepresent his or her age
by a written card or document for the purpose of obtaining liquor, beer or wine
even though the purchase and sale is not consummated.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-5) (Ord. 18-85, passed 6-15-1987; Ord. 32-85, passed 5-7-
1990) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.006 PUBLIC DRINKING, DISPLAY AND EXHIBITION.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      BEER.
         (a)   1.   A malt beverage containing not more than 8.75% of alcohol
by volume; or
            2.   Aan alcoholic beverage containing not more than 14% alcohol by
volume:
               a.   That is made by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion
or decoction, or a combination of both, in potable brewing water, of malted
cereal grain; and
               b.   In which the sugars used for fermentation of the alcoholic
beverage are at least 75% derived from malted cereal grain measured as a
percentage of the total dry weight of the fermentable ingredients.
         (b)   The term does not include a caffeinated or stimulant-enhanced
malt beverage.
      BUSINESS DISTRICT. The portion of the city which comprises the following
designated areas:
         (a)   The portion of Merrill Avenue from West Brennan Street to Clough
Street and one-half block on either side of said portion of Merrill Avenue;
         (b)   The portion of Kendrick Avenue from West Clement Street to South
Douglas Street and one-half block on either side of said portion of Kendrick
Avenue; and
         (c)   The portion of Meade Avenue from West Clement Street to South
Douglas Street and one-half block on either side of said portion of Meade
Avenue.
      LIQUOR or LIQUORS. Any alcoholic, spirituous, vinous, fermented, malt or
other liquor, but which shall not mean or include BEER or TABLE WINE as those
terms are defined in the State Alcoholic Beverage Code.
      PUBLIC DISPLAY OR EXHIBITION OF BEER OR LIQUOR. The carrying or
exhibiting of open cans or bottles of beer or liquor, or the carrying or
exhibiting of glasses or other types of containers, either empty or containing
beer or liquor within a public place, as defined herein; but does not include
carrying or transporting beer or liquor in sacks, cases, boxes, cartons or
other similar containers that conceal the contents, provided such beer or
liquor has not been opened and seals have not been broken; it further does not
include the collection and transportation of empty containers for salvage or
refuse collection purposes in those portions of vehicles not used for passenger
purposes.
      PUBLIC DRINKING. The drinking or consuming of beer or liquor in any
public place, as defined herein.
      PUBLIC PLACES. All streets, avenues, alleys, parking lots and sidewalks,
not including the inside of any buildings, within the Business District of the
city, as defined in this section, and within 80 feet of any doorway of any
retail liquor or beer establishment in the city, and within 80 feet of any
portion of public or private school property in the city.
   (B)   Prohibited. Public drinking and public display or exhibition of beer
or liquor, as defined in division (A) above, are hereby prohibited, and it
shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor for any person to engage in public
drinking, as herein defined within the limits of the city. It shall be unlawful
and a misdemeanor for any person to engage in any public display or exhibition
of beer or liquor, as herein defined within the city limits.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-6) (Ord. 33-85, passed 5-7-1990) Penalty, see §
112.999
BEER AND WINE
§ 112.020 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the definition of words and terms
contained in the State Alcoholic Beverage Code are adopted as fixing the
meaning of the words and terms as used in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-1)
§ 112.021 STATUTE ADOPTED.
   All the prohibitory and regulatory provisions of the State Alcoholic
Beverage Code are hereby adopted as provisions of this subchapter, except the
provisions of the Act relating to the licensing of common carriers. It is the
duty of all city officials, and particularly of the city police force, to aid
in the enforcement of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code. All licenses issued
under the provisions of this subchapter shall be subject to all applicable
prohibitory and regulatory provisions of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code in
addition to the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-2) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.022 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   No person to whom a license is issued by the State Department of Revenue for
the manufacture, sale or distribution of beer and wine within the city shall
engage in such manufacture, sale or distribution of beer and wine within the
city without first obtaining from the Finance Clerk-Treasurer a city license
and paying for the same as provided in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-3)
§ 112.023 APPLICATION.
   (A)   Required. The applicant for a license required by this subchapter
shall present to the Finance Clerk-Treasurer an application for a city license
to dispense beer and wine subject to the provisions of the State Alcoholic
Beverage Code and this code and any other ordinances of the city applicable
thereto.
   (B)   Form. The application shall be on an official form to be furnished by
the Finance Clerk-Treasurer, which shall be in substantially the following
language.
 
   CITY OF GLENDIVE
   APPLICATION FOR LICENSE TO DISPENSE BEER AND WINE
 
To the Finance Clerk-Treasurer of Glendive, Montana:
 
   The undersigned hereby makes application for a license to dispense beer and wine within the City of Glendive pursuant to the
provisions of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code and the applicable ordinances of the city.
 
   My name is                                                                    
   Sex                             
   Age                              
 
I am the holder of a license from the State of Montana under the State Alcoholic Beverage Code as a                        . The date
of said license is                     ; its number is                 ; and it expires                                 . My residence
is                                                        ; and I have resided there                                               .
 
The location in the City of Glendive at which I desire a license to dispense beer and wine is                                      .
 
I understand that this license is issued subject to the terms and conditions of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code as well as those of
the city ordinances of Glendive applicable thereto;
 
I also understand that the revocation, withdrawal or suspension of any license granted to me by the State of Montana pursuant to the
State Alcoholic Beverage Code shall simultaneously and without further action of the City, operate as a revocation, withdrawal or
suspension of any city license created pursuant to this application.
 
STATE OF MONTANA

COUNTY OF DAWSON

(Prior Code, § 3-1A-4)
§ 112.024 FEES.
   The fees for licenses under this subchapter shall be payable in advance in
the amounts specified by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-5)
§ 112.025 STATE LICENSE PREREQUISITE.
   Nothing contained in this subchapter shall authorize the manufacture,
possession or sale of beer and wine within the city by any person not holding a
state license as required by the State Alcoholic Beverage Code unless such
manufacture, possession or sale shall be permitted by the laws of the United
States of America.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-6)
§ 112.026 INVESTIGATION; ISSUANCE.
   (A)   Issuance by Finance Clerk-Treasurer. Upon the filing of an application
for a license under this subchapter, it shall be the duty of the Finance Clerk-
Treasurer to pass originally upon the moral qualifications of the applicant.
The fact that a certificate of good moral character has heretofore been issued
to the same applicant by the state shall not be conclusive of such fact upon
the Finance Clerk-Treasurer, but the Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall have
authority and it shall be his or her duty to ascertain and pass upon the moral
qualifications of the applicant. In the event the Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall
determine that the applicant is of good moral character, he or she shall issue
such license forthwith.
   (B)   Investigation. In case he or she shall determine that the applicant is
not a person of good moral character, or for any other reason is not qualified
to receive such license, the Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall refer the
application to a Board consisting of the Chief of Police and the Fire and
Police Committee for an investigation and for report to the City Council. The
Committee shall thereupon investigate the applicant and may for the purpose
receive testimony from the applicant or from any other source as to the moral
qualifications and standing of the applicant.
   (C)   Council action. The Board shall report its findings to the City
Council and the City Council shall, by an order entered upon its minutes,
either grant or deny the license applied for and shall direct the Finance
Clerk-Treasurer accordingly.
   (D)   Denial; return of fee. If a license is refused, the fee tendered shall
be returned to the applicant.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-7)
§ 112.027 LICENSE.
   (A)   Form; contents. Licenses issued under the provisions of this
subchapter shall be in substantially the following form.
 
   State Alcoholic Beverage Code
   CITY OF GLENDIVE LICENSE
 
   The City of Glendive hereby licenses                                            as a                                               under
and subject to all the provisions of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code and the ordinances of Glendive applicable to the subject. The
business authorized under this license shall be carried on only at the premises known as
                                                                in Glendive, Montana, and at no other place unless otherwise authorized by
the City Council. The license expires                                   unless sooner suspended or revoked.
 
   This license shall be prominently posted at the premises herein described and is subject to suspension or revocation as provided by the
laws of Montana and the ordinances of the City of Glendive.
 
      Dated this           day of                               ,       .
 
                                                           
          Finance Clerk-Treasurer
 
   (B)   Record. The Finance Clerk-Treasurer shall keep an accurate record of
all licenses issued under this subchapter indicating all essential details
thereto.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-8)
§ 112.028 TERM OF LICENSE.
   All licenses issued in any year shall expire June 30 at 12:00 a.m. of such
year.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-9) (Ord. 02-2020, passed 7-2-2020)
§ 112.029 RENEWAL; TRANSFERABILITY.
   (A)   Renewal. Any person holding a license issued pursuant to the
provisions of this subchapter may renew the same for the ensuing year by paying
the Finance Clerk-Treasurer, in advance, the license fee provided by this
subchapter.
   (B)   Transfer of license. Whenever any licensee shall transfer a state
license issued under the State Alcoholic Beverage Code, the transferee shall
not be permitted to manufacture, sell or handle beer or wine within the city
without first procuring from the Finance Clerk-Treasurer a license in the same
manner as required by this subchapter for the issuance of an original license;
provided, that in the event a city license is issued to such transferee, no
charge shall be made for the same by the city for the unexpired period for
which the original license was issued.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-10)
§ 112.030 REGULATIONS.
   The following provisions shall apply to all sales of beer and wine by all
licensees.
   (A)   Sale to minors; minors frequenting premises. No licensee shall sell or
furnish beer or wine to any person under the age of 21 years. In any
prosecution for the violation of this provision, the burden of proof shall be
upon the licensee to establish the fact that the person to whom beer or wine
was sold or furnished by such licensee was over the age of 21 years. No person
under the age of 21 shall misstate or misrepresent his or her true age to the
licensee or to any other person for the purpose of inducing such licensee to
sell or furnish beer or wine to any person under the age of 21.
   (B)   Sale to habitual drunkards. No licensee shall sell or furnish beer or
wine to any habitual drunkard or to any person who shall appear to be visibly
intoxicated or who is acting in a disorderly manner.
   (C)   Possessing intoxicating beverages on-premises. No licensee shall sell,
furnish or possess at his or her licensed place of business any intoxicating
liquor of any sort or kind whatsoever, or any whiskey, beer, wine, gin or
brandy or any other alcoholic beverage of any sort or kind, except beer, wine
or other beverages as are authorized to be sold and possessed under the terms
of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code.
   (D)   Purchase from persons other than licensed wholesalers. No licensee
shall purchase or otherwise acquire beer or wine from anyone except a brewer or
a wholesaler duly licensed under the State Alcoholic Beverage Code.
   (E)   Permitting alcoholic beverages on premises. No licensee shall
knowingly permit any intoxicating liquor or any alcoholic beverage of any sort
or kind, except beer or wine authorized by the State Alcoholic Beverage Code to
be brought into or consumed upon the place of business of such licensee. No
person shall bring or in any manner introduce into the place of business of any
such licensee any such intoxicating liquor or alcoholic beverage.
   (F)   Disturbing the peace. It shall be the duty of every person licensed
under this subchapter to conduct his or her place of business in a quiet,
peaceable manner, and no such licensee shall knowingly permit any disturbance
of the peace or other improper or disorderly conduct to occur in or about the
premises operated by such licensee.
   (G)   Violation. For a violation of divisions (C) and (D) above, in addition
to any penalty as provided for in §
10.99, the offender may suffer the forfeiture of his or her city license to
dispense beer and wine. Upon a second conviction, it shall be mandatory upon
the court to order the immediate cancellation of such license, and no renewal
of the same shall be had by such offender for a period of one year thereafter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-11) (Ord. 16-82, passed 5-21-1984) Penalty, see §
112.999
Cross-reference:
   Minors, see §
112.005
§ 112.031 HOURS OF OPERATION.
   (A)   Retail sale. Places licensed under the State Alcoholic Beverage Code
and under this subchapter to sell beer and wine at retail shall be closed and
shall not sell or serve beer or wine between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 8:00
a.m. of each day.
   (B)   Hotel, restaurant or club. Places licensed under the hotel, restaurant
or club provisions of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code and this subchapter
shall not sell or serve beer or wine between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 8:00
a.m. of each day.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-12)
§ 112.032 OPERATION IN RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS.
   No license under this subchapter shall be granted to any person to sell beer
or wine at any location within a residential district of the city. The
determination of the City Council as to what constitutes a “residential
district” shall be conclusive for all applicants for license under this
subchapter. This section supplants M.C.A. § 16-3-306(1) and the prohibition set
forth thereunder.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-13) (Ord. 77-85, passed 12-15-1997) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.033 INSPECTIONS.
   Every place of business operated under authority of this subchapter and
under authority of the State Alcoholic Beverage Code shall be subject to
regulation, inspection, control and supervision under the general police powers
of the city and shall be subject to this code and all ordinances of the city
adopted in aid of such police powers and regulations.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-14)
§ 112.034 SUSPENSION; REVOCATION.
   The City Council shall have the same power and authority with respect to
licensees under the terms of this subchapter as are set forth in §
112.058.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-15)
LIQUOR
§ 112.045 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CLUB. A national fraternal organization, except college fraternities, or an
association of individuals organized for social purposes and not for profit,
with a permanent membership and in existence for two years prior to making
application for a license, with permanent quarters or rooms.
   CODE. Montana Code Annotated or State Alcoholic Beverage Code.
   INTERDICTED PERSON. A person to whom the sale of liquor is prohibited under
the laws of the state.
   LICENSE. A license issued by the city to a qualified person, under which it
shall be lawful for the licensee to sell and dispense liquor at retail as
provided in this subchapter.
   LICENSEE. The person to whom a license is issued.
   LIQUOR. All kinds of liquor sold by or in a state liquor store.
   STATE LIQUOR STORE. A liquor store established by the Department of Revenue
under the laws of the state.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-1)
§ 112.046 LICENSE REQUIRED; EXCEPTIONS.
   (A)   Required. No person shall sell at retail within the city any liquors
until such person shall have procured a license therefor as provided in this
subchapter.
   (B)   Exceptions. Nothing in this subchapter shall apply to those engaged in
the sale of liquor as follows:
      (1)   State liquor stores. At the various state liquor stores; and
      (2)   Railroad dining or buffet car. In any dining or buffet car operated
by any railroad in connection with regularly operated train service, when the
person serving such liquor is in the employ of the railroad and is acting
within the scope of his or her employment in so doing; provided, that a license
has been issued to the railroad by the Department of Revenue, and the same, or
a duplicate thereof, is displayed in such car.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-2) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.047 APPLICATION.
   Prior to the issuance of a license under this subchapter, the applicant
therefor shall file with the Finance Clerk-Treasurer an application, in
writing, signed by the applicant and directed to the City Council, which
application shall specify the location by street and number and the part of the
premises where the business is to be carried on under the license applied for;
and the names of the persons conducting the business if the same is a
partnership. If the same is a fraternal order, such fact shall be therein set
forth. The application shall be accompanied by satisfactory evidence that the
applicant has the licenses required by §
112.049. Such application shall be accompanied with the license fee as provided
in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-3)
§ 112.048 QUALIFIED APPLICANTS.
   Licenses under this subchapter may be issued to qualified applicants,
whereby the licensee shall be authorized and permitted to sell liquor at retail
in accordance with the provisions of this subchapter. Qualified applicants
shall include persons, hotels, clubs and fraternal organizations.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-4)
§ 112.049 ADDITIONAL LICENSES REQUIRED.
   No person, club, or fraternal organization shall be entitled to a license
under this subchapter unless such person, club or fraternal organization shall
have, in respect to the same premises for which a license under this subchapter
is sought, the following:
   (A)   State liquor license. A subsisting license issued by the Department of
Revenue;
   (B)   State beer and wine license. A subsisting beer and wine license,
issued under the laws of the state; and
   (C)   City beer and wine license. A subsisting beer and wine license issued
under this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-5)
§ 112.050 FEES.
   (A)   Annual fee. Each licensee under the provisions of this subchapter
shall pay an annual license fee for each license as provided by resolution.
   (B)   Disposition of funds. All receipts from license fees and fines
collected under the provisions of this subchapter shall be deposited to the
credit of the General Fund of this city.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-6)
§ 112.051 ISSUANCE.
   (A)   Issuance by Finance Clerk-Treasurer. Upon the filing of an application
under this subchapter, accompanied by the evidence required, and upon payment
of the necessary and required license fee to the Finance Clerk-Treasurer, it
shall be the duty of the Finance Clerk-Treasurer to issue and deliver to the
applicant a license to carry on the business for which the applicant owns and
holds a subsisting license in respect to the premises for which such license is
applied, as provided in §
112.049.
   (B)   Council review. The Finance Clerk-Treasurer, in his or her discretion,
may hold the application for a license so delivered to him or her until the
next regular meeting of the City Council, at which time he or she shall submit
such application to the City Council so that the City Council may, in its
discretion, decline to authorize such license, if, in the judgment of the City
Council, it will be for the best interests of the city to refuse such license.
   (C)   Denial; return of fee. Upon such refusal, the license fee paid by the
applicant and all documents filed by him or her, other than such application,
shall be returned to the applicant.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-7)
§ 112.052 LICENSE.
   (A)   Contents. Every license issued under this subchapter shall set forth
the name of the person to whom issued; the location by street and number of the
premises where the business is to be carried on under the license; and the
number of the license issued by the Department of Revenue to the applicant. If
it is a partnership, it shall set forth the names of the persons conducting the
business.
   (B)   Transferability. Such license shall be signed by the licensee and
shall be nontransferable; provided, that a transfer of any such license may be
made on application to the City Council accompanied by satisfactory evidence of
the consent of the Department of Revenue to such transfer of the license by it.
No charge shall be made in such a transfer of license for the unexpired period
for which the original license was issued.
   (C)   Posting. Such license shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the
premises in respect to which it is issued and shall be exhibited to any member
of the Police Department whenever the same is requested.
   (D)   Licenses separate and distinct as to licensee and premises. Every
license issued under the provisions of this subchapter is separate and
distinct, and no person, except the licensee therein named, shall exercise any
of the privileges granted thereunder; and all licenses are applicable only to
the premises in respect to which they are so issued.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-8)
§ 112.053 TERM OF LICENSE.
   All licenses issued in any year shall expire on December 31, at 12:00 a.m.
of such year.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-9)
§ 112.054 RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   Restricted to licensee. No business shall be carried on under any
license issued under this subchapter except in the name of the licensee.
   (B)   Operation in residential districts. No liquor license shall be issued
for any premises situated in the residential district of the city. The
determination of the City Council as to what constitutes a “residential
district,” shall be conclusive for all applicants for licenses under this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-10) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.055 HOURS OF OPERATION.
   No liquor shall be sold, offered for sale or given away upon any premises
licensed to sell liquor at retail during the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 8:00 a.m.
of each day.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-11) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.056 PROHIBITED SALES.
   No licensee under this subchapter shall sell, deliver or give away or cause
or permit to be sold, delivered or given away any liquor to the following
persons:
   (A)   Any minor under the age of 21 years;
   (B)   Any habitual drunkard;
   (C)   Any interdicted person; and
   (D)   Any intoxicated person or person actually, apparently or obviously
intoxicated.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-12) Penalty, see §
112.999
§ 112.057 INSPECTIONS.
   The City Council, or duly authorized representative thereof, or the Mayor,
Chief of Police or any member of the Police Department shall have the right at
any time to make an examination of the premises of a licensee under this
subchapter as to whether this subchapter is being compiled with.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-13)
§ 112.058 SUSPENSION; REVOCATION.
   (A)   Power to suspend or revoke. The City Council may, upon its own motion,
and shall, upon a written verified complaint of any other person, investigate
the action and operation of any licensee under this subchapter, and shall have
the power to temporarily suspend or permanently revoke a license issued under
this subchapter for violation of any provision of this subchapter.
   (B)   Complaint.
      (1)   Issuance of citation. Upon the filing with the City Council of a
verified complaint within one year prior to the date of filing the complaint,
charging the licensee with the commission of any act which would be cause for
the suspension or revocation of a license, the City Council shall forthwith
issue a citation directing the licensee to appear before the City Council
within 20 days after the date of the service of the citation, and by filing his
or her verified answer to the complaint show cause, if any, why his or her
license should not be suspended or revoked.
      (2)   Service. Service of the citation may be effected by mailing a true
copy thereof, with a true copy of the complaint, by registered mail addressed
to the licensee at his or her last address of record, or by the Chief of
Police.
      (3)   Failure to answer. Failure of the licensee to answer shall be an
admission by him or her of the truthfulness of the charge made, and, thereupon,
the City Council shall be authorized to suspend or revoke the license.
   (C)   Hearing; notice.
      (1)   Scheduled. Upon the filing of the answer, the City Council shall
fix the time and place of the hearing on the charges made, which hearing shall
be in the City Council chamber of the City Hall. Not less than five days’
notice of the hearing shall be given to the complainant and licensee.
      (2)   Notice of hearing. The notice of hearing shall be served in the
same manner as is the citation. With the notice of the hearing to the
complainant, there shall be attached a true copy of the answer of the licensee.
If either party has appeared by counsel, the notice shall be given in like
manner to the counsel of the party.
      (3)   Evidence; testimony. At the hearing, the City Council shall hear
the evidence presented which may be in the form of oral testimony or
affidavits, or both.
   (D)   Decision of Council.
      (1)   Written decision. After the hearing has been concluded, the City
Council shall, within ten days, render its decision, in writing, stating the
reasons therefor.
      (2)   Notice of decision. Notice of the decision, with a copy thereof,
shall be served upon the parties, or their counsel, in the manner provided in
this section as to other notices. When the City Council shall have revoked or
cancelled a license previously issued by it, the City Council shall notify the
licensee, in writing, by registered mail, to the address of such licensee, of
its action, giving reasons therefor.
   (E)   Appeal. Should the action of the City Council be arbitrary or
capricious, anyone aggrieved thereby shall, by mandamus or other appropriate
proceeding, be entitled to have the action of the City Council reviewed by the
district court of the state in and for the county.
   (F)   Power to renew. After suspension or revocation of a license, the City
Council shall have the power to renew the same if, in its discretion, a proper
showing therefor has been made.
   (G)   Notice to state. Any suspension or revocation by the City Council
shall be immediately reported to the State Department of Revenue with a request
that the Department of Revenue suspend or revoke the liquor license issued by
the state.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-14)
SPECIAL BEER AND TABLE WINE PERMIT
§ 112.070 SPECIAL PERMIT REQUIRED.
   Any association or corporation conducting a picnic, convention, fair, civic
community enterprise, or sporting event, in the city, shall, in the discretion
of the Finance Clerk-Treasurer be entitled to a special permit to sell beer and
table wine to the patrons of such event to be consumed within the enclosure
wherein the event is held.
(Prior Code, § 3-1C-1)
§ 112.071 APPLICATION.
   The application of any such association or corporation shall be presented
five days in advance and shall describe the location of such enclosure where
such event is to be held, the nature of the event and the period when it is
contemplated that the event will be held. The application shall be accompanied
by the amount of the permit fee.
(Prior Code, § 3-1C-2)
§ 112.072 STATE PERMIT REQUIRED.
   Upon application for said permit, the applicant shall present to the Finance
Clerk-Treasurer, proof that the applicant has received a special permit to sell
beer and table wine from the liquor division of the State Department of
Revenue, pursuant to M.C.A. § 16-4-301.
(Prior Code, § 3-1C-3)
§ 112.073 FEE.
   The fee for said permit is 100% of the fee charged by the division for a
state beer or beer and wine license. This fee shall be paid upon presentation
of the application to the Finance Clerk-Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 3-1C-4)
§ 112.074 TERM.
   The permit issued to such association or corporation is a special permit,
but shall not authorize the sale of beer and table wine, except starting one
day in advance of the regular period when events are being held upon such
grounds and during the period described in the application and for one day
thereafter.
(Prior Code, § 3-1C-5)
§ 112.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person convicted of a violation of §
112.005 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and punished according to §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-5)
   (C)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §
112.006 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be punished as provided in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 3-1-6)
   (D)   (1)   No licensee under the provisions of §§
112.020 through
112.034 shall violate any of the terms or provisions of the State Alcoholic
Beverage Code within the city. Any violation of such Code shall be unlawful and
shall constitute a violation of §§
112.020 through
112.034.
      (2)   Violations of §§
112.020 through
112.034 shall be punished as set forth in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 3-1A-16)
   (E)   Violations of §§
112.045 through
112.058 shall be punished as set forth in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 3-1B-15)
(Ord. 18-85, passed 6-15-1987; Ord. 32-85, passed 5-7-1990)
TITLE XIII: GENERAL OFFENSES
   Chapter
      
130.   GENERAL OFFENSES
CHAPTER 130: GENERAL OFFENSES
Section
   
130.01   Curfew
   
130.02   Dangerous weapons
 
   
130.99   Penalty
§ 130.01 CURFEW.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      CURFEW HOURS.
         (a)   11:00 p.m. on any Sunday, Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday or Thursday
until 6:00 a.m. of the following day; and
         (b)   12:01 a.m. until 6:00 a.m. on any Saturday or Sunday.
      EMERGENCY. An unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting
state that calls for immediate action. The term includes, but is not limited
to, a fire, natural disaster, an automobile accident or any situation requiring
immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life.
      ESTABLISHMENT. Any privately-owned place of business operated for a
profit to which the public is invited, including, but not limited to, any place
of amusement or entertainment.
      GUARDIAN.
         (a)   A person who, under court order, is the guardian of the person
of a minor; or
         (b)   A public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by
a court.
      MINOR. Any person under 18 years of age.
      OPERATOR. Any individual, firm, association, partnership or corporation
operating, managing or conducting any establishment. The term includes the
members or partners of an association or partnership and the officers of a
corporation.
      PARENT. A person who is:
         (a)   A natural parent, adoptive parent or step-parent of another
person; or
         (b)   At least 18 years of age and authorized by a parent or guardian
to have the care and custody of a minor.
      PUBLIC PLACE. Any place to which the public or a substantial group of the
public has access and includes, but not limited to, streets, highways and the
common areas of schools, hospitals, apartment houses, office buildings,
transport facilities and shops.
      REMAIN.
         (a)   Linger or stay; or
         (b)   Fail to leave premises when requested to do so by a police
office or the owner, operator or other person in control of the premises.
      SERIOUS BODILY INJURY. Bodily injury that creates a substantial risk of
death or that causes death, serious permanent disfigurement or protracted loss
or impairment of the function of any bodily member or organ.
   (B)   Offenses. 
      (1)   A minor commits an offense if they remain in any public place or on
the premises of any establishment within the city during curfew hours.
      (2)   A parent or guardian of a minor commits an offense if he or she
knowingly permits or by insufficient control allows, the minor to remain in any
public place or on the premises of any establishment within the city during
curfew hours.
      (3)   The owner, operator or any employee of an establishment commits an
offense if they knowingly allow a minor to remain upon the premises of the
establishment during curfew hours.
   (C)   Exemptions.
      (1)   It is an exemption to division (B) above that the minor was:
         (a)   Accompanied by the minor’s parent or guardian;
         (b)   On an errand at the direction of the minor's parent or guardian;
without any detour or stop;
         (c)   In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
         (d)   Engaged in an employment activity, or going to or returning home
from an employment activity, without any detour or stop;
         (e)   Involved in an emergency;
         (f)   On the sidewalk abutting the minor’s residence or abutting the
residence of a next-door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the
police department about the minor’s presence;
         (g)   Attending an official school, religious or other recreational
activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the city, a civic organization
or similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor, or going to or
returning home from, without any detour or stop, an official school, religious
or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the city,
a civic organization or other similar entity that take responsibility for the
minor;
         (h)   Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the United States
Constitution, such as free exercise of religion, freedom of speech and the
right of assembly; or
         (i)   Married or had been married or had disabilities of minority
removed in accordance with state law.
      (2)   It is a defense to prosecution under division (B)(3) above that the
owner, operator or employee of an establishment promptly notified the Police
Department that a minor was present on the premises of the establishment during
curfew hours and refused to leave.
   (D)   Enforcement. Before taking any enforcement action under this section,
a police officer shall ask the apparent offender’s age and the reason for being
in a public place. The officer shall not issue a citation or make an arrest
under this section unless the officer reasonably believes that an offense has
occurred and that, based on any response and other circumstances, including
investigation additional to the actions required by this division (D) as a
reasonable person would deem necessary, no exemption in division (C) above is
present.
(Ord. 03-2025, passed 2-18-2025) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.02 DANGEROUS WEAPONS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, other than a peace officer in the
discharge of his or her duties or a citizen in the protection of his or her
life or that of his or her family or his or her property, to discharge any
firearm, air gun, pistol, slingshot or bow and arrow within the corporate
limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 5-5-1) Penalty, see §
130.99
§ 130.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be punished
in accordance with §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 5-5-2)

CODES ADOPTED
§ 150.01 BUILDING CODES.
   The current editions of the Building Codes and all accompanying appendices,
amendments and modifications adopted by the Building Codes Bureau, State
Department of Labor and Industry (or its successor), as set out in the
administrative rules of the state, as amended from time to time by the Building
Codes Bureau, shall be adopted by reference by administrative order of the City
Council as authorized by M.C.A. § 50-60-301(1)(b), except for any exceptions
noted in this chapter or any regulations not applicable to local government
jurisdictions. These codes are applicable to all buildings within the Building
Code enforcement area of the city, including, but not limited to, commercial
buildings, residential buildings, or their attached-to structures, and any
private garage or private storage structure used only for the owner’s own use
as provided by M.C.A. § 50-60-102(1)(a).
   (A)   The adopted Building Codes shall regulate the erection, construction,
enlargement, alteration, repair, moving, removal, demolition, conversion,
occupancy, equipment, use, height, area and maintenance of all buildings and/or
structures in the city and its jurisdictional area, providing for issuance of
permits and collection of fees and penalties.
   (B)   One copy of each code shall be on file in the office of the Fire
Chief.
   (C)   Any codes or amendments adopted by the Building Codes Bureau which
apply to local government jurisdictions, including the adoption of the latest
editions of the model technical codes or applicable administrative rules of the
state, shall become effective in the city upon order of the City Council within
ten days after the date that they are approved by a resolution at a City
Council meeting.
   (D)   City amendments thereto are as follows.
      (1)   Schedule of permit fees. Schedule of permit fees for use by the
city will be established by resolution.
      (2)   Appeals. In order to hear and decide appeals of orders, decisions
or determinations made by the Building Official relative to the application and
interpretation of this code, there shall be and is hereby created a Board of
Adjustment. The Board of Adjustment proceedings will be in accordance with §§
155.295 through
155.308.
      (3)   Debris. The city requires that all buildings that have been
removed, demolished or destroyed must have all the debris removed, including
the basements and/or foundations.
(Prior Code, § 9-1-1) (Ord. 03-2004, passed 6-15-2004; Ord. 02-2023, passed 12-
5-2023)
§ 150.02 NATIONAL ELECTRICAL CODE ADOPTED.
   There is hereby adopted for the purpose of prescribing regulations governing
electrical work, that certain code known as the National Electrical Code, being
particularly the code that is currently adopted by the state’s electrical
inspector, and the pertinent parts thereof are hereby adopted and incorporated
herein as fully as if set out at length, and from the date of which this
chapter shall take effect, the provisions thereof shall be controlling within
the limits of the city.
(Prior Code, § 9-2-1)
PLUMBING
§ 150.15 APPLICABILITY.
   This subchapter shall not apply to or affect plumbing or pipe fitting in any
railroad or oil industry.
(Prior Code, § 9-3-1)
§ 150.16 PLUMBER’S LICENSE REQUIRED.
   Any person working at the business of plumbing in the city as a master
plumber who, while working at the business of plumbing, shall connect plumbing
to or disconnect plumbing from a water or sewer system of the city, shall first
secure a master plumber’s license from the state.
(Prior Code, § 9-3-2) (Ord. 11-85, passed 4-21-1986)
§ 150.17 COMPLIANCE TO STATE CODES.
   All plumbing in residential and nonresidential buildings shall conform to
all current State Plumbing Codes and regulations.
(Prior Code, § 9-3-3)
§ 150.18 CONNECTION REQUIRED.
   All buildings in which there is human occupancy or employment located within
100 feet of a public sewer shall be connected to such public sewer.
(Prior Code, § 9-3-4)
TRAILERS AND TRAILER COURTS
§ 150.30 COMPLIANCE WITH STATUTE.
   Tourist campgrounds and trailer courts shall comply with M.C.A. §§ 50-52-101
through 50-52-303 and 70-24-311.
(Prior Code, § 9-4-1)
§ 150.31 PLUMBING.
   All plumbing in each trailer court shall comply with city and state plumbing
laws and regulations.
(Prior Code, § 9-4-2)
§ 150.32 ELECTRICITY.
   An electrical outlet supplying at least 110 volts shall be provided for each
trailer coach space. Such installation shall be in compliance with all city and
state electrical codes and resolutions. Such electrical outlets shall be
weatherproof. No power line shall be permitted to lie on the ground or to be
suspended less than ten feet above the ground.
(Prior Code, § 9-4-3) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.33 OCCUPIED TRAILERS.
   No person shall permit, maintain or allow an occupied trailer coach to be
parked, located or stationed within the city except in a duly authorized
trailer court.
(Prior Code, § 9-4-4) Penalty, see §
150.99
SWIMMING POOLS
§ 150.45 APPLICABILITY; COMPLIANCE.
   No person shall erect, construct, enlarge, alter, repair, improve, convert,
equip, use or maintain any private swimming pool in the city, or cause or
permit the same to be done, contrary to or in violation of any of the
provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-1) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.46 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   No private swimming pool shall be erected, constructed, altered or
maintained, except as provided by this subchapter, without first having
obtained a permit for the same as issued by the building inspector.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-2)
§ 150.47 APPLICATION.
   An application for a permit for a private swimming pool shall be made, in
writing, to the building inspector. The application shall contain the location,
by street and number, of the proposed swimming pool, the name and address of
the owner together with a description of the proposed swimming pool.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-3)
§ 150.48 CONNECTION REQUIRED.
   All private swimming pools shall be connected with the city sanitary sewer
system for the purpose of draining.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-4)
§ 150.49 FENCES.
   All private swimming pools shall be fenced by a suitable fence of not less
than six feet in height with a gate thereto of the same height. Such gate shall
be provided with a self-closing, self-locking catch or lock and placed at a
height sufficient to keep small children from opening the gate. The fence shall
be of such material as to render it difficult for small children to scale or
climb the same.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-5)
§ 150.50 NUISANCE PROHIBITED.
   No private swimming pool shall be permitted to become a private or public
nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-6) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.51 BOARD OF ADJUSTMENTS.
   In order to provide reasonable interpretation of the provisions of this
subchapter, there is hereby established a Board of Adjustments.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-7)
§ 150.52 ENFORCEMENT.
   The building inspector shall enforce all the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 9-5-8)
§ 150.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of the codes
adopted in this chapter, or fail to comply therewith, or who shall violate or
fail to comply with any order made there under, or who shall build in violation
of any detailed statement of specifications or plans submitted and approved
there under, or any certificate or permit issued there under, and from which no
appeal has been taken, or who shall fail to comply with such an order as
affirmed or modified by the City Council or by a court of competent
jurisdiction, within the time fixed herein, shall severally for each and every
such violation and noncompliance respectively, be guilty of a misdemeanor,
punishable by a fine of not less than $100 nor more than $500 or by
imprisonment for not less than three days nor more than 180 days or by both
such fine and imprisonment. The imposition of one penalty for any violation
shall not excuse the violation or permit it to continue; and all of such
persons shall be required to correct or remedy such violations or defects
within a reasonable time; and when not otherwise specified, each ten days that
prohibited conditions are maintained shall constitute a separate offense. The
application of the penalty shall not be held to prevent the enforced removal of
the prohibited conditions.
(Prior Code, § 9-1-1) (Ord. 03-2004, passed 6-15-2004; Ord. 02-2023, passed 12-
5-2023)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 151.001 DEPOSITING MATERIALS ON PUBLIC WAYS.
   (A)   Permit required. Any person, firm, association or corporation,
desiring to place, dump, push upon or deposit any material, including ice and
snow, upon any street, avenue or alley within the corporate limits of the city,
must first file an application with the City Engineer and obtain a written
permit.
(Prior Code, § 8-8-1)
   (B)   Excluded material. This section is to be so construed that the
material herein referred to does not include any of the material set forth and
included in Chapter 50, more commonly referred to as the garbage ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 8-8-2)
SIDEWALKS AND CURB
§ 151.015 CONSTRUCTION SUPERVISION.
   The construction of concrete driveways and concrete crosswalks used for
private purposes, constructed, reconstructed or laid within the street rights-
of-way of the city shall be under the supervision and direction of the Director
of Public Works, authorized assistant or duly appointed inspector. The design
and concrete mixture shall conform to standard specifications for concrete
sidewalks and driveways on file in the Director of Public Works office of the
city.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-1) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.016 CONCRETE SPECIFICATIONS.
   All sidewalks laid, constructed or reconstructed on any street shall be
uniformly constructed of concrete four inches thick, poured in place, and such
concrete and construction shall conform to specifications set forth in the most
current edition of Montana Public Works Standard Specifications for concrete
sidewalks and structural concrete.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-2) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.017 LOCATIONS AND DIMENSIONS OF SIDEWALKS.
   All sidewalks constructed, reconstructed or laid within the city shall be
located and be of the following dimensions.
   (A)   Twelve feet wide (green). Sidewalks abutting or adjacent to those lots
or parcels of land, the outside lot lines of which are colored green on the map
thereof on file in the Office of Public Works, reference to which is hereby
made and by this reference is made a part hereof, are to be 12 feet in width
and are to be located immediately adjacent to the inside line of the curb.
   (B)   Ten feet wide.
      (1)   Brown. Sidewalks abutting or adjacent to those lots or parcels of
land, the outside lot lines of which are colored brown on such map are to be
ten feet in width and are to be located immediately adjacent to the inside of
the curb.
      (2)   Purple. Sidewalks abutting or adjacent to those lots or parcels of
land, the outside lot lines of which are colored purple on such map are to be
ten feet in width and are to be located immediately adjacent to the inside line
of the curb.
   (C)   Five feet wide.
      (1)   Red. Sidewalks abutting those lots or parcels of land, the outside
lot lines of which are colored red on such map are to be five feet in width and
are to be located so that the inside line of such sidewalk shall be one foot
out from the adjacent property line.
      (2)   Blue. Sidewalks abutting or adjacent to those lots or parcels of
land, the outside lot lines of which are colored in blue on such map are to be
five feet in width and are to be located immediately adjacent to the inside
lines of the curb.
   (D)   Grade. All sidewalks shall rise one-fourth inch to the foot from the
curb grade to the property line.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-3) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.018 EXISTING SIDEWALK LOCATION.
   If more than one-half of the block of the sidewalk is in place and built to
acceptable grades and in serviceable condition, then the remaining sidewalks in
the same block shall conform to the location of the sidewalks already
installed. If less than one-half of the existing sidewalk is in place, the
location of the walk will be determined by §
151.017. Areas not designated in this section will be determined by considering
good design principles, wishes of the affected property owners, the costs
involved and other existing conflicts such as trees, shrubs, light fixtures,
fire hydrants and other utilities.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-4) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.019 REPAIR TO SIDEWALKS.
   It shall be the duty of the owners and tenants of any premises within the
city limits to keep the sidewalk in front of and adjoining their premises in
good, safe and substantial condition, and the owners shall see that all breaks
or unsoundness of any character resulting from natural deterioration, or from
any cause whatsoever, is repaired with all dispatch. All the repairing of
sidewalks laid and constructed shall be the responsibility of the abutting
property owner.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-5) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.020 LOCATION OF CURBING.
   The outside of the curbing which is the side nearest the center of the
street shall be at the distance as shown on the official street plats on file
in the office of the Director of Public Works.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-6) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.021 CURB SPECIFICATIONS.
   All curbs shall be so constructed as to conform with Montana Public Works
Standard Specifications, most current edition. When curbs are replaced or built
anew, provisions must be made for handicap accessible ramps at all
intersections. All curbs replaced or installed as new construction shall be of
integral curb and gutter.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-7) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.022 RESPONSIBILITY OF ABUTTING PROPERTY OWNERS.
   (A)   Whenever any street or avenue in the city shall be ordered improved by
the City Council by the construction, repair or removal of sidewalks or curbs,
or the removal of any obstruction, along either or both sides thereof, the
duties, burden or expense of constructing, maintaining, repairing or removing
of such curb or sidewalk, or the removal of any obstruction, shall devolve upon
and be paid for by the owner of the property directly abutting on that side of
such street or avenue along which such sidewalk or curb has been ordered
constructed, repaired or removed, or the obstruction removed therefrom.
   (B)   Such a construction, repair or removal of a sidewalk or curb, or the
removal of an obstruction therefrom, shall require a written notice thereof
shall be given by the Director of Public Works to the owners or agent of the
owners of the lots or parcels of land along which such sidewalks or curb may be
ordered built or repaired or removed or the obstruction removed therefrom;
which notice shall specify the nature of the work to be done and the time
within which the same shall be commenced, that if the work is not commenced by
the owner of the property within 30 days after the date of service of such
notice to cause such work to be done, that the owner of such property and the
property itself shall be liable for the cost and assessment of the same and
that if such work will be done by the city, and under its authority and
supervision, and the costs thereof assessed against such property and the owner
thereof.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-8) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.023 FAILURE TO COMPLY.
   If the owner of any lot or parcel of land fronting or abutting where any
curb or sidewalk shall have been ordered constructed, repaired or removed or
obstruction removed therefrom shall refuse, fail or neglect to have the work
specified done or commenced within 30 days, as notified, the city shall procure
the same to be done either by a contractor or by its duly authorized officers.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-9) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.024 PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTOR TO RECORD COSTS.
   Whenever any curb or sidewalk shall have been constructed, repaired or
removed, or any obstruction removed therefrom by the city as provided by this
subchapter, the Director of Public Works shall keep an account of all costs or
expenses incurred in his or her office in connection with any work under any
such order or notice, which shall include the costs of preparation of plats,
plans, specifications, maps, engineering, superintendence and inspection and
preparation of any assessment rolls, and cost of the work performed, and the
Director of Public Works shall certify all such costs to the Administrative
Clerk, whose duty it shall be to prepare all necessary schedules and
resolutions levying any taxes or assessments against the property abutting any
curb or sidewalk which has been constructed, repaired or removed, or has had an
obstruction removed therefrom.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-10) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.025 SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS.
   The Administrative Clerk shall certify to the City Council the costs of any
improvements or work required by this subchapter, and the City Council shall
thereupon proceed by resolution to assess a special tax or assessment upon each
lot or parcel of land for such sum of money as may be required for the purpose
of paying the costs of such improvements, and such resolution shall contain a
list of the assessment and apportionment, which shall, as nearly as
practicable, contain a correct description of the real property on which such
tax or assessment is assessed or apportioned, with the name of the person
owning the same, if known, and the amount of such special tax as assessed or
apportioned against such property.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-11) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.026 NOTICE OF MEETING REGARDING SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS.
   (A)   Hearing scheduled. The resolution referred to in §
151.025 shall fix the time and place at which the City Council will hear and
consider objections to such assessment or apportionment.
   (B)   Publication of notice. Notice of the time and place of the meeting of
the City Council for the purpose of hearing objections to such resolution
making the assessment for the purpose of paying such construction, repair or
removal of such curb or obstructions as provided for in this subchapter shall
be given by the Administrative Clerk by one publication in a newspaper, which
notice shall be published at least five days preceding the date upon which the
City Council will hear and consider such objections.
   (C)   Hearing. At the meeting referred to in this section the parties
interested may appear in person or by their agents or attorneys. The City
Council shall consider all objections that may be made to the assessment or
apportionment and shall make such provisions, amendments and changes therein as
shall seem to them right and equitable and may adjourn from time to time until
all objections shall have been considered. When such resolution shall have been
finally amended and adopted, the City Council shall levy such special tax as
therein assessed and apportioned.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-12) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.027 LIEN FOR SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS.
   All special taxes for the construction of curbs or sidewalks shall be a lien
upon the real estate upon which the same are assessed or apportioned from the
date of such assessment or apportionment until the same are paid or such real
estate shall have been sold therefor as provided by law.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-13) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.028 PAY PERIOD, INTEREST.
   The payment of costs of construction, repair or removal of such curbs or
sidewalks or obstructions therefrom may be spread over a term of years not to
exceed 12 years, payments to be made in equal annual installments. Each
installment shall be payable on or before January 1 of each year, and all
deferred payments shall bear interest at a rate pursuant to M.C.A. § 17-5-102
per annum from the date of the passing of the resolution referred to in this
subchapter until the final payment of the last installment.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-14) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.029 COSTS TO BE EXTENDED UPON TAX ROLLS.
   (A)   Certification. Within three days after the resolution levying and
assessing the special tax or assessment for the costs of construction, repair
or removal of any curb or sidewalk or obstruction therefrom shall have been
adopted and approved, the resolution shall be certified by the Administrative
Clerk.
   (B)   Extended to tax rolls. If such resolution shall be certified to the
Administrative Clerk so that the same may be certified to the proper officers
of the county, to extend upon the tax rolls, with other city taxes, for the
current year, then, and in that event, the Administrative Clerk shall certify
such tax or assessment to the proper officer of the county.
   (C)   Unable to extend for current year. If such resolution is adopted and
approved at a time when it cannot be certified so as to be extended upon the
tax rolls for the current year, it shall be the duty of the Administrative
Clerk to mail a notice to each owner, containing a description of their
property and the amount of the assessment, which may be contained in such
special assessment roll for the construction, repair or removal of such curb or
sidewalk, and the further fact that the taxes to be due and payable at the
office of the Administrative Clerk within a period of 30 days, specifying the
date upon which such special tax or assessment will be due, which date shall
not be less than 30 days nor more than 45 days from the date of such notice.
   (D)   Deferred payments. It shall be the duty of the Administrative Clerk
each year after the time referred to in this section to certify at the proper
time, to the proper officers of the county, the amount of the annual differed
payment due at the coming tax paying time so that it may be extended upon the
tax rolls of the county with other city taxes and collected by the County
Treasurer at the time that other city taxes or assessments are collected by the
County Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-15) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.030 SPECIAL FUND CREATED.
   There is hereby authorized and created a fund to be known as the Special
Sidewalk and Curb Fund in which shall be placed any money collected from any
owner of property for any taxes or assessments levied for the purpose of
constructing, repairing or removing any curbs or sidewalks or obstructions
therefrom.
(Prior Code, § 8-1-16) (Ord. 01-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
CONSTRUCTION OF CURB CUTS AND DRIVEWAYS
§ 151.045 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ALLEY. A narrow public thoroughfare providing access to the rear of the
abutting property.
   ALLEY APPROACH. A curb cut and driveway apron at each end of the alley
intended to benefit all property in the entire block.
   CURB CUT. The portion of the street curbing that is removed excluding curb
return to provide ingress or egress from abutting property.
   CURB OPENING. The total street curbing that is removed to place a curb cut
and slopes.
   CURB RETURN. The curved portion of a street curb at drive approaches.
   DRIVEWAY. The area on private property which solely serves a building, such
as a house or garage, where vehicles are operated, parked or allowed to stand.
   DRIVEWAY APRON. The area, construction or improvement between the curb
opening or proposed curb line and the back edge of walk or proposed walk.
   INTERSECTION. The area embraced within the prolongation or connection of the
lateral curb lines or, if not, then the lateral boundary lines of the roadways
which join each other at, or approximately at right angles, or the area within
which vehicles traveling upon different roadways joining at any other angle may
come into conflict.
   PERSON. Every natural person, firm, copartnership, association or
corporation.
   RIGHT-OF-WAY. Public property dedicated for streets, alleys or other public
uses.
   ROADWAY. The portion of a street improved, designed and customarily used for
vehicular travel, exclusive of the shoulder.
   SIDEWALK. The portion of a street between curb lines or the outer lateral
lines of roadway and the adjacent property lines, intended for use by
pedestrians.
   STREET. The entire width between the boundary lines of the right-of-way
publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for
purposes of vehicular travel.
   TRAFFIC. Pedestrians, vehicles and other conveyances, either singly or
together, while using any street, alley or roadway for purposes of travel.
(Prior Code, § 8-2-1) (Ord. 02-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.046 PERMIT REQUIRED; INSPECTION.
   It shall be unlawful for any person either as owner, agent contractor or
employee to cut, break, remove or alter any curbing, driveway apron or sidewalk
or cause to have cut, broken or removed any curbing, driveway apron or
sidewalk, or to install or cause to have installed any driveway on any public
right-of-way in the city without a permit. The city shall provide an inspection
for alignment, grade and materials and to see that work is done in accordance
with the specifications of the city. The city shall be notified at least 24
hours in advance of the time the work is proposed to be started.
(Prior Code, § 8-2-2) (Ord. 02-2001, passed 3-20-2001) Penalty, see §
151.999
§ 151.047 ALLOWABLE CURB CUT LENGTHS.
   (A)   Single-family residential districts. In single-family residential
districts (R-1, R-2), the maximum curb cut length shall be 24 feet.
   (B)   Multi-family residential districts. In multi-family residential
districts (R-3, R-4), the maximum curb cut length shall not exceed 30 feet.
   (C)   Commercial and industrial districts. In all commercial and industrial
districts, the maximum curb cut length shall not exceed 40 feet.
   (D)   Minimum distance between curb cuts. The minimum distance between all
curb cuts in all districts shall be not less than 30 feet.
   (E)   Frontage. Frontage of 60 feet or less shall be limited to one curb cut
with not more than two curb cuts to be provided to any single tract or business
establishment, except where the property frontage exceeds 250 feet.
(Prior Code, § 8-2-3) (Ord. 02-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
§ 151.048 REGULATIONS GENERALLY.
   Every curb cut and driveway apron constructed or altered in the street
right-of-way shall conform to the following regulations.
   (A)   Location. Driveways shall be so located at the discretion and by the
approval of the Director of Public Works as to result in no undue interference
with or hazard to the free movement of normal traffic or interfere with the
placement and proper functioning of highway signs, signals, lighting or other
devices that affect traffic operation. Any necessary adjustments to utility
facilities, light standards, fire hydrants, catch basins, street signs,
signals, underground conduits for street lighting or other public improvements
or installations shall be done without cost to the city.
   (B)   Construction. All driveways shall be so constructed so as not to
impair drainage within the street or highway right-of-way nor alter the
stability of the roadway subgrade and at the same time not impair or materially
alter drainage of the adjacent areas. All drainage structures required within
the public right-of-way and under the driveways as a result of the property
being developed shall be installed in accordance with the standards of the
Director of Public Works.
   (C)   Transition from street to driveway. All driveways shall have the back
of curb dropped a minimum of four and one-half inches for the width of the
driveway. The minimum driveway transition distance shall be from the back of
the curb to the property line and shall occur in a uniform manner. Curb fillets
constructed by filling in the curb and gutter are prohibited as a means of
transition from the street to the driveway.
   (D)   Distance between two adjacent driveways. The distance between two
adjacent driveways to the same frontage shall be not less than 30 feet.
   (E)   Corner clearance. At an intersecting street or highway, the dimension
measured along the edge of the traveled way to provide adequate corner
clearance shall be measured a minimum distance of ten feet from the
intersection property line, except at intersections where there are traffic
signals, the nearside clearance shall be two or more times this distance.
   (F)   Curb openings. No curb opening shall be made between the points of
curvature of any curvature at intersections, or between the points of curvature
of any curb return of short radius, if deemed hazardous by the city.
   (G)   Commercial and industrial off-site parking lots. In all commercial and
industrial off-site parking lots, the designs shall be such that vehicles
egressing shall not be required to back out into a roadway or driving lane.
   (H)   Curb cuts and driveway aprons. All curb cuts and driveway aprons are
to be constructed of Portland cement concrete of a quality and type as
specified by the Director of Public Works, and in accordance with city
specifications in effect at the time of such work. Curb cuts shall be permitted
only with construction of adjoining Portland cement concrete aprons having a
minimum depth of five feet.
   (I)   Driveway approach.
      (1)   Construction across sidewalk. No driveway approach shall be
constructed across any sidewalk unless such sidewalk is constructed or
reconstructed in accordance with specifications pertaining to the construction
of sidewalks to be used as driveway approaches.
      (2)   Interference with gutter flow line or sidewalk grade. No driveway
approach shall be constructed in a manner so as to change or interfere with the
gutter flow line or sidewalk grade where such driveway approach crosses any
such gutter or sidewalk.
   (J)   No existing sidewalk. Where no sidewalk exists, the portion of the
driveway approach adjacent to the property line shall be constructed as though
a sidewalk did exist.
   (K)   City street rights-of-way. City street rights-of-way may not be used
for private or commercial purposes. A permit for the construction of a curb cut
driveway shall not be issued unless vehicles which will use said driveway can
be parked entirely within the private property lines.
   (L)   Abandoned or unused curb cut or driveway apron. Any curb cut or
driveway apron which has become abandoned or unused through a change of the
conditions for which it was originally intended shall be closed and the owner
shall replace any curb cut and/or driveway apron with a standard curb and
sidewalk to be constructed according to the city’s specifications in effect at
the time of such work. This division (L) shall be applicable to any existing
driveway, the use of which is presently discontinued. Upon the failure or
refusal of the owner to restore the sidewalk and curbing as provided in this
section, the City Council may order the restoration of the sidewalk and curbing
and the cost of such replacement be at the expense of the owner.
   (M)   Joints. The sidewalk and curb shall, insofar as possible, be cut and
removed at the nearest joint. Upon replacement and reconstruction of a sidewalk
as a driveway approach, the construction of the curb return and any pavement in
connection with a driveway approach, suitable joints shall be provided and all
such spaces shall be filled with a bituminous fibrous compound in accordance
with the specifications of the city. When it is not possible to cut and remove
at an existing joint, such cutting shall be performed by using a concrete saw.
   (N)   Interference with intersecting sidewalks, utility facilities. No curb
cut shall be closer than five feet to, nor shall it be so located as to
interfere with intersecting sidewalks, utility facilities, light standards,
fire hydrants, catch basin, street signs, signals or other public improvements
or installations.
(Prior Code, § 8-2-4) (Ord. 02-2001, passed 3-20-2001) Penalty, see §
151.999
§ 151.049 RESTRICTIONS.
   In addition to the general regulations prescribed in §
151.048, curb cuts and driveway aprons to be constructed or altered in all
zoning districts must conform to the following.
   (A)   Property abutting more than one city street and/or alley. Where a
property abuts more than one city street and/or alley, the maximum curb cut
permitted on each street and/or alley shall be considered separately and shall
be governed by the frontage of the property on that street and/or alley only.
   (B)   Property 60 feet wide or less. Where a property width is 60 feet or
less, joint curb cut with an adjoining property of 60 feet or less may be
constructed at a maximum width of 30 feet. Both property owners must be in
agreement to a joint curb cut.
   (C)   Encroachment on adjacent property. To prevent encroachment on adjacent
property, the entire driveway approach, including the flared portions for
turning purposes, must be constructed on the petitioner’s property frontage
extended. Exceptions may be allowed by written consent of any adjacent affected
property owners. Extension of property frontage is to be determined by
projecting lines at right angles from the street centerline to the intersection
of the abutting property lines with the street right-of-way.
(Prior Code, § 8-2-5) (Ord. 02-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
SIDEWALK REQUIREMENTS
§ 151.060 AWNINGS.
   (A)   Required height. All awnings hung so as to project over any part of
sidewalks or other walks or roads used for travel by pedestrians shall be at
least eight feet above any such sidewalk, walk or road, in the clear.
   (B)   Declared nuisance. Every awning hung at a lower level than that
prescribed in division (A) above shall be considered an obstruction to traffic
and be declared a nuisance, and such awnings shall be removed immediately.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-1)
§ 151.061 DUTY OF OCCUPANT.
   (A)   Duty to keep clear. It shall be the duty of the occupant of any
premises within the city, or in the case the same are unoccupied, then of the
owner or his or her agent, to keep the sidewalks in front of and adjoining his
or her premises clean and safe for pedestrians and to repair the same from time
to time. Such occupant, owner or agent shall, with all responsible dispatch,
remove snow, ice, slush, mud or other impediment to safe and convenient foot
travel and prevent the accumulation of the same.
   (B)   Failure to comply. Every person failing to comply with the provisions
of this section shall be deemed guilty of committing a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-2) Penalty, see §
151.999
§ 151.062 OBSTRUCTIONS.
   The streets, avenues, alleys and sidewalks in the city shall be kept free
and clear of all obstructions, encumbrances or encroachments upon their use by
the public and shall not be used and occupied in any other way than is provided
in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-3)
§ 151.063 LITTERING.
   (A)   Prohibited. No person shall throw or deposit empty boxes of any kind
whatsoever, straw, dirt, filth, chips, shavings, paper, cans, bottles or other
rubbish on any sidewalk or in any street, alley, avenue or any public place.
   (B)   Exception. No person shall spill, drop, place or leave any gravel,
sand, dirt, coal, oil or grease whatsoever on any pavement or sidewalk within
the city except when necessary for safe movement of traffic and pedestrians and
when necessary and routine maintenance is being performed.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-4) Penalty, see §
151.999
§ 151.064 BUILDING MATERIALS.
   No person shall encumber or obstruct or cause to be encumbered or
obstructed, any street, avenue, alley or public place in the city by placing
therein or thereon any building material or any articles or things whatsoever
without first having obtained written permission from the Public Works
Director.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-5) Penalty, see §
151.999
§ 151.065 ADVERTISEMENTS.
   No person shall paste, paint or otherwise affix any sign or advertisement on
any sidewalk or pavement within the city.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-6) Penalty, see §
151.999
§ 151.066 RESTRICTIONS ON SUBWAY.
   (A)   Designated foot thoroughfare. The subway built and constructed under
the tracks of the Northern Pacific Railway Company and extending in an easterly
direction thereunder from the intersection of the easterly line of Merrill
Avenue and Power Street to the intersection of the westerly line of Anderson
Avenue and Power Street is hereby designated as a foot thoroughfare only.
   (B)   Animals, vehicles prohibited. The leading, driving, riding, moving or
conveying of any animal, bicycle or any vehicle propelled by steam, motor or
gas power through such subway is prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-7) Penalty, see §
151.999
§ 151.067 CLEARANCE ABOVE SIDEWALKS AND STREETS.
   (A)   Electrical cords or conduits. It shall be unlawful for any person,
firm or corporation to place or maintain an electrical cord or conduit over a
public sidewalk or walkway used for travel by pedestrians unless such cord or
conduit is placed a minimum of seven feet above the surface of such sidewalk or
walkway.
   (B)   Trees, bushes or shrubs. All trees, bushes or shrubs or any part
thereof that project beyond the established or proposed curb line and over
public sidewalks or walkways shall be maintained to allow an unobstructed
height of seven feet as measured from the surface of the adjacent sidewalk,
walkway or top of curb.
(Prior Code, § 8-3-8) Penalty, see §
151.999
TRENCH BACKFILL AND STREET RESTORATION
§ 151.080 DEFINITIONS; REFERENCES; STANDARD DRAWINGS.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this subchapter, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      AASHTO. American Association of State Highway and Transportation
Officials.
      ALTERNATE METHODS. Any one of the methods designated as alternate are
acceptable and can be used at the contractor’s option.
      IMPROVED AREAS. The areas that lie within the area from the centerline of
a road or street to the back of the sidewalk lines (either existing or
proposed, within two years) and any area lying within the right-of-way of an
alley (either existing or proposed, within two years).
      MUTCD. Manual of Uniform Traffic Control Devices.
      TRENCH EXCAVATIONS. The method of construction generally employing the
open cut method of placing underground utilities and not including boring,
jacking or other recognized construction methods that do not disturb the
surface or require backfilling.
   (B)   References.
      AASHTO T11 (ASTM C117). Materials finer than 75 millimeters (No. 200)
sieve in mineral aggregates by washing.
      AASHTO T27 (ASTM C136). Sieve analysis of fine and coarse aggregate.
      AASHTO T89. Determining the liquid limit of soils.
      AASHTO T90. Determining the plastic limit and plasticity index of soils.
      AASHTO T99. Moisture-density relations of soils and soil aggregate
