mixtures using five-pound (2.5 kg) rammer and 12-inch (305 mm) drop.
      AASHTO T191 (ASTM D1556). Density of soil in-place by the sand-cone
method.
      AASHTO T238 (ASTM D2922). Density of soil and soil aggregate in place by
nuclear methods (shallow depth).
      AASHTO T239 (ASTM D3017). Moisture content of soil and soil aggregate in
place by nuclear methods (shallow depth).
      ASTM D698. Moisture-density relations of soils and soil aggregate
mixtures using five-pound (2.5 kg) rammer and 12-inch (305 mm) drop.
      ASTM D4318. Test method for liquid limit, plastic and plasticity index of
soils.
   (C)   Standard drawings. Standard drawings applicable to this subchapter are
as follows:
      (1)   Standard Drawing No. 02221-1. Typical utility trench detail; and
      (2)   Standard Drawing No. 02221-2. Pipe bedding alternate.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-1) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.081 PERMIT REQUIRED; FEE.
   (A)   Permit required. No person, association or corporation, except public
utilities, shall excavate any material from any street, avenue or alley in the
city without first securing a permit from the Public Works Department.
   (B)   Deposit. At the time of applying for said permit, the person applying
shall make a deposit in the amount set by resolution with said Public Works
Department for the purpose of surface restoration.
   (C)   Responsibility for backfilling and restoration. All persons,
associations or corporations making excavations in any street, avenue or alley
shall be responsible for refilling and compacting in accordance with
specifications set forth in this subchapter and shall be responsible for
surface restoration within 14 days from the date of making said excavation.
   (D)   Failure to restore. If said restoration is not made within said time,
the city shall cause said street to be resurfaced and shall retain said trench
deposit to resurface said street. The party making excavation is responsible
for all costs incurred in the resurfacing.
   (E)   Refund of deposit; additional costs. In the event the contractor
satisfactorily makes surface restoration, his or her deposit will be refunded.
In all events, any excess money deposited over the cost of resurfacing said
excavations shall be refunded to the party making said deposit, and any
additional charges incurred in surface restoration will also be billed to the
party making said deposit.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-2) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.082 PIPE BEDDING MATERIALS.
   (A)   Type 1 pipe bedding. Type 1 pipe bedding includes the material placed
from four inches (100 mm) below the bottom of the pipe, around the pipe and up
to the springline of the pipe. Provide Type 1 bedding consisting of sand, sandy
gravel or fine gravel having a maximum three-fourths inch size (19 mm) and a
maximum plasticity index of six, determined by AASHTO T89 and T90 or by ASTM
D4318. Where trench excavation encounters wet or unstable material, Type 1
bedding must be free draining and nonplastic. Refer to Standard Drawing 02221-
1.
   (B)   Select Type 1 bedding. Select Type 1 bedding includes the material
placed from the spring line of the pipe to six inches (15 cm) over the pipe.
Select Type 1 bedding shall consist of soil, sand or fine gravel, free from
clods, lumps or frozen material, or rock exceeding one and one-half inches (38
mm) in its greatest dimension. Excavated trench material may be screened or
sorted for use as backfill subject to approval of the Public Works Department.
Where trench excavation encounters wet or unstable material, select Type 1
bedding must be free draining and nonplastic.
   (C)   Pipe bedding alternative. Pipe bedding alternative material is
described on Standard Drawing 02221-2 and is applicable only if specified.
   (D)   Type 2 pipe bedding. Type 2 pipe bedding is used as directed by the
Public Works Department to replace unsuitable material encountered in the
trench bottom. Place Type 2 pipe bedding from the bottom of the Type 1 bedding
material to the depth required to adequately support the pipe. The Type 2
bedding consists of granular material meeting the following gradation.
 
Sieve Opening % Passing
3-inch        100
No. 4         0-25
No. 8         0-10
 
(Prior Code, § 8-4-3) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.083 TRENCH BACKFILL MATERIALS.
   Backfill material obtained from trench excavations must be free of cinders,
ash, refuse, organic or frozen material, boulders or other deleterious
materials. Backfill materials and placement are further described in this
section.
   (A)   Imported backfill material. Imported backfill material is from borrow
sources outside the area and is used when, in the opinion of the Public Works
Department, an adequate volume of suitable backfill material is not available.
Imported backfill materials must comply with the requirements above for
backfill material.
   (B)   Flowable fill. Flowable fill may be required for certain areas or
trenches that do not allow for sufficient compaction. Flowable fill will be
required in all rights-of-way controlled by the State Department of
Transportation. Specifications for flowable fill shall be specified by the
State Department of Transportation in Guidelines For Utility Occupancy On
Highway Right-of-Way and the standard trench replacement section for roadway
cuts.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-4) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.084 PROTECTION OF EXISTING UTILITIES.
   (A)   Protection required. Precautions shall be taken to protect all
adjoining private and public property and facilities, including underground and
overhead utilities, curbs, sidewalks, driveways, structures and fences. It
shall be the responsibility of the contractor to replace all disturbed or
damaged facilities to their original condition.
   (B)   State one call system. The contractor shall contact utility owners
using the state’s one call system as required by state law for utility locates
before starting work.
   (C)   Responsibility for protection. It shall be the responsibility of the
contractor to protect the utilities exposed during the work and prevent
damaging underground utilities adjacent to excavations and immediately notify
the utility owner of any construction damage.
   (D)   Cost of repairs or damage. The cost of repairs or damage to marked
utilities are at the expense of the contractor. Failure to locate such
utilities or property or failure to show on the plans shall not relieve the
contractor’s liability for all damage to existing utilities at his or her own
expense.
   (E)   Locations not shown or incorrect. Any delay or extra cost to the
contractor caused by pipe lines or other underground structures or obstructions
not shown on the plans or found in locations different from those indicated
shall not constitute a claim for extra work or additional payment of damages.
   (F)   Disruption of service. Adequate provisions shall be made for
maintaining the flow of sewers, drains and watercourses encountered during
construction. Structures which may have been disturbed shall be satisfactorily
restored upon completion of the work.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-5) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.085 PRIVATELY OWNED UTILITIES.
   If any existing private utility interferes with the work in either alignment
or grade and has to be moved, the work will be performed by the appropriate
utility owner unless otherwise specified. Such private utilities may include
gas mains, underground electrical and telephone cables, telephone poles, light
poles and the like. If, however, such private utility relocation is done by the
contractor, an adjustment in payment will be made at a price agreed upon, in
writing, before the work is started if it is determined to be a change from the
original contract work scope. Extreme caution shall be exercised to avoid
conflict, contact or damage to overhead utilities during the work.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-6) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.086 PAVEMENT REMOVAL AND STRIPPING.
   (A)   Cutting.
      (1)   Where trench excavation or appurtenant structure excavation
requires removing curb and gutter, concrete sidewalks, asphalt concrete
pavement or Portland cement concrete pavement, cut the concrete or pavement in
a straight line parallel to the excavation’s edge using a spade bitted air
hammer, concrete saw or other suitable equipment to produce a straight, square
and clean break. Recut edges broken during construction before concrete or
paving operations.
      (2)   For trenches passing through existing pavement, cut the pavement
along a neat vertical line at least 12 inches (30 cm) from the trench edge.
Where the neat line cut is less than three feet (0.9 m) from the edge of the
existing pavement, remove and replace the entire pavement section between
trench and edge of pavement. Dispose of the asphalt concrete and/or Portland
cement concrete debris off-site according to applicable state and local
regulations.
   (B)   Removal of surface material.
      (1)   Gravel street or developed surface. When excavating across existing
gravel streets or other developed surfaces, remove the surfacing material full
depth and stockpile for inclusion as trench backfill or legally dispose of the
surfacing material.
      (2)   Cultivated or sodded areas. When excavating across cultivated or
sodded areas, remove topsoil full depth or to a maximum 12-inch (30 cm) depth,
whichever is less, and stockpile for possible use.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-7) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.087 TRENCH EXCAVATION.
   (A)   Standards. Trench excavation shall meet current OSHA safety and health
standards for all excavation, trenching, shoring and related work.
   (B)   Crossing under sidewalks or curbs. Crossing under sidewalks or curbs
may be made by tunneling. If a portion of a sidewalk or curb is removed, use a
concrete saw to make joints, compact the backfill as specified and replace the
removed section with new concrete sidewalk or curb.
   (C)   Stockpiling backfill. During excavation, stockpile backfill materials
away from the trench banks to assure trench wall stability. Stockpile excavated
materials on only one side of the trench without obstructing existing fire
hydrants, valves, manholes and other appurtenances. Contractors shall ensure
surface drainage of adjoining areas is unobstructed.
   (D)   Surface water. Contractors shall prevent surface water from flowing
into excavations. Promptly remove all water accumulating in trench excavations.
Do not permit water to accumulate in any open trench. Pipe that is out of
alignment or grade caused by trench flooding shall be removed and relaid.
   (E)   Trench bottoms. Trench bottoms shall be graded to the specific lines
and grades. Bedding material shall provide uniform bearing and support for each
pipe section along its entire length. Joints and bells shall be excavated for,
with the excavation limited to the length, depth and width for the particular
type of joint used. Backfill over excavations with Type 2 bedding material.
   (F)   Hand methods. If trenching operations are likely to cause damage to
existing structures or features, hand methods are to be employed.
   (G)   Excavation. The trench shall be excavated as required for the invert
grade or pipe bury as specified plus four inches (ten cm) for the Type 1 pipe
bedding. If bedrock, boulders or large stones are encountered at the bottom of
the trench, excavate at least six inches (15 cm) below the bottom of the pipe
for backfilling with Type 1 pipe bedding.
   (H)   Soft or unstable material. When soft or unstable material is
encountered at the trench subgrade which will not uniformly support the pipe,
excavate the material to a depth sufficient and backfill to trench subgrade
elevation with Type 2 pipe bedding.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-8) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.088 PAVEMENT DAMAGE CAUSED BY EQUIPMENT.
   All track mounted equipment operated on pavement surfaces shall be equipped
with pads to prevent pavement damage. All pavement damaged by construction
shall be restored to original condition by the contractor at his or her
expense.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-9) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.089 EXCAVATION STABILITY AND SAFETY.
   (A)   Standards. The contractor shall provide all shoring, bracing and tight
sheeting required to prevent caving and protect workers, meeting current
Occupational Safety and Health Act, 29 U.S.C. §§ 651 - 678 requirements and all
other local, state and federal laws and regulations, and to protect adjacent
property and structures.
   (B)   Responsibility of contractor. The stability of construction
excavations and associated worker safety, including slope geometry and shoring/
bracing considerations, are the responsibility of the contractor and shall meet
current OSHA and all other applicable local, state and federal laws and
regulations.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-10) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.090 TRENCH FILLING AND BACKFILLING.
   All trenches shall be backfilled immediately after grade, alignment and pipe
jointing has been inspected and approved. Backfill materials shall not be water
jetted or ponded. Limit water in the backfill material to that required to
provide adequate moisture for compaction.
   (A)   Pipe bedding placement.
      (1)   Place Type 1 bedding material four inches (ten cm) under the pipe,
around the pipe and up to the springline of the pipe. Place in maximum lifts of
six inches (15 cm), using hand or other compaction methods without damaging or
disturbing the pipe. Thoroughly compact each layer. Use special care to assure
compaction under the pipe haunches. Place backfill material in equal lifts on
both sides of the pipe for the full trench width. Take care to prevent
migration of Type 1 bedding into surrounding soils during placement and
compaction.
      (2)   Select Type 1 bedding material shall be placed from the springline
to six inches (15 cm) over the pipe. Where wet or unstable material exists,
ensure the material is free draining and nonplastic. Place in maximum lifts of
six inches (15 cm) using hand or other compaction methods without damaging or
disturbing the pipe. Thoroughly compact each layer. Place backfill in equal
lifts on both sides of the pipe for the full trench width. Take care to prevent
migration of select Type 1 bedding into surrounding soils during placement and
compaction.
      (3)   Use Type 2 pipe bedding material as described in the Montana Public
Works Standard Specifications Manual, current edition, to replace unsuitable
material encountered in the trench bottom, placing it from the bottom of the
Type 1 bedding material to the depth required to adequately support the pipe.
   (B)   Trench backfill.
      (1)   After the pipe bedding materials are placed and compacted as
specified, backfill the trench. Use backfill material free of cinders, ash,
refuse, organic or frozen material, boulders or other deleterious materials.
From the top of the select Type 1 pipe bedding to six inches (15 cm) below the
ground surface, or the subgrade elevation, material containing rock up to eight
inches (20 cm) in the greatest dimension may be used.
      (2)   Trench backfill from the top of the pipe bedding to ground surface
or the street subgrade is separated into three classifications. Type A trench
backfill is compacted backfill typically used in streets or paved areas. Type B
trench backfill is typically used for alleys, cultivated areas, borrow pits,
unimproved streets or other unsurfaced areas, and other areas where compaction
is less critical. Type C trench backfill is typically used in open and
unimproved areas outside of the public right-of-way. The contractor shall meet
the backfill and compaction requirements for all of the backfill types
described in the contract documents.
      (3)   Where any settlement has occurred, the contractor shall remove,
replace and recompact the backfill in trenches at his or her expense.
      (4)   Type A trench backfill: Place trench backfill in maximum eight-inch
compacted lifts within 3% of optimum moisture content and compact to at least
95% of maximum dry density determined by AASHTO T99 or by ASTM D698.
      (5)   Type B trench backfill: Place backfill in maximum eight-inch (205
cm) lifts, within 3% of optimum moisture content, and compact to at least 90%
of maximum dry density as determined by AASHTO T99 (ASTM D698). Cultivated
areas are to be backfilled with Type B trench backfill.
      (6)   In cultivated areas, place stripped topsoil uniformly over the
backfilled trench to the original depth. Do not compact the topsoil, but grade
to provide a smooth surface conforming to the adjoining ground surfaces.
Remediate any settlement of the trench surface below final surface grade
throughout the contract warranty period.
      (7)   Type C trench backfill: Place and compact Type C trench backfill in
maximum 12-inch lifts at densities equal to or greater than the densities of
adjoining undisturbed soil. Mound earth over the trench top if so directed.
   (C)   Replacement of unsuitable backfill materials. Remove and dispose of
excavated soils that are saturated, contain deleterious materials or have
characteristics that render the soils unsuitable as backfill. If suitable
replacement material is not available within project limits, obtain material
from an approved borrow source. Place and compact all imported material
according to the applicable backfill specification requirements.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-11) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.091 PAVEMENT RESTORATION.
   (A)   Replacement. The pavement section shall be replaced with a section and
material equal to or better than that removed from the street as noted below
and shall be placed in a workmanlike manner that will produce a smooth surface
street cross-section and prevent any puddling of runoff on either side or the
middle of the restored section.
   (B)   Specifications. The replacement surfacing section will not be less
than three inches of asphaltic hot mix and six inches of one and one-half
inches uniformly graded gravel. In no case will the new replacement section be
less than the existing roadway section. The gravel shall have optimum moisture
and compacted to 95% proctor density or to the satisfaction of the inspector.
Tack coat shall be applied to all square cut edges of existing asphalt. The
asphaltic hot mix shall be placed and compacted so as to leave no noticeable
dip or depression. In emergency conditions, cold mix can be used but will be
replaced by hot mix as soon as the weather will permit. Trenches will be
restored a minimum of 12 inches beyond the trench walls.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-12) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.092 TRAFFIC CONTROL.
   (A)   Minimum interference. The contractor shall conduct his or her work so
as to interfere as little as possible with public travel, whether vehicular or
pedestrian.
   (B)   Temporary expedients. Whenever it is necessary to cross, obstruct or
close roads, driveways and walks, whether public or private, the contractor
shall obtain approval from the governing party and shall, at his or her own
expense, provide and maintain suitable and safe bridges, detours and other
temporary expedients for the accommodation of public and private drives before
interfering with them.
   (C)   Traffic control devices. All traffic control devices shall meet the
requirements of the Manual of Uniform Traffic Control Devices and the Traffic
Control Devices Handbook and all other local, state and federal laws and
regulations.
   (D)   Signs and barricades. All signs and barricades shall be reflectorized
and all nighttime traffic control devices shall meet MUTCD lighting
requirements.
   (E)   Placement. All traffic control devices as planned shall be placed
before permitting people or equipment on the traveled way.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-13) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.093 CLEANUP AND INSPECTION.
   (A)   Cleanup. It is the contractor’s responsibility to remove from the
project any excess material and ensure that the premises are left in a clean
and presentable condition.
   (B)   Inspection. Before backfilling, the contractor will notify the Public
Works Department so that an authorized representative will be present to
perform necessary tests and inspections to assure that all work is in
compliance with these specifications.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-14) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
§ 151.094 PROOF OF INSURANCE.
   Any person, association or corporation or public utility who has cause to
excavate any street, avenue or alley in the city shall file a certificate of
insurance or its equivalent with the city providing public liability coverage
which limits are set by resolution.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-15) (Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997)
POLES, WIRES AND PIPES
§ 151.105 DESIGNATION OF LOCATION.
   All poles, pipes, conduits or mains of any description which shall be
placed, located in, along, under or upon any of the streets, avenues or public
places of the city, by any person, shall be placed and located where designated
by the City Engineer under and in conformity and in accordance with the
provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 8-5-1)
§ 151.106 STREETS AND ALLEYS.
   (A)   Width. Any person placing or locating any poles, pipes, conduits or
mains within the city shall place such poles, pipes, conduits or mains in the
alleys of the city where the alleys are of sufficient width to permit the
placing of such poles, pipes, conduits or mains therein without causing any
inconvenience to the public in its travel along or upon such alleys. Where the
alleys are not of sufficient width to permit the placing of such poles, pipes,
conduits or mains therein without causing unnecessary inconvenience to the
public in the use thereof, such poles, pipes, conduits or mains are to be
placed and erected along and upon such streets and avenues of the city as shall
be designated by the City Engineer and in conformity with the provisions of
this subchapter. The City Engineer shall be the sole judge of what alleys are
of sufficient width to permit of the placing of such poles, pipes, conduits or
mains therein and that all poles, pipes, conduits or mains are to be placed and
erected in, along, under or upon any of the streets, avenues, alleys or public
places in the city, shall be so placed and erected therein, under the general
supervision and subject to the approval of the City Engineer.
   (B)   Location. Where poles, pipes, conduits or mains are located upon or
under any of the streets or avenues of the city, they shall be located on the
outside edge of the sidewalk immediately inside the curbstone and on the line
dividing the lots, one from the other, as far as practicable. Poles, pipes,
conduits or mains shall be placed in the alleys as near the sides thereof as
practicable and in such manner as to occasion no unreasonable inconvenience to
the public or to the adjoining property owners. In no case are poles, pipes,
conduits or mains to be placed so as to interfere with any sewer or any part of
the drainage system of the city or with any water main or pipe, nor shall any
poles, pipes, conduits or mains be placed so as to interfere with free access
to the entrances or exits of any building or buildings, public places or
established entrances to any premises.
(Prior Code, § 8-5-2)
§ 151.107 NOTICE OF INTENTION TO INSTALL.
   Any person, firm or corporation desiring to install telephone lines, pipes,
conduits and mains along or under any streets, avenues or alleys in the city
shall file a notice and a plat or map showing the proposed location of such
desired installation with the City Engineer for approval before any such
installation of telephone lines, pipes, conduits or mains is allowed.
(Prior Code, § 8-5-3)
§ 151.108 RESTORATION OF SURFACES.
   When any excavation is made in any street, avenue or alley for the erection
of poles or the placing of pipes, conduits or mains underground, or for any
other purpose in connection with the erection, construction, maintenance and
operation of any public utility in such city, as provided in this subchapter,
such street, avenue or alley shall be restored to its former condition without
unnecessary delay.
(Prior Code, § 8-5-4)
Cross-reference:
   Trench backfill and street restoration, see §§
151.080 through
151.094
§ 151.109 INDEMNIFICATION.
   Any person who shall construct, own, operate or control any public utility
within the city under the provisions of this subchapter shall save the city
harmless from any damage or claim for damages to any person or property which
may accrue, be caused or occasioned from the construction, operation or
maintenance of any public utility within the city.
(Prior Code, § 8-5-5)
§ 151.110 ADDITIONAL RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   The city reserves the right to make, by resolution or ordinance, other and
further regulations and rules governing the erection of poles in and the
stringing of wires along, in, upon or through its streets, avenues or alleys
and the laying, maintenance and operation of pipes, conduits or mains under any
of its streets, avenues or alleys as may from time to time appear necessary.
(Prior Code, § 8-5-6)
SPECIAL IMPROVEMENT DISTRICTS
§ 151.125 APPLICATION.
   (A)   Form. Applications for consideration for approval by the City Council
of special improvement districts shall be made in the form and according to the
procedure set down by the Finance Department for the city.
   (B)   Fees and deposits. The application shall be accompanied by an
administrative fee and deposit. The administrative fee for an accepted SID
shall be 3% of the SID total construction cost and shall be allocated to the
General Fund for costs incurred by the city for formation of the district and
sale of bonds. There shall be a required nonrefundable deposit in the amount of
$5,000 to cover costs, including, without limitation, city administrative
costs, legal fees and costs and other costs associated with a proposed special
improvement district. In the event the proposed special improvement district
fails to be established, the city shall receipt such deposit into its General
Fund to reimburse such costs. In the event the proposed special improvement
district is established, the deposit shall be applied to administrative fees
and funding the District Reserve Account in that order.
(Prior Code, § 8-6-1) (Ord. 04-2012, passed 8-21-2012)
§ 151.126 REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Creation of special improvement districts and issuance of bonds
secured by the Revolving Fund. In accordance with the provisions of M.C.A.
Title 7, Chapter 12, parts 42 and 43, the city may create special improvement
districts (SIDs) for financing improvements upon a determination that the
creation of the district and the installation of the improvements are in the
public interest. The city may issue special improvement district bonds for
financing the costs of construction and installing the improvements and paying
incidental costs related thereto as follows.
      (1)   Developed districts. The maximum amount that may be financed
through an SID shall be $200,000 for residential properties and $300,000 for
commercial properties. The foregoing maximum amounts shall be the maximum total
for all infrastructure related to the property.
      (2)   Developed previously platted/subdivided property. The maximum
amount that may be financed through an SID shall be $200,000 for residential
properties and $300,000 for commercial properties. The foregoing maximum
amounts shall be the maximum total for all infrastructure related to the
property.
      (3)   Developed annexed property. The maximum amount to be financed
through an SID shall be $200,000 for residential properties and $300,000 for
commercial properties. The foregoing maximum amounts shall be the maximum total
for all infrastructure related to the property.
      (4)   Undeveloped districts. The city will not finance undeveloped
districts through an SID.
      (5)   Undeveloped previously platted/subdivided property. The city will
not finance undeveloped previously platted/subdivided property through an SID.
      (6)   Undeveloped annexed property. The city will not finance undeveloped
annexed property through an SID.
   (B)   Costs of improvements. Any costs of the improvements, including,
without limitation, engineering, survey and legal work incurred prior to the
issuance of the bonds, deposits to the Revolving Fund and city expenses, may be
eligible for financing by the district as defined in M.C.A. § 7-12-4169(1) if
the reimbursement is in compliance with United States Treasury regulations.
   (C)   Amount of improvements to be financed. The determination of which
improvements to finance by special improvement districts will be made by the
city in consultation with the developer, where appropriate. In making its
determination, the city will consider the nature of the improvements and the
ability to finance them on a tax exempt basis.
   (D)   Delinquent developers. It is the general policy of the city that any
person requesting the creation of a special improvement district shall, as a
condition of approval of said district, be current in the payment of all
existing city special improvement district assessments for which said person is
responsible on all properties owned by said person. Additionally, as a
condition of approval of said district, such person shall not have been
delinquent on any prior special improvement district assessments with the city.
   (E)   Annexed property. Annexed property shall waive the right to protest
special improvement districts for infrastructure improvements required as a
condition of and relative to the property being annexed into the city.
   (F)   Amortization of bonds. All special improvement bonds shall be
amortized over a period not to exceed 15 years.
(Prior Code, § 8-6-2) (Ord. 04-2012, passed 8-21-2012)
§ 151.127 REVOLVING FUND AND DISTRICT RESERVE ACCOUNT.
   (A)   Deposit to the Revolving Fund.
      (1)   For districts for which the city issues bonds secured by the
Revolving Fund, the costs of the improvements shall include a deposit to the
Revolving Fund of at least 5% and not more than 10% of the principal amount of
the bonds to be issued. As allowed in M.C.A. § 7-12-4169(3), the city will also
require the establishment of a District Reserve Account in addition to the
deposit to the Revolving Fund.
      (2)   The District Reserve Account will be in the amount of 5% of the
principal amount of the bonds, will be created and maintained in the district
fund, will be accounted for separately from the deposits into the Revolving
Fund and will be designated for the district which it secures. Deposits to the
District Reserve Account shall be made from sources other than proceeds of the
bonds issued for such district financing.
   (B)   Bonds not secured by the Revolving Fund. For districts for which the
city issues bonds not secured by the Revolving Fund, the city will require the
establishment of a District Reserve Account. The deposit into the District
Reserve Account will be in the amount of 5% of the principal amount of the
bonds. The District Reserve Account will be created and maintained in the
district fund, will be available only for use in connection with payments of
principal and interest on the bonds issued in connection with that district and
will be designated for the special improvement district which it secures.
Deposits to the District Reserve Account shall be made from sources other than
proceeds of the bonds issued for such district financing.
   (C)   Payments from revolving and District Reserve Account for delinquent
assessments. At any time an assessment becomes delinquent, the District Reserve
Account and/or Revolving Fund, in that order, shall provide funds, if
available, to meet the current payment of principal, interest and other amounts
due with respect to the bonds.
   (D)   Amounts remaining in Revolving Fund and District Reserve Account. Any
amounts, specific to a particular bond, remaining in the District Reserve
Account shall be applied to the final bond payment(s). Any amount remaining in
the Revolving Fund, specific to a particular bond and not required to be kept
or maintained in the Revolving Fund shall be deposited into the city’s General
Fund.
(Prior Code, § 8-6-3) (Ord. 04-2012, passed 8-21-2012)
§ 151.128 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANNEXED PROPERTY. Property annexed into the city after January 1, 2010.
   COMMERCIAL PROPERTY. Property zoned R-3 (multiple-family dwelling), R-4
(multiple-family dwelling and townhouses), C-1 (general commercial), C-2
(central business), C-3 (highway commercial) and M-1 (light industrial).
   COSTS OF IMPROVEMENTS. The incidental expenses and costs described in M.C.A.
Title 7, Chapter 12, parts 41 and 42.
   COSTS OF ISSUANCE. All items of cost or expense directly or indirectly
payable by or reimbursable to the city and related to the authorization, sale
and issuance of bonds, including, without limitation, the city’s fees, bond
discount fees, costs of preparation and reproduction of documents, initial fees
and charges of a trustee, if any, legal fees and charges, fees and charges
related to authorization and issuance of the bonds, fees and costs of financial
consultants and underwriters and fees for preparation, execution and
safekeeping of the bond.
   DEVELOPED ANNEXED PROPERTY. Property which has been annexed in which 51% or
more of the lots, tracts or parcels have occupied structures located thereon
and where 51% or more of the costs of any district will be assessed against
such improved lots, tracts or parcels.
   DEVELOPED DISTRICT. A special improvement district in which 51% or more of
the costs of the district will be assessed against lots, tracts or parcels
which have occupied structures located thereon.
   DEVELOPED PREVIOUSLY PLATTED/SUBDIVIDED PROPERTY. Property located within
the city limits in which 51% or more of the lots, tracts or parcels have
occupied structures located thereon, which was platted and/or subdivided prior
to January 1, 2010, and where 51% or more of the costs of any district will be
assessed against such improved lots, tracts or parcels.
   DEVELOPER. Any person requesting the creation of a special improvement
district for undeveloped property.
   DISTRICT RESERVE ACCOUNT. An account authorized under M.C.A. § 7-12-4169(3)
and funded by the developer requesting the creation of a special improvement
district from sources other than bond proceeds, and used specifically to fund
deficiencies in principal, interest and other payments within the district
requested.
   IMPROVEMENTS. Public improvements authorized by M.C.A. § 7-12-4102 to be
constructed and financed through the creation of special improvement districts.
   ON-SITE IMPROVEMENTS. The improvements located within the boundaries of a
special improvement district.
   PERSON. Any individual, corporation, firm, partnership, limited liability
company, organization or other entity.
   RESIDENTIAL PROPERTY. Property zoned R-1 (one-family residential) and R-2
(one-family and two-family residential).
   REVOLVING FUND. The fund established by the city pursuant to M.C.A. §§ 7-12-
4221 et seq.
   SPECIAL IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT BONDS or BONDS. Bonds issued by the city
pursuant to M.C.A. Title 7, Chapter 12, parts 41 and 42 for the purpose of
financing improvements within special improvement districts and paying
incidental costs, as defined in M.C.A. § 7-12-4101, related to the creation of
the districts and the issuance of the bonds.
   SPECIAL IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT OR DISTRICT (SID). The districts established or
proposed to be established pursuant to M.C.A. Title 7, Chapter 12, parts 41 and
42 for the purpose of constructing and installing improvements for the special
benefit of properties located within such districts.
   UNDEVELOPED ANNEXED PROPERTY. Property in which less than 51% of the lots,
tracts or parcels have occupied structures located thereon.
   UNDEVELOPED DISTRICT. A special improvement district in which less than 51%
of the costs of the district will be assessed against lots, tracts or parcels
which have occupied structures located thereon.
   UNDEVELOPED PREVIOUSLY PLATTED/SUBDIVIDED PROPERTY. Property located within
the city limits in which less than 51% of the lots, tracts or parcels have
occupied structures located thereon and which was platted and/or subdivided
prior to January 1, 2010.
(Prior Code, § 8-6-4) (Ord. 04-2012, passed 8-21-2012)
§ 151.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Violation of the provisions of §§
151.045 through
151.049, or failure to comply with any of its requirements, shall constitute a
misdemeanor. Any person who violates §§
151.045 through
151.049 or fails to comply with any of its requirements shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined as specified in §
10.99 and, in addition, shall pay all costs and expenses involved in the case.
Each day such violation continues shall be considered a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 8-2-6)
   (B)   Violation of the provisions of §§
151.080 through
151.094 or failure to comply with any of its requirements shall constitute a
misdemeanor. Any person who violates §§
151.080 through
151.094 or fails to comply with any of its requirements shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined as specified in §
10.99, and in addition shall pay all costs and expenses involved in the case.
Each day such violation continues shall be considered a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 8-4-16)
   (C)   Any person, firm, association or corporation who shall refuse or
neglect to comply with any provision of this chapter for which no specific
penalty is prescribed shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished in accordance
with §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 8-8-3)
(Ord. 74-85, passed 6-2-1997; Ord. 02-2001, passed 3-20-2001)
CHAPTER 152: TREES
Section
   
152.01   Definitions
   
152.02   Nuisance declared
   
152.03   Dead or diseased trees
   
152.04   Planting of elm trees and other species
   
152.05   Trimming of trees
   
152.06   Injury to trees or shrubbery
   
152.07   Boulevards; regulation of trees
 
   
152.99   Penalty
§ 152.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BOULEVARD. The strip of land abutting on either side of the streets of the
city lying between the outside edge of the sidewalks and the curb along such
streets or that area between the inside edge of sidewalks and the lot lines in
areas having curbed sidewalks.
   PERSON. Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
   PROPERTY OWNER. The person owning such property as is shown by the County
Clerk and Recorder.
   PUBLIC NUISANCE. A condition which endangers safety or health, is offensive
to the senses or obstructs the free use of property so as to interfere with the
comfortable enjoyment of life or property by an entire community or
neighborhood or by any considerable number of persons, or a condition which
renders dangerous for passage any public highway or right-of-way or waters used
by the public.
   STREET. The entire width between property lines of every way or place of
whatsoever nature when any part thereof is open to the use of the public as a
matter of right-of-way for the purpose of vehicular traffic.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-1) (Ord. 60-85, passed 8-7-1995)
§ 152.02 NUISANCE DECLARED.
   The following conditions are public nuisances whenever they may be found
within the city:
   (A)   Diseased or infected elm trees. Any living or standing elm tree or
part thereof infected to any degree with the Dutch elm disease fungus,
Ceratocystis ulmi, and which harbors any of the elm bark beetles, Scolytus
multistriatus or Hylurgpoinus rufipes; and
   (B)   Projections over public ways. All limbs of trees, shrubs, bushes and
plants which project over any public sidewalks, streets or alleys and which are
less than eight feet above the surface of said public sidewalks and less than
14 feet above the surface of any such street or more than one foot from the
property line for a distance of 14 feet above the alley surface.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-2) (Ord. 60-85, passed 8-7-1995; Ord. 07-2002, passed 5-21-
2002)
§ 152.03 DEAD OR DISEASED TREES.
   (A)   Notice to remove. Whenever the Public Works Director becomes aware of
existence of any dead or diseased tree or part thereof located within the city
limits, or the existence of any trees or parts thereof that constitute a hazard
to life and/or property, or pose a threat to harbor insects or disease which
may constitute a potential threat to other trees within the city limits, he or
she shall notify, in writing, the owner of the property where said tree is
located of the condition and direct that said tree or any part thereof be
removed.
   (B)   Removal; disposal. Removal shall be done by said owner at their own
expense within 30 days after the date of service of said notice. The removed
tree shall be transported to the city landfill for disposal by burial or
burning.
   (C)   Stumps. All stumps of trees shall be removed below the surface of the
ground so that the top of the stump shall not project above the surface of the
ground or the entire stump shall be stripped of the bark upon cutting of the
tree.
   (D)   Removal by city; costs.
      (1)   In the event the owner fails to remove said tree within the 30-day
period in the manner provided herein, the city shall have the authority to
remove said tree and charge the cost of removal to the real property in
question by billing or special assessment if not paid in the manner prescribed
by law.
      (2)   Said costs and expenses shall become a lien on said premises and
shall be certified and collected as other taxes or the City Attorney may begin
a civil action in the city court in the name of the city and against any owner,
occupant or agent of said premises for the collection of said costs and
expenses and the cost of the action.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-3) (Ord. 60-85, passed 8-7-1995)
§ 152.04 PLANTING OF ELM TREES AND OTHER SPECIES.
   In order to prevent Dutch elm disease, the planting of elm trees (American,
Siberian, Dropmore and any and all other elm selections of Ulmus species) shall
be prohibited on boulevards, public property and city rights-of-way. In
addition, Carolina poplar, Canadian poplar, Lombardy poplar, Silver Leaf
poplar, willows, Box elder, aspen, cottonwoods and birch trees shall not be
planted in streets, avenues, boulevards or alleys or other public ways of the
city.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-4) (Ord. 07-2002, passed 5-21-2002) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.05 TRIMMING OF TREES.
   (A)   Duty to trim. All owners and occupants of real property located within
the city limits shall keep trimmed all trees located on their property which
overhang on any public thoroughfare so that the branches thereon do not
interfere with pedestrians or public travel.
   (B)   Public nuisance prohibited. It shall also be the duty of the owners of
all real property located within the city, as well as the duty of all persons
in possession of such property, to cause all trees, shrubs, bushes and plants
located on their property to be trimmed, so as not to constitute a public
nuisance, as defined above.
   (C)   Notice to abate. The Public Works Director shall have the authority to
make determinations as to whether a condition exists so as to constitute a
public nuisance. Upon determination that such a condition does exist, the
Public Works Director shall then notify, in writing, the property owner or
person in possession of said property.
   (D)   Contents of notice. Such notice shall inform the property owner or
person in possession of said property that the public nuisance condition must
be corrected within 30 days or the Public Works Director will direct the
trimming of said trees, shrubs, bushes and plants which constitute the
nuisance. The necessary expense of such trimming or maintenance shall be
charged against the real property in question by billing or special assessment
if not paid in the manner prescribed by law. Said costs and expenses shall
become a lien on said premises and shall be certified and collected as taxes or
the City Attorney may begin a civil action in the city court in the name of the
city and against any owner, occupant or agent of said premises for the
collection of said costs and expenses and the cost of the action.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-5) (Ord. 60-85, passed 8-7-1995) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.06 INJURY TO TREES OR SHRUBBERY.
   It is hereby declared unlawful for any person who is not the owner thereof
or who is without lawful authority so to do, to willfully injure, deface,
disfigure or destroy any tree or shrub, or to injure, destroy, cut or pick any
flower or plant located either on private property or on any public property or
thoroughfare.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-6) (Ord. 60-85, passed 8-7-1995) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.07 BOULEVARDS; REGULATION OF TREES.
   (A)   Responsibility of owner. The owner of the real property adjoining a
boulevard shall be responsible for the care and maintenance of the boulevard,
and he or she shall keep the tree, shrubs, bushes and plants located thereon
trimmed and in condition so the same shall not constitute a public nuisance.
   (B)   Trees. Trees shall be spaced 30 to 50 feet apart depending on the
mature height and width of the tree type planted and shall be located so as not
to interfere with pedestrian or vehicular traffic or vision.
   (C)   Shrubs. No shrub shall be planted within five feet of a fire hydrant
or within a clear view triangle if its mature height will exceed three feet.
   (D)   Removal by city. If it becomes necessary for the city to remove any
trees, shrubs, bushes and plants from said boulevard, the costs of such removal
shall be assessed against said adjoining property.
   (E)   Costs; lien. Such costs and expenses shall become a lien on said
adjoining premises and shall be certified and collected as other taxes, or the
City Attorney may begin a civil action in the city court in the name of the
city against any owner, occupant or agent of said adjoining premises for the
collection of said costs and expenses and the cost of the action.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-7) (Ord. 07-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
§ 152.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction or
a plea of guilty, be subject to a fine as provided in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 8-9-8) (Ord. 60-85, passed 8-7-1995)
CHAPTER 153: RADIO, TELEVISION AND WIRELESS COMMUNICATIONS FACILITIES
Section
   
153.01   Amateur radio antenna
   
153.02   Wireless communication facilities
   
153.03   Appeals
§ 153.01 AMATEUR RADIO ANTENNA.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      AMATEUR RADIO ANTENNA. A ground, building or tower mounted antenna
operated by a federally licensed amateur radio operator as part of the Amateur
Radio Service, 49 C.F.R. part 97 and as designated by the Federal
Communications Commission (FCC).
      AMATEUR RADIO ANTENNA SUPPORT STRUCTURE. Any structure or device
specifically designed, constructed and/or erected for the purpose of attaching,
mounting or otherwise affixing amateur radio antennas. The term includes the
structure and any support thereto.
      ANTENNA SUPPORT STRUCTURE HEIGHT. The vertical distance measured from the
base of the antenna support structure at grade to the highest point of the
structure, including any attached antennas. If the support structure is on a
sloped grade, then the average between the highest and lowest grades shall be
used in calculating the antenna height.
   (B)   General provisions. All amateur radio towers shall comply with the
following requirements.
      (1)   Location. Amateur radio antenna support structures and antennas
shall be located only within the rear yard and shall not be placed within any
required setback and shall be located so as to minimize their impact on
adjacent residential properties and adjacent rights-of-way while maintaining
acceptable signal quality.
      (2)   Building permit required. Amateur radio antenna support structures
and antennas exceeding six feet in height above grade (if ground-mounted) or
above the roof or ridge of the building on which they are located (if building-
mounted) shall require a building permit. With each building permit, the
applicant shall submit evidence as is required to show that the device is
adequately anchored, designed and/or constructed so as to safeguard the general
public and/or adjacent property from damage in the event of failure of the
device.
      (3)   Design, installation and maintenance. It is recommended that
amateur radio antenna support structures be designed, installed and maintained
so as to blend into the surrounding environment through the use of color and
alternative designs, except in instances where the color is dictated by the
Federal Aviation Administration (FAA).
      (4)   Height limitations. In accordance with the FCC preemptive ruling
PRB 1,101 FCC 2d 952 (1985), antenna support structures erected for the primary
purpose of supporting amateur radio antennas may exceed the height limitations
of the underlying zoning as indicated in §
155.017.
      (5)   Attachments. Attachments to amateur radio antenna support
structures, such as guy wires, shall not cross any property line or any
existing or proposed easement.
      (6)   Lighting. No lighting shall be permitted on any amateur radio
antenna support structures except as mandated by the FAA.
      (7)   Signage. No signage, other than required warning signs or displays
of any type shall be permitted on any amateur radio antenna support structure.
      (8)   Use.
         (a)   Allowed. Amateur radio support structures and antennas that are
50 feet or less above grade shall be an allowed use in all residential zones.
         (b)   Conditional use permit required. Amateur radio support
structures and antennas that exceed 50 feet in height above grade are allowable
only with a conditional use permit.
   (C)   Applicability. All amateur radio antenna support structures and
antennas located within the city zoning jurisdiction whether upon private or
public lands shall be subject to this section. This section shall apply to
amateur radio antenna support structures and antennas upon state and federal
lands to the extent of the city’s jurisdiction by way of law, pursuant to any
memoranda of understanding or otherwise. Preexisting amateur radio antenna
support structures and preexisting amateur radio antennas shall not be required
to meet the requirements of this section, so long as said preexisting antenna
support structures and antennas have received all required approvals, permits
and exceptions prior to adoption of this section.
(Prior Code, § 9-6-1) (Ord. 06-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
§ 153.02 WIRELESS COMMUNICATION FACILITIES.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      ABANDONED ANTENNA SUPPORT STRUCTURES. Any antennas or antenna support
structures that are not utilized for the provision of wireless communications
services for a continuous period of six months shall be considered ABANDONED.
      ALTERNATIVE ANTENNA SUPPORT STRUCTURE. An antenna support structure
designed to shield, conceal or disguise the presence of antennas or towers and
blend with the surrounding setting. ALTERNATIVE STRUCTURES may include, but are
not limited to, unobtrusive architectural features on new or existing
structures, utility poles, clock towers, flagpoles and church steeples.
      ANTENNA. Any structure or device used for the purpose of collecting or
transmitting electromagnetic waves, including, but not limited to, directional
antennas, such as panels, microwave dishes and satellite dishes and omni-
directional antennas, such as whip antennas, but not including satellite earth
stations.
      ANTENNA SUPPORT STRUCTURE. Any structure or device specifically designed,
constructed and/or erected for the purpose of attaching, mounting or otherwise
affixing antennas. ANTENNA SUPPORT STRUCTURES may include, but are not limited
to, self-supporting lattice towers, guyed towers or monopole towers. The term
also includes radio and television transmission towers, microwave towers,
common carrier towers, cellular telephone towers, alternative antenna support
structures and the like. The term includes the structure and any support
thereto.
      ANTENNA/ANTENNA SUPPORT STRUCTURE HEIGHT. The vertical distance measured
from the base of the antenna support structure at grade to the highest point of
the structure, including any attached antennas. If the support structure is on
a sloped grade, then the average between the highest and lowest grades shall be
used in calculating the antenna height. The height of roof-mounted ANTENNA
SUPPORT STRUCTURE HEIGHT does not include the height of building on which they
are mounted.
      COLLOCATION. The use of a wireless communications facility by more than
one wireless communications provider.
      COMMERCIAL WIRELESS COMMUNICATIONS SERVICES. Licensed commercial wireless
telecommunication services, including cellular, personal communications
services (PCS), specialized mobilized radio (SMR), enhanced specialized
mobilized radio (ESMR), paging and similar services that are marketed to the
general public.
      EQUIPMENT ENCLOSURE. A structure, shelter, cabinet or vault used to house
and protect the electronic equipment necessary for processing wireless
communication signals. Associated equipment may include air conditioning,
backup power supplies and emergency generators.
      FAA. Federal Aviation Administration.
      FCC. Federal Communications Commission.
      WIRELESS COMMUNICATION FACILITY. An unstaffed facility for the
transmission and/or reception of radio frequency (RF), microwave or other
signals for commercial communications purposes, typically consisting of an
equipment enclosure, an antenna support structure and one or more antennas.
Amateur radio, land mobile radio and commercial radio and television facilities
are excluded from this definition.
      WIRELESS COMMUNICATION FACILITY ANTENNA OR TOWER FARM. An antenna or
tower farm is a tract of land that contains no more than three antenna support
structures within 750 linear feet of each other. No antenna support structures
located in tower farms shall exceed 250 feet in height. Legal tracts must be
adjacent to each other to be included in this definition.
   (B)   Applicability. All wireless communication facilities located within
the city jurisdiction, whether upon private or public lands, shall be subject
to this section. This section shall apply to wireless communication facilities
upon state and federal lands to the extent of the city’s jurisdiction by way of
law, pursuant to any memoranda of understanding or otherwise. Only the
following facilities shall be exempted from the application of this section:
      (1)   Amateur radio stations and antenna support structures;
      (2)   Antennas and antenna support structures for land mobile radio and
radio and television; and
      (3)   Preexisting antenna support structures or antennas. Preexisting
antenna support structures and preexisting antennas shall not be required to
meet the requirements of this section, so long as said preexisting antenna
support structures have received all required approvals, permits and exceptions
prior to adoption of this section.
   (C)   Standards. This section is to establish regulations for the siting of
antenna support structures and antennas on public and private property. The
goals of this section are to:
      (1)   Encourage the location of antenna support structures in
nonresidential areas and minimize the total number of antenna support
structures throughout the community;
      (2)   Strongly encourage the joint use of new and existing antenna
support structures;
      (3)   Require wireless communication facilities to be located, to the
extent possible, in areas where the adverse impact on the community is minimal;
      (4)   Require wireless communication facilities to be configured in a way
that minimizes the adverse visual impact of the towers and antennas; and
      (5)   Enhance the ability of the providers of wireless communication
services to provide such services to the community, as quickly, effectively and
efficiently as possible.
   (D)   Commercial antenna support structures and antennas.
      (1)   Residential zoning districts. Antenna support structures and
antennas shall be permitted as an allowed use in all residential zoning
districts, provided they meet all of the following criteria.
         (a)   Alternative antenna support structures conforming to all
applicable provisions of this code and roof-mounted antennas that do not add
more than 20 feet to the total height of the building on which they are mounted
shall be permitted as an allowed use only when located on school, government
owned utility and other government sites. Proposed antennas or antenna support
structures that are contrary to this section are subject to the conditional use
requirements of the zoning regulations or may be submitted to the Board of
Adjustment for a hearing. The Board of Adjustment shall hold a public hearing
and shall forward comments and recommendations to the City Council for its
consideration.
         (b)   Antennas collocated on existing or approved alternative antenna
support structures or existing or approved antenna support structures which
have previously received all required approvals and permits shall be permitted
as an allowed use.
      (2)   Commercial zoning districts.
         (a)   Alternative antenna structures shall be permitted as an allowed
use in all commercial zoning districts.
         (b)   Antenna support structures shall be permitted as an allowed use
in all commercial zoning districts when located on school, government owned
utility and other government sites. Proposed antennas or antenna support
structures that are contrary to this section are subject to the conditional use
requirements or may be submitted to the Board of Adjustment for a hearing. The
Board of Adjustment shall hold a public hearing and shall forward comments and
recommendations to the City Council for their consideration.
         (c)   Antennas collocated on existing alternative antenna support
structures or existing antenna support structures which have previously
received all required approvals and permits shall be permitted as an allowed
use in all commercial zones.
         (d)   Antenna support structures and antennas located in Residential
Professional (RP) and Neighborhood Commercial Limited (NCL) that do not meet
the requirements of divisions (D)(2)(a), (D)(2)(b) and (D)(2)(c) above shall be
required to obtain conditional use approval. Wireless communication facility
tower farms are not allowed in these zoning districts.
         (e)   Antenna support structures and antennas located in the General
Commercial District (C-1), Central Business District (C-2) and the Highway
Commercial District (C-3) shall be permitted as an allowed use, provided that
the towers meet the requirements of divisions (D)(2)(a), (D)(2)(b) and (D)(2)
(c) above or:
            1.   Roof-mounted antenna that do not add more than 20 feet to the
total height of the building on which it is mounted shall be permitted as an
allowed use;
            2.   Antenna support structures 50 feet in height or less shall be
permitted as an allowed use;
            3.   Antenna support structures that are greater than 50 feet in
height shall be required to obtain a conditional use permit; and
            4.   Wireless communication facility tower farms are permitted with
conditional use permits, except in the RP, NCL and C-1 Districts.
         (f)   All antenna support structures located in the M-1 and M-
2 Districts shall be permitted as an allowed use, including tower farms.
      (3)   Parks. The presence of certain wireless communication facilities
may conflict with the purpose of some city owned parks and will not be allowed.
   (E)   General requirements. The requirements set forth in this section
govern the location and construction of all wireless communications facilities
governed by this section.
      (1)   Building codes and safety standards. To ensure the structural
integrity of wireless communication facilities, the owner of a facility shall
ensure that it is maintained in compliance with standards contained in
applicable local Building Codes and the applicable standards for such wireless
communication facilities, as amended from time to time.
      (2)   Regulatory compliance. All wireless communication facilities must
meet or exceed current standards and regulations of the FAA, the FCC and other
local, state or federal agencies with the authority to regulate facilities
governed by this section. All wireless communication facilities must comply
with all revised standards and regulations within the date established by the
agency promulgating the standards or regulations.
      (3)   Setbacks.
         (a)   Residential uses or zoning. Antenna support structures must be
set back, from all property lines, a distance equal to one-half the height of
the structure from any off-site residential structure or residentially zoned
lot. Accessory structures must maintain a minimum of a 15-foot setback from any
lot line adjacent to a residential structure or residentially zoned lot, or the
required setback of the zoning district where the antenna support structure is
located, whichever is greater.
         (b)   Commercial and industrial zoning. Commercial and industrial
zoning setbacks antenna support structures and accessory facilities must meet
the minimum yard setback requirements for the zoning district in which they are
located.
      (4)   Lot coverage and height. Antenna support structures and accessory
structures shall not exceed lot coverage requirements for the zoning district
in which they are located. Accessory structures shall not exceed the height
restrictions for the zoning district in which they are located.
      (5)   Fencing and buffering.
         (a)   Fencing. A chain-link or solid wood fence, or masonry wall at
least six feet in height (eight feet, if razor or barbed wire is to be used)
shall be constructed and maintained around the perimeter of the antenna support
structure site. Climb-proof shields can be substituted for a fence or wall
around the structure. Solid fences, at least six feet in height, are required
adjacent to residential uses and residentially zoned property.
         (b)   Landscaping. For all facilities the following will be required.
            1.   A continuous evergreen hedge at least four feet in height when
planted shall be planted and maintained around the perimeter of the antenna
support structure outside of the required fencing and spaced close together to
provide a continuous visual screen.
            2.   Shrubs shall also be planted and maintained around the guy
anchors for visual screening purposes.
         (c)   Commercial landscaping. Landscaping requirements shall not apply
to antenna support structures located in the industrial districts.
      (6)   Lighting. Antenna support structures shall not be artificially
lighted unless required by the FAA or other local, state or federal agency. If
the FAA requires safety lighting, the use of red beacons is preferred to
flashing strobe lights. Security lighting on-site may be mounted up to 20 feet
high on the tower and shall be directed towards the ground to reduce light
pollution, prevent off-site light spillage and avoid illuminating the tower.
Cut-off security lighting must be used adjacent to residential uses or
residentially zoned lots. When incorporated into the approved design of the
facility, light fixtures used to illuminate sports fields, parking lots or
similar areas may be included in the facility.
      (7)   Signage. Signage shall be limited to non-illuminated warning and
equipment identification signs.
      (8)   Collocation.
         (a)   Antenna support structures should be designed in all respects to
accommodate both the applicant’s antennas and antennas for at least two
additional comparable antennas if the antenna support structure is over 100
feet in height or for at least one additional comparable antenna if the tower
is between 50 feet and 100 feet in height.
         (b)   All new antennas must collocate on existing or approved antenna
support structures or alternative antenna support structures unless it can be
demonstrated collocation is not feasible under conditional use submitted
information.
      (9)   Maintenance.
         (a)   Equipment at a wireless communication facility shall be
automated to the greatest extent possible to reduce traffic and congestion.
Where the site abuts or has access to a collector or local street, access for
maintenance vehicles shall be exclusively by means of the collector or local
street.
         (b)   All property used for the siting of an antenna support structure
or antenna shall be maintained, without expense to the city, so as to be safe,
orderly, attractive and in conformity with city codes, including those
regarding the removal of weeds, trash and landscape maintenance.
      (10)   Visual impact/aesthetics.
         (a)   Wireless communication facilities shall either maintain a
galvanized steel finish or, subject to any applicable standards of the FAA or
other applicable local, state or federal agency, or be painted a neutral color
or painted and/or textured to match the existing structure so as to reduce
visual obtrusiveness.
         (b)   If an antenna is installed on a structure other than a tower,
the antenna and associated electrical and mechanical equipment must be of a
neutral color that is identical to, or closely compatible with, the color of
the supporting structure so as to make the antenna and related equipment as
visually unobtrusive as possible. Antennas and antenna support structures may
be mounted on existing buildings that are 30 feet or more in height above the
street grade.
         (c)   Roof-mounted antennas and antenna support structures shall not
add more than 20 feet to the total height of the building on which they are
mounted. Roof-mounted equipment shall be made visually unobtrusive to match
existing air conditioning units, stair, elevator towers or other architectural
elements. Only monopole antennas support structures with omni-directional
(whip) or low profile single-directional (panel) shall be installed on building
roofs. Crow’s nest antennas arrays are prohibited on rooftop structures.
         (d)   Wireless communication facilities attached to new or existing
structures shall be designed to blend with the structure’s architecture and
should be placed directly above, below or incorporated with vertical design
elements of a structure.
         (e)   Wireless communication facilities shall be located as to
minimize their visibility and not be placed within historic or scenic view
corridors as designated by the City Council or by any state or federal law or
agency.
      (11)   Antenna support structure separation.
         (a)   All antenna support structures over 50 feet in height,
regardless of the zoning district in which the structure is located, shall be
located at least one mile from any other antenna support structure that is over
50 feet in height. Up to three antenna support structures located within an
approved wireless communication facility tower farm shall be located at least
one mile from any other tower farm.
         (b)   Exceptions to the terms of this section may be granted by the
governing body during the conditional use review process when it is found that
no existing or approved antenna support structure within the required
separation distance of the proposed site can accommodate the applicant’s
proposed antenna, or a critical need exists for the proposed location, and it
is technically infeasible to locate or collocate structures at or beyond the
required separation distance.
   (F)   Nonconforming wireless communication facilities. Antenna support
structures and/or facilities in existence on the date of the adoption of these
regulations, that do not comply with the requirements of these regulations,
(nonconforming antenna support structures) are subject to the following
provisions.
      (1)   Nonconforming antenna support structures may continue their present
use but may not be expanded or increased in height without complying with these
regulations except as further provided in this section.
      (2)   Nonconforming antenna support structures which are hereafter
damaged and destroyed, by less than 50% of its replacement value, due to any
reason or cause may be repaired and restored to their former use, location and
physical dimensions, subject to obtaining a building permit and other necessary
approvals thereof, but without otherwise complying with these regulations. If
an antenna support structure is destroyed or damaged by more than 50% of its
replacement value, the antenna support structure must be brought into
compliance with these regulations.
      (3)   The owner of any nonconforming antenna support structure may make
minor modifications in order to improve the structural integrity of the
facility, to allow the facility to accommodate collocated antennas of
facilities or to upgrade the facilities to current engineering, technological
or communications standards, without having to conform to the provisions of
these regulations.
   (G)   Modifications of existing wireless communication facilities that meet
the requirements of these regulations.
      (1)   Minor modifications. Minor modifications to facilities permitted
under these regulations shall be approved by the Building Department so long as
they comply with the original approved design. Minor modifications are as
follows: the addition of more antenna arrays to any existing antenna support
structure, so long as the addition of the antenna arrays add no more than 20
feet in height to the facility and the increase in height of the support
structure is no greater than 10%. Placement of additional antennas, up to the
number the antenna support structure was originally designed to accommodate,
shall be considered a minor modification.
      (2)   Major modifications. Major modifications to antenna support
structures permitted under these regulations shall be approved through a
conditional use. Major modifications are any that exceed the definition of
minor modifications.
   (H)   Abandonment. Wireless communication facilities will be considered
abandoned if they are unused by all providers at the facility for a period of
six months. Determination of abandonment shall be made by the Building
Department which shall have the right to request documentation from the
facility owner regarding support or antenna usage. Upon abandonment, the
facility owner shall have 90 days to:
      (1)   Reuse the facility or transfer the facility to another owner who
will reuse it; or
      (2)   If the facility is not removed within 90 days of abandonment, the
city may remove the facility at the facility and/or property owner’s expense.
If the facility is removed, city approval of the facility will expire. If the
facility owner is unable to remove the facility within the 90 days due to
unusual circumstances, the Building Department may grant the facility owner an
additional 90 days in which to comply with the requirements of this division
(H).
   (I)   Conditional use submittal requirements. The applicant of new wireless
communication facilities shall provide the following documentation for review
by the Zoning Coordinator and Building Official:
      (1)   A map to scale showing the service area of the proposed wireless
communication facility and an explanation of the need for that facility;
      (2)   A site/landscaping plan showing the following items:
         (a)   North arrow;
         (b)   The location and dimensions of all vehicular points of ingress
and egress; drives, alleys and streets;
         (c)   Property boundaries and lot line dimensions;
         (d)   The locations and dimensions of all existing and proposed
buildings, structures and improvements, including those that will be removed.
All information must be labeled;
         (e)   Setbacks from all property boundaries for existing and proposed
structures and buildings;
         (f)   Centerline and names of major and minor arterial streets
relevant to the application;
         (g)   Elevation drawing of proposed wireless communication facility,
including the antenna support structure, antenna platforms and associated
equipment enclosures. Also indicate the maximum number of antenna platforms
that can be supported;
         (h)   Detailed landscaping plan of the site;
         (i)   Location of artificial light sources and the areas of
illumination;
         (j)   Applications for tower farms shall include divisions (I)(2)(a)
through (I)(2)(i) above and an overall development plan showing the location of
future structures and equipment enclosures;
         (k)   Latitude, longitude and height of proposed antenna support
structures; and
         (l)   Other pertinent features as determined by the Zoning
Coordinator.
      (3)   Area map showing the property boundaries of adjacent property and
the location of existing buildings;
      (4)   Each applicant for one or more antenna support structures shall
provide to the Zoning Coordinator and Building Official a map showing the
locations and service areas of existing and approved antenna support structures
operated or utilized by the applicant, including specific information on the
location, height and design of each antenna support structure. The Public Works
Department shall maintain an inventory of existing and approved antenna support
structure, including specific information about the location, height and design
of each antenna support structures. The city may share such information with
other persons, organizations or governmental authorities;
      (5)   Documentation of minimum light requirements from the FAA or other
local, state or federal agency for the antenna support structure and/or
antennas. Where applicable, applicant will provide documentation of the FAA
airspace review and a copy of comments from the FAA;
      (6)   When the applicant is a wireless service provider, proof that the
applicant is licensed by the FCC to provide the wireless communication services
that the proposed facility is designed to support;
      (7)   Availability of suitable existing or approved antenna support
structures. No new antenna support structure shall be permitted unless the
applicant clearly demonstrates, in writing, to the reasonable satisfaction of
the Zoning Coordinator and Building Official that no existing or approved
antenna support structure within the required separation distance of the
proposed site can accommodate the applicant’s proposed antenna. Closer
separation distances may be approved if the applicant clearly demonstrates a
critical need for the alternative location and the infeasibility of locating or
collocating a wireless communication facility at or beyond the required
separation distance. Evidence submitted to demonstrate that no existing or
approved structure can accommodate the applicant’s proposed antenna must
include a discussion of the following items, if relevant:
         (a)   No existing or approved antenna support structures are located
within the geographic area required to meet the applicant’s engineering
requirements;
         (b)   Existing or approved antenna support structures are not of
sufficient height to meet the applicant’s engineering requirements;
         (c)   Existing or approved antenna support structures do not have
sufficient structural strength to support the applicant’s proposed antenna and
related equipment and cannot be reinforced to provide sufficient structural
strength;
         (d)   The applicant’s proposed antenna would cause electromagnetic
interference with the antenna on the existing or approved antenna support
structures, or the antenna on the existing or approved antenna support
structures would cause interference with the applicant’s proposed antenna;
         (e)   The fees or costs required to share an existing or approved
antenna support structure or to adapt an existing or approved antenna support
structure for sharing are unreasonable. Costs below new tower development are
presumed reasonable;
         (f)   Property owners or owners of existing or approved antenna
support structures are unwilling to accommodate the applicant’s needs; and
         (g)   The applicant demonstrates that there are other limiting factors
that render existing or approved antenna support structures unsuitable.
      (8)   If collocation is feasible, the owner of the antenna support
structure shall certify, prior to permit approval, that the owner will accept
for collocation any FCC licensed wireless communication provider using
compatible technology on commercially reasonable terms up to the antenna
support structure’s capacity to accommodate additional antennas. The applicant
shall also include a statement on how requests for collocators will be
processed; and
      (9)   The applicant must submit information that substantiates that there
will be no adverse effects on surrounding property values resulting from the
proposed facility.
   (J)   Nuisances. Wireless communication facilities, including, without
limitation, power source, ventilation and cooling, shall be operated at all
times within the city noise regulations, shall not be operated so as to cause
the generation of heat that adversely affects a building occupant and shall not
be maintained or operated in such a manner as to be a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 9-6-2) (Ord. 06-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
§ 153.03 APPEALS.
   Appeals from any decision of the Zoning Coordinator and Building Official
may be taken by any person aggrieved or any official of the city by the
decision of the Zoning Coordinator and Building Official. Such appeal shall be
to the city Board of Adjustment pursuant to Chapter 155.
(Prior Code, § 9-6-3) (Ord. 06-2002, passed 5-21-2002)
